### B266 ‚Äî Sheet sidebar labels from the title block (real sheet # + name, not "Sheet N") `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; delivered 2026-06-21 as a follow-up to #242)*
`[x]` **Shipped.** The single-sheet Markup sidebar now shows each sheet's real **sheet # + title** read
from its title block (e.g. "C-5 ‚Äî GRADING PLAN", "COVER SHEET"), not generic "Sheet N". Built on #242's
shared reader (`sheetMeta.readSheetMeta` ‚Äî which locates the title-block band first, so a "SEE SHEET X"
cross-ref or a detail/grid ref can't masquerade as the sheet number, the crux this item called out).
**No-auto-guess:** a sheet with no detected title block / no readable number falls back to "Sheet N"
(gated on `meta.titleBlock || meta.sheetNumber`, so a stray body-text line is never surfaced as the
label). OCR for scanned sheets stays the shared remaining slice (tracked under B267 + #242's dormant OCR
seam in `sheetRead.js`). 7/7 headless (`ui-audit/verify-markup-sheet-labels.mjs`, V90); #242's viewer
suite still 13/13.

### B343 ‚Äî Collapse the Markup single-sheet sidebar into logical sheets (parity with the Stitcher) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived 2026-06-21; minted **B343** ‚Äî next free after B342)*
`[x]` **Shipped (follow-up to #242).** #242 collapses a dropped set into logical sheets in the STITCHER
tray; this brings the same collapse to the single-sheet **Markup** sidebar: consecutive pages sharing a
plan type + a contiguous sheet-number run show as one expandable entry ("Grading Plan ¬∑ C-5‚ÄìC-7 ¬∑ 3
sheets"); cover/notes/one-offs stay standalone. Reuses #242's `sheetGroups.groupSheets` (the same engine
the Stitcher uses, so the two surfaces agree) + surfaces the per-sheet stated-scale auto-calibrate (¬∑‚âà)
via `sheetRead.statedCalibration`. The sidebar count reads "N sheets ¬∑ M pages" so the collapse is
visible. Verified: a 4-page set ‚Üí 2 logical entries, the group expands to its members (V90).
### B341 ‚Äî Stress-test the drawing stitch tool: harden the auto-stitch against bad PDF sets `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (task)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21: "stress test the stitch tool, look up how to break things and implement strategies to do so"; minted **B341** ‚Äî next free after B340)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/stitch-tool-stress-test-1tvw5b`).** Adversarial pass over the stitch core (`stitchGeom.js`, `autoStitch.js`, `sheetGroups.js`, `sheetMeta.js`) ‚Äî drove each engine with the inputs a messy real-world PDF set throws at it and fixed four ways it could **fail silently** (the worst kind here: a bad transform flings a sheet off-canvas, or ‚Äî worse ‚Äî butts two drawings together at the wrong size/place and the takeoff reads a confident wrong number). All four follow the owner rule **"a wrong stitch is worse than an un-stitched one"**: when a signal is unreliable the sheet is left **unplaced ‚Üí manual-Align safety net**, never auto-guessed.
- **Non-finite endpoints (NaN/Infinity) used to slip past the degenerate-baseline guard** ‚Äî `Math.hypot(NaN) < 1` is `NaN < 1` ‚Üí `false`, so a NaN coordinate (bad read / mis-built drawing area) reached `solveM`, produced a NaN matrix, and poisoned the sheet transform **and** the whole composite's bbox (every `Math.min/max` over it ‚Üí NaN). `alignBaselinesDegenerate` now rejects any non-finite point. (`stitchGeom.js`)
- **Contradictory match-line labels produced a wrong (overlapping/mirrored) stitch** ‚Äî if both sheets claimed the seam on their "right", `buildAdjacency` trusted it. It now treats the **geometric opposite** as the source of truth and **drops the edge** when a sheet's own label contradicts it (‚Üí manual Align). (`autoStitch.js`)
- **Mismatched page sizes were silently rescaled** ‚Äî a similarity fit from two endpoints will shrink/blow up a half-size detail page to make the seam meet. `autoPlaceGroup` now rejects a placement whose implied scale strays past **`MAX_STITCH_SCALE` (¬±25%)** and leaves the sheet for manual Align. (`autoStitch.js`)
- **Grouping chained across a major rollover** ‚Äî the packed `ordinal` (major¬∑100+minor) made `C-1.99 ‚Üí C-2.00` look consecutive (and could collide two codes onto one ordinal). `consecutiveCodes` now compares the parsed major/minor by numbering level, so a rollover starts a new logical sheet. (`sheetGroups.js`)
- **New `test/stitchStress.test.js` ‚Äî 29 adversarial tests** across 8 break-strategy groups (non-finite/degenerate coords, contradictory seams, size mismatch, cycles/duplicates/self-refs/missing targets, sheet-code edge cases, reader junk/empty/huge input, a **300-iteration randomized fuzz** asserting the partition + finiteness + scale-band invariants, and the measure-over-unaligned guard). Full suite green (**879 tests**, lint 0 errors, build clean). Pure-engine + DI hardening, so no live-browser verification needed; the manual-Align safety net and text-layer path are unchanged.

### B336 ‚Äî Sheet-metadata reader: title block, scale, match-line labels `[Doc Review]` (feature)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21; arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B336**)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/loving-newton-t7gzpq`).** The shared positional reader the whole batch consumes. New `extractPageItems` (pdf.js) keeps each text run's x/y; pure `src/shared/files/sheetMeta.js` finds the **title-block band** (text-density on the right/bottom edge), the **sheet title** (largest wordy line in the band, label/data rows skipped), the **stated scale** (reuses B267 `parseSheetScale`), and every **MATCH-LINE label** with its position + orientation (page-edge ‚Üí vertical/horizontal cut). Reuses B312's `titleBlockParse` for discipline/number/revision/date ‚Äî no second/parallel reader; surfaces a `confidence` instead of guessing. `doc-review/lib/sheetRead.js` glues pdf.js ‚Üí reader ‚Üí grouping with a **dormant injectable OCR seam** for scanned pages (‚Üí B340). **12 + 6 unit tests** (`test/sheetMeta.test.js`, `test/sheetRead.test.js`).
> **Dedup:** folded the CLAUDE.md roadmap "read its title block" (auto-filing) ‚Äî extends the shipped filing readers with the positional layer they lacked, doesn't duplicate them.

### B335 ‚Äî Drop a whole set ‚Üí auto-group pages into logical sheets (collapsed list) `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (feature)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B335**)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21.** Pure `src/shared/files/sheetGroups.js` collapses consecutive pages that share a plan type (discipline + `item`) AND a contiguous sheet-number run into logical sheets ("Grading Plan ¬∑ C-5‚ÄìC-7 ¬∑ 3 sheets"); cover/general-notes stay standalone; conservative (under-groups rather than mis-merges). The Stitcher tray now shows **logical sheets** (read+grouped in the background after a drop), with an **"all pages"** safety-net toggle and a "Reading sheets‚Ä¶" state. Clicking a grouped plan adds every page at once (auto-stitched, B337). **7 unit tests** (`test/sheetGroups.test.js`); headless V87 confirmed a 4-page set ‚Üí 2 logical entries.

### B337 ‚Äî Automatic match-line stitching `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (feature)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21; arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B337**)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21.** Pure `doc-review/lib/autoStitch.js` builds the seam graph from B336's match-line labels and places each sheet by feeding the shared seam's two endpoints into the **existing `solveM()`** similarity fit (`stitchGeom.js`, B300) ‚Äî BFS from the most-connected anchor, the whole group then slotted to the right of existing content. A label-less sheet stays **unplaced** and drops to the 2-point manual Align **pre-seeded** with its detected seam endpoints (half the clicks); manual Align remains the safety net. **5 unit tests** (`test/autoStitch.test.js`); headless V87 confirmed 3 sheets auto-stitch with **coincident seams** (Œîx ‚âà 0.78¬∑width, not the old +40 gap).
> **Dedup:** this WAS the roadmap's "automatic match-line detection later," now specified ‚Äî folded, built on `solveM`. The geometric edge-line middle-fallback (when labels are missing) is deferred ‚Üí B340.

### B338 ‚Äî Crop title blocks + single merged legend on stitched plans `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (feature)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21; arrived as "NEW-4"; minted **B338**)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21.** On a grouped composite each sheet is **clipped to its drawing area** (the B336 title-block band hidden) so the drawings butt cleanly, with a **"Crop blocks"** toggle. One **pinned "Composite key"** panel lists the group merged + the auto-set scale ‚Äî rendered as an overlay (not baked into the raster) so it stays readable at any zoom. Grouping/crop metadata now rides the saved stitch (additive, back-compatible) so a reload keeps the cropped composite + key. Headless V87 confirmed 3 clipPaths + the pinned key + the toggle. The graphical legend **symbol-union** is deferred ‚Üí B340.

### B339 ‚Äî Auto-calibrate from the sheet's stated scale `[Doc Review]` (feature)  *(owner chat 2026-06-21; arrived as "NEW-5"; minted **B339**)*
`[x]` **Shipped + verified 2026-06-21.** When a grouped plan is added, `groupCalibration` (`doc-review/lib/sheetRead.js`) reads the group's stated scale and sets the composite `ftPerUnit` automatically ‚Äî gated on a standard plot size (`detectSheet`) so a resized/half-size sheet can't mis-scale the set; manual Calibrate still overrides. Reuses `overlayScale.js` (`parseSheetScale`/`ftPerPointForScale`). Headless V87 confirmed the composite auto-calibrated from "1\"=40'" (takeoff "Calibrated", key "Scale set").
> **Dedup:** the SINGLE-SHEET half already shipped (B267 `autoDetectScales`); this added the stitcher/grouped-composite half. The graphic scale-bar fallback is deferred ‚Üí B340.

### B321 ‚Äî `deleteReview` orphans the Drive copy when the cloud record can't be read `[Doc Review / Files]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-21; minted **B321**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/bold-bohr-hohz2x`).** Deleting a review no longer leaves source bytes orphaned in Google Drive (or Supabase Storage) when the cloud record read misses.
- **Already shipped (B207 Drive wiring):** the brief's primary point ‚Äî "there is no Drive delete anywhere in the code" ‚Äî was already addressed: `deleteReview` removes every `sources[].driveKey` through `deleteFromDrive` (a `DELETE /api/files?key=‚Ä¶`) alongside the Supabase `BUCKET.remove(keys)`.
- **Residual fix (this session):** if `loadReview(id)` returns `null` (a transient network miss), `sources` was `[]`, so **neither** the Supabase objects **nor** the Drive objects were removed. `deleteReview` now falls back to the synchronous **local mirror** (`readDraft(uid, id)`, which carries the same `sources[]` incl. `storageKey` + `driveKey`) to recover the file list, so cleanup still runs. Best-effort and in parallel; it never blocks the row delete, and the legacy `<uid>/<id>/` folder sweep is unchanged.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 788 tests ¬∑ build green** (8 new in `test/docPersistence.test.js`); doc-review lazy chunk intact. The storage path is auth-gated (cloud + Drive), so the unit tests assert the graceful-degrade contract; a signed-in delete-with-Drive is the live check (logged in VERIFICATION).
> **Dedup:** primary already done under B207; this is the loadReview-null residual. Distinct from B38(a) (upsert re-file orphaning).

### B322 ‚Äî "Open PDF‚Ä¶" and every Stitcher sheet upload to Supabase only, never Drive `[Doc Review / Stitch + Files]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-2" 2026-06-21; minted **B322**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/bold-bohr-hohz2x`).** Interactively-opened single sheets and **all** stitched sheets now go through the **same Drive-first / Supabase-fallback path** as filing, instead of Supabase-only.
- **One shared storage policy:** added `reviewStore.storeSource(srcId, blob, { projectId, discipline, fileName })` ‚Äî push to Google Drive (the primary home); only if Drive doesn't take it, fall back to Supabase Storage. `fileNewReview` was refactored to call it too, so there's a single source of truth for "where a source's bytes live" (no more two slightly-different copies of the policy).
- **Call sites:** `DocReview.openFile` and `Stitcher.openFiles` now call `storeSource` (were `uploadSource` ‚Üí Supabase only) and persist `driveKey`; both `buildSnapshot`s carry `driveKey`; `Stitcher.loadStitch` reads back Drive-first then Supabase (`DocReview.fetchSourceBytes` already did). 
- **Why it matters:** (a) these files now live in Drive like filed ones (the "Drive is the primary file home" direction); (b) they **bypass Supabase's 50 MB per-file cap on the happy path** ‚Äî an E-size sheet or a large multi-sheet set that used to silently flag `oversize` ("re-drop on load") now stores in Drive; (c) stitched sheets carry a `driveKey`, so a stitched set can read its sheets back from Drive.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 788 tests ¬∑ build green** (`storeSource` degrade-path test); doc-review lazy chunk intact. The full Drive round-trip needs the (not-yet-deployed) Drive backend + sign-in, so it's the live check; the fallback to Supabase keeps today's behaviour until Drive is on.
> **Dedup:** net-new; the viewer (B288‚ÄìB296) and stitch-guard (B300‚ÄìB302) batches never touched the storage backend choice. Pairs with B321 (Drive delete) and B323 (keyless-source window).

### B323 ‚Äî A source saved with a null key during the upload window becomes unfetchable on a quick reload `[Doc Review]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-3" 2026-06-21; minted **B323**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/bold-bohr-hohz2x`).** A file opened and then reloaded **before its upload resolved** no longer strands the backdrop with a pointer the loader can't fetch.
- **Cause:** `openFile`/`openFiles` set the source into state immediately with `storageKey:null` (and no `driveKey`), which made it an autosave dep; the debounce + the synchronous local mirror could capture that **keyless** source before the upload's `.then(setSource w/ key)` ran. A reload in that window saved a record pointing at a source with no key ‚Üí `fetchSourceBytes` couldn't fetch it ‚Üí a permanent "re-open it to view", even though the bytes may have landed.
- **Fix:** `buildSnapshot` now persists a source only when it's actually stored ‚Äî `isStoredSource(s) = !!(s.storageKey || s.driveKey || s.oversize)`. While a just-opened/added file is still uploading (keyless), it's **omitted** from the saved `sources`, so a mid-upload reload can't save a broken pointer; the markups still save, and once the upload resolves the source is persisted normally (its key change re-triggers autosave). Applied to both the single-sheet and the per-sheet Stitcher snapshots. (`oversize` still counts as "stored" ‚Üí the existing graceful "re-drop on load" path is unchanged.)
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 788 tests ¬∑ build green** (`isStoredSource` unit tests: keyed/drive/oversize ‚áí persistable; keyless/absent ‚áí not); doc-review lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** net-new; shares the `isStoredSource` predicate with B322's snapshots. Backdrop-only loss (markups were always safe).

### B324 ‚Äî A genuine edit made within the post-open suspend window isn't flagged dirty ‚Üí never reaches the cloud `[Doc Review]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-4" 2026-06-21; minted **B324**)*
`[x]` **Fixed + verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/bold-bohr-hohz2x`).** An edit made right after opening/resuming a review (inside the ~1.5 s programmatic-load window) is now mirrored, flagged dirty, and reaches the cloud.
- **Cause:** the autosave effect early-returned for the whole suspend window (B19), skipping **both** the local mirror **and** `dirtyRef=true`. The unmount/hide flush gates its cloud upsert on `dirtyRef`, so an edit in that window never reached the cloud (lost cross-device, or entirely on a tab crash before flush). The window is armed at load-start, so it usually elapsed harmlessly during a large PDF's fetch ‚Äî it bit on small/cached PDFs.
- **Fix:** the per-tick decision is now a pure, unit-tested `lib/autosavePlan.js ‚Üí planAutosave({enabled, empty, loadEcho, suspended})`. The programmatic-load **echo** is identified precisely by a `loadEchoRef` flag (armed by `suspendSave`, consumed on the echo tick) rather than by the blunt time window, so it's still skipped ‚Äî but a **genuine edit**, even inside the window, now **mirrors + flags dirty** (so it's recoverable on-device AND flushes to the cloud); only its **debounced cloud re-save** stays suppressed while suspended, preserving B19's "don't re-stamp the just-loaded snapshot" intent (and B44's "no re-upsert of unchanged data on a mode toggle").
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 788 tests ¬∑ build green** (`planAutosave` unit tests cover: load echo ‚áí consume only; edit-in-window ‚áí mirror+dirty, no debounce-save; edit-out-of-window ‚áí mirror+dirty+save; blank/disabled ‚áí nothing).
> **Dedup:** net-new; interacts with B19 (suspendSave) + B44 (dirty-gated flush), both preserved. Not covered by any open item.

### B325 ‚Äî Stitcher pan crash: "Cannot read properties of null (reading 'panX')" when a pan is interrupted `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-21: "its broken, i was on the stitcher and it broke"; minted **B325** ‚Äî a hot `main` had reached B324)*
`[x]` **Fixed + shipped 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/awesome-feynman-i7wypf`).** The pan handler's `setView` updater read `drag.current` **inside** the deferred updater. That updater runs in React's render phase, which for a continuous `pointermove` can be deferred a tick; a discrete event in between ‚Äî `pointerup`, `pointercancel`, or the **B270** blur/visibility gesture-abort ‚Äî nulls `drag.current` first. Reading the ref then dereferenced null and threw in the render phase ‚Üí the Document Review **error boundary** caught it ("hit an error and couldn't load") and the whole stitcher went down. A real user hits this by tab-switching / losing focus / a pointer-cancel mid-pan. **Fix:** capture the drag origin into a local and close over it via a pure `panTo()` helper in `lib/stitchGeom.js`, so an aborted gesture can't crash the deferred updater. **Verified:** 4 unit tests (`test/stitchGeom.test.js` ‚Äî math, null-ref-survival, + a teeth test that the OLD ref-reading pattern throws `/panX/`) and a headless harness (`ui-audit/verify-b325-pan.mjs`: a normal pan moves the world; 12 mid-pan aborts ‚Üí no error boundary, 0 `panX` errors; pan still works after). lint 0 ¬∑ build green. VERIFICATION **V84**.

### B341 ‚Äî Contrast regression from the scheme change; full-app audit `[Site / shared / theming]` (bug)  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-21 "Backlog mode"; arrived as "NEW-1"; first filed B321, renumbered **B341** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B321‚ÄìB340)*
`[x]` **Fixed + audited + verified this session (branch `claude/dreamy-fermi-qqyt9j`).** After the
B316‚ÄìB320 scheme change, several chrome elements rendered too light to read. **Root cause:** B318 flipped
the chrome from always-dark to **themes-with-the-app** (light theme ‚Üí light chrome), and migrated
`index.css` + `AppHeader` + `palette.js` + the per-file `PAL` *objects* to tokens ‚Äî but a set of
**chrome-region components kept inline hardcoded old-dark-chrome hexes** (`#ece7db` cream text,
`#fff` active text, `#9b9482`/`#8a8473` warm grays, `#2e2a23` borders, `rgba(255,255,255,0.0x)` fills,
a hardcoded-dark status-bar bg, and pale dark-chrome badge colors `#86efac`/`#fbbf24`). On the new
**light** chrome those became cream/white-on-white; one (the planner status bar) was dark-text-on-a-
still-hardcoded-dark-bg. The two reported cases ‚Äî the **user-name pill** and the **Dashboard/Map
toggle** ‚Äî were exactly this class, so the fix audited the **whole tree**, not just the three reported spots.
- **Audit method (as briefed):** diffed the scheme commit (`32a1b8a`) to see which tokens changed,
  then grepped every consumer of the retired hexes; built a **programmatic WCAG checker over every
  defined token pair** in both themes (`ui-audit/contrast-audit.mjs`, parses the real `index.css`) +
  a **live headless probe** that reads the computed text/bg of the actual chrome elements
  (`ui-audit/verify-b341-contrast.mjs`).
- **Token system itself was sound** ‚Äî every actionable pair clears AA in both themes; the only WARNs
  are documented exceptions (locked Site/Schedule brand fills, only ever used as ‚â•3:1 underline +
  unused `--on-accent-*` text tokens; the amber Markup underline whose state is also carried by its
  passing text; owner-exempt subtle borders). So the regression was purely the unmigrated components.
- **Fixes (repointed to tokens):** `Shell.jsx` (account pill + dropdown), `ProjectBreadcrumb.jsx`
  (crumbs + dropdown; **AppHeader now passes the `-text` accent token**, never the fill, for the
  "current"/"New project" labels ‚Äî fill-as-text was 3.4:1), `SitePlanner.jsx` (status bar bg, Files
  button, left-rail + tool-rail + snap/parcel active text, hdrTab chips, save-slot warn color),
  `DocReview.jsx` (header title + Files + chrome buttons), `Stitcher.jsx` (toolbar dividers/buttons),
  `ReviewsBar.jsx` (badge colors + dropdown), `LayerPanel.jsx` (warm grays ‚Üí tokens; it rides the
  themed surface-overlay so it was dark-on-dark in dark mode), and the reusable `Field` label.
- **Two new tokens** (both themes, AA-checked): **`--on-accent`** (text ON the global accent fill ‚Äî
  white in light, near-black in dark because the B319 dark accent `#F26B3A` is too light for white at
  only 3.0:1) and **`--warn-text`** (legible amber for saving/unsaved/offline badges, replacing the
  dark-chrome `#fbbf24`).
- **Before ‚Üí after (reported + key siblings), contrast on the light chrome:**

  | Element | before | after (light / dark) |
  |---|---|---|
  | User-name / Sign-in pill text | `#ece7db` on `#FFF` ‚âà **1.2:1** | **16.66 / 15.11** |
  | Dashboard¬∑Map crumb (active) | `#fff` on `#FFF` = **1.0:1** | **16.66 / 15.11** |
  | Dashboard¬∑Map crumb (idle) | `#9b9482` ‚âà **3.0:1** | **11.2 / 10.4** |

- **Deliverables:** `ui-audit/contrast-audit.mjs` (token-pair report, exits non-zero on any actionable
  fail) + **`test/contrast.test.js`** (3 tests ‚Äî both themes pass their floor; the WARN set stays
  locked) so a future palette edit that drops a pair below AA fails CI instead of the eye. Module

### B316 ‚Äî Light / dark / system theme with cool-gray light palette `[AppHeader / theming]` (feature) ‚Äî foundation-scale  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-20; arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B316** ‚Äî next free after B272)*
`[x]` Add a theme selector with three modes ‚Äî **Light**, **Dark**, **System** (`prefers-color-scheme`). App is currently hard-locked to one look; this adds the switch. **Both modes are net-new full surface palettes** (owner decision 2026-06-20, see below): Light = cool gray-white surfaces; Dark = a genuine dark-*surface* mode (dark content panels), **retiring** today's warm cream/paper work area.
> **‚úì DECISION (owner, 2026-06-20) ‚Äî "build a true dark mode":** the app today is **not all-dark** ‚Äî content surfaces are a warm **cream/paper** ("drafting") palette (`body #efeadf`, panels `#f6f3ec`, ink `#26231e`) under **dark graphite chrome** (top bars + rail, `#14110e`/`#191613`). Asked whether "keep the existing dark unchanged" meant preserve today's cream-content + dark-chrome look, or build a real dark-*surface* mode, the owner chose the latter: build a **genuine dark-surface** Dark mode (dark content panels) and **retire the cream**, alongside the cool-gray Light. **Consequence for scope:** *both* themes are net-new surface palettes ‚Äî the only "existing dark" that survives is the dark **chrome** (bars/rail); the dark **content-surface** values (dark equivalents of surface-page / surface-raised / borders / text) **don't exist yet and must be designed**, and every one of the ~886 color spots needs a proper two-way (light‚Üîdark) mapping, not a one-way "add light." This increases effort vs. preserving the current look and reinforces the multi-pass-foundation plan below.

> **üîÅ UPDATE 2026-06-21 ‚Äî design RESOLVED + decomposed into B317‚ÄìB320 (building this session).** The owner ran the theming design through a ChatGPT visual pass; the returned spec settles every open question here. Implemented as four sibling children of this umbrella: **B317** (infrastructure), **B318** (full palette + theme-aware chrome), **B319** (work-surface canvas/sheet), **B320** (contrast + status). B316 stays as the umbrella/record. **Canonical visual reference: `planyr-theming-mockup.html`** ‚Äî match its *rendered* result, not just raw hexes. ‚öÝ Owner named that file as the reference but it is **not in the repo** as of this update ‚Äî request a copy to keep in-repo + diff against. **Two assumptions in THIS item are now reversed/resolved:** (1) ~~"the dark chrome survives unchanged in both themes"~~ ‚Üí **chrome now themes WITH the app** (light theme = light chrome, dark theme = dark chrome); a permanently-dark bar in an otherwise-white app forces constant pupil readjustment ‚Äî worst case for eye strain (see B318). (2) the net-new dark surface palette **and** the two-value accent-text question are now **fully specified** in B318. Retire the warm cream, the old always-dark warm chrome (`#14110e`/`#191613`), and the ember accent (`#e8590c`).

**Mechanics (from the owner's spec):**
- Drive theming off `data-theme="light|dark"` on `<html>`. All colors as CSS variables, both themes fully defined.
- **System** resolves via `prefers-color-scheme` and must update **live mid-session** ‚Äî attach a `matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)')` change listener.
- Persist the choice (light/dark/system) in **localStorage as source-of-truth on load**; mirror to the `profiles` row (NEW-1) for cross-device. localStorage wins on first paint to avoid a network round-trip.
- **FOUC gotcha (do this FIRST):** an inline script in `index.html <head>` that reads the stored choice (or system pref) and sets `data-theme` **before React mounts** ‚Äî otherwise every load flashes the wrong theme. ("FOUC" = flash of un-themed content.)
- Theme control lives in the **account dropdown (NEW-2)** or **Settings** ‚Äî consolidate, don't duplicate.
- Files likely touched: `index.html` (inline pre-paint script), a `ThemeProvider`/context, the token stylesheet (`src/index.css`), the account dropdown (NEW-2), the `profiles` mirror via the NEW-1 hook.

**Light-mode surface tokens (cool gray-white ‚Äî owner-verified legible):**

| Token | Light value | Dark value |
|---|---|---|
| surface-page | `#F3F5F8` | existing locked dark |
| surface-raised (cards) | `#FFFFFF` | existing locked dark |
| border-default | `#E1E5EB` | existing |
| border-strong (hover) | `#CDD3DC` | existing |
| text-primary | `#1B1E26` | existing |
| text-secondary (muted) | `#565E6E` | existing |
| text-tertiary (hints) | `#8B92A1` | existing |

> ‚öÝ **Per the decision above, "Dark value = existing" for the *surface* rows is now a net-new true-dark surface palette to be designed** (dark page / dark cards / dark borders / light-on-dark text), NOT the current cream. Only the dark **chrome** (bars/rail) pre-exists. The owner's Light column is fixed; the Dark surface column needs its cool-neutral dark equivalents specced as part of the build.

**Accent pair model:** each module accent is **two tokens** ‚Äî a **fill/brand** value (unchanged, locked hexes ‚Äî these already live in `src/shared/ui/moduleAccent.js` as `MODULE_ACCENT`) and an **on-light text** value (tuned, AA-passing as foreground). The `-text` token is theme-dependent.

| Module | fill (both modes) | text ‚Äî light mode | text ‚Äî dark mode |
|---|---|---|---|
| Site | `#1D9E75` | `#0F6E56` | `#5DCAA5` |
| Schedule | `#7F77DD` | `#534AB7` | `#AFA9EC` |
| Markup | `#EF9F27` | `#8A5410` | `#EF9F27` |

- **On-fill text rule (both modes):** text/icons **on** an accent fill ‚Äî Site & Schedule fills carry **white** (`#FFFFFF`); **Markup (amber) fill carries dark text** (`#412402`). White-on-amber is unreadable; enforce wherever a status/tab chip uses the amber fill.
- **Usage rule:** accent-as-**fill** (tab band, active indicator, status-chip bg) ‚Üí **fill** token. Accent-as-**foreground** (colored text, thin icons, links) ‚Üí **`-text`** token, never the fill token.
- **Edge case ‚Äî status palette:** the locked status tokens (Pursuit / Active / On Hold / Complete / Dead) need the same discipline. For each status color used as text/icon on a light surface, **derive programmatically** the nearest variant that clears **AA ‚â• 4.5** as foreground on `#FFFFFF`/`#F3F5F8`; keep originals as fills with the same on-fill rule. **Flag any status color whose foreground variant can't reach 4.5** for review (don't hand-pick).
- **Constraint (unchanged):** module accents stay confined to the **top tab row only** ‚Äî light mode doesn't change that.

> **Build plan / scope (grounds the "foundation-scale" tag) ‚Äî REUSE, don't rebuild:**
> The app has **no central theming layer today**: ~**886 hardcoded hex literals across ~30 files**, **9 local `PAL` objects** (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `MapFinder.jsx`, `AuthPanel.jsx`, `ParcelDrawing.jsx`, `DocReview.jsx`, `Stitcher.jsx`, `ProjectLibrary.jsx`, `ProjectFilesDrawer.jsx`, `ReviewsBar.jsx`), inline styles throughout, plus literals inside `src/index.css`. `MODULE_ACCENT` (`moduleAccent.js`) is already the single source for the **fill** colors ‚Üí extend it with the `-text` counterparts rather than re-listing hexes. `BrandMark` already takes a `surface="dark|light"` prop (theme-aware) ‚Üí just feed it the active theme. The Scheduler is an **iframe** (`public/sequence/index.html`) with its **own** colors ‚Üí needs its own token sheet or a postMessage theme bridge (separate surface).
> Recommended sequence: **(1)** define the full token set for both themes in `:root` / `[data-theme]`; **(2)** FOUC inline script; **(3)** `ThemeProvider` + `matchMedia` live listener + localStorage persistence; **(4)** migrate the 9 PALs + inline literals + `index.css` literals to consume tokens (the bulk ‚Äî do it per-workspace, verifying each surface); **(5)** AA-derive the status palette; **(6)** theme the Scheduler iframe; **(7)** wire the control into NEW-2/Settings + the NEW-1 cross-device mirror. A shell-only/partial theme that leaves the canvas/map/doc-review hardcoded would be a **misleading half** (per the "finish the job" rule) ‚Äî so this ships as a deliberate multi-pass foundation, ideally after NEW-1 + NEW-2 land.

### B317 ‚Äî Light / Dark / System theme infrastructure `[Global / theming]` (feature) ‚Äî child of B316; build FIRST  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-21 via ChatGPT spec; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B317**)*
`[x]` Build the theming foundation every module inherits. **Ships together with B318‚ÄìB320; build B317 first (they depend on it).**
- **Token system:** CSS custom properties driven by `data-theme="light|dark"` on `<html>`. Components reference **tokens only**, never raw hex. **Extend** the existing locked token set (`:root` vars in `src/index.css` + the per-file `PAL` objects) rather than starting fresh ‚Äî repoint them at tokens.
- **Three modes:** Light, Dark, System. **System** follows the OS via `window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)')` and must **live-update** when the OS flips ‚Äî attach a `change` listener, don't read once at load.
- **Persistence:** store the choice in `localStorage['planyr.theme']`; **default System** on first run.
- **No theme flash (FOUC):** apply the resolved theme in a tiny inline `<head>` script **before first paint**, so the page never flashes the wrong colors before React boots.
- **Switch UI:** three-way control in Settings and/or the **row-1 settings menu in `AppHeader`**.
- Files: new `ThemeProvider`/context, the global token stylesheet (`src/index.css`), `AppHeader`, `index.html` (pre-paint script).
> Lineage: the **infrastructure half of B316**. Finalizes B316's FOUC/ThemeProvider/matchMedia/localStorage mechanics. localStorage is source-of-truth on load; the `profiles` cross-device mirror stays a later additive follow-on, not a prerequisite.

### B318 ‚Äî Full theme palette + theme-aware chrome `[Global / AppHeader]` (feature) ‚Äî depends on B317; child of B316  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-21 via ChatGPT spec; arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B318**)*
`[x]` Replace the retired warm-cream work surface **and** the old always-dark chrome. **Chrome now themes WITH the app** ‚Äî this deliberately **reverses** B316's "dark chrome in both themes" assumption: a dark bar in an otherwise-white app (bright office) forces constant pupil readjustment, the worst case for eye strain. **Light theme ‚Üí light chrome; Dark theme ‚Üí dark chrome.** Depends on B317.

**Surfaces:**

| Token | Light (fixed) | Dark (new) |
|---|---|---|
| surface-page | `#F3F5F8` | `#14161B` |

| text-primary | `#1B1E26` | `#E8EBF0` |
| text-secondary | `#353B49` | `#CAD0DA` |
| text-tertiary | `#4B5263` | `#A4ABB8` |

**Chrome (themes with app):**

| Role | Light | Dark |
|---|---|---|

| chrome-bg-elev | `#FFFFFF` | `#171A21` |

| chrome-muted | `#353B49` | `#A6ADBA` |
| chrome-tab-inactive | `#454C5C` | `#C2C8D2` |
| save-badge | `#0F6E56` | `#7FD8B8` |

- **Module fills (fixed, both themes):** Site `#1D9E75`, Schedule `#7F77DD`, Markup `#EF9F27`. **On-fill text:** white for Site/Schedule; **dark `#412402` for Markup** ‚Äî never white on amber.

NB `src/index.css :root` hardcodes `--chrome/--chrome-line/--chrome-ink/--chrome-muted/--accent` to warm/ember + a `rgba(232,89,12,‚Ä¶)` focus ring, and `Shell.jsx`/`AppHeader.jsx` hardcode `#14110e`/`#2e2a23`/`#c9c3b4` ‚Äî all move to per-theme tokens.

### B319 ‚Äî Work-surface theme behaviors: canvas + Markup sheet `[Site, Markup]` (feature) ‚Äî depends on B317/B318; child of B316  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-21 via ChatGPT spec; arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B319**)*
`[x]` The drafting canvas and the document viewer need their own dark behavior, distinct from panel surfaces. Depends on B317/B318.
- **Site canvas dark tokens:** `canvas-bg #0E1014`, `grid-minor rgba(232,235,240,0.05)`, `grid-major rgba(232,235,240,0.10)`; lift **parcel stroke to `#2FBE90`** on dark.
- **Drafting/selection accent dark variant:** the selected-element + dimension-line **red-orange is a work-surface color, NOT a module accent** ‚Äî the "accents don't change" rule doesn't apply: light `#C2410C` ‚Üí dark **`#F26B3A`** (`#C2410C` too dim on the dark canvas).
- **Markup in Dark:** the **mat** (around the drawing, `#cfc8ba` today at `DocReview.jsx:539` + `Stitcher.jsx:343`) darkens to **`#0E1014`**; the **drawing sheet stays white** ‚Äî it's the **immutable backdrop**, and inverting a construction sheet misrepresents it. Direct application of the standing immutable-backdrop principle, not a one-off.
- Files: Site Planner canvas renderer (`SitePlanner.jsx`); Markup viewer mat/sheet container (`DocReview.jsx`, `Stitcher.jsx`).

### B320 ‚Äî Contrast + text-hierarchy pass `[Global / theming]` (task) ‚Äî depends on B317/B318; child of B316  *(owner-dropped 2026-06-21 via ChatGPT spec; arrived as "NEW-4"; minted **B320**)*
`[x]` Apply the dark text ramp (B318) and lock the rule behind it. Depends on B317/B318.
- **Standing rule (also added to `CLAUDE.md`):** build text hierarchy through **weight, size, and uppercase letter-spacing ‚Äî never by fading text toward the background.** Low-contrast gray body/label text is an eye-strain problem in bright offices and is **disallowed**. Subtle grays stay correct **only** for borders, the drafting grid, and the semantic "Complete" status badge.
- **Status badges need dark-surface variants.** The canonical `STATUS_TOKENS` (`src/shared/ui/statusTokens.js`: pursuit `#378ADD`, active `#639922`, onhold `#BA7517`, complete `#888780`, dead `#E24B4A`) are tuned for white cards; saturated values go muddy on `#1D2027`. Add a lighter dark-mode variant per status (mockup direction: Active ‚Üí `#2FBE90`, Complete ‚Üí `#8B92A1`). NB a drifted duplicate `STATUS_COLOR` lives in `ProjectLibrary.jsx:13` ‚Äî reconcile while here.
- **Verify all body text clears WCAG AA (‚â• 4.5:1)** against its surface in **both** themes; flag any accent/status that fails and propose the fix rather than shipping it silent.

### B312 ‚Äî Auto-filing reads the title block with plain code first; AI only as a fallback `[Document Review / Files]` (feature) ‚Äî owner direction on B299  *(owner 2026-06-20: "a ton of this could be done without an LLM‚Ä¶ is this gonna cost tokens?"; minted **B312** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B300‚ÄìB311)*
`[x]` **Built + tested + shipped this session.** Re-architected auto-filing (B299) to **"plain code first, AI only as fallback"** so the common case is **free, instant, and needs no cloud or API key** ‚Äî exactly the owner's point that reading a title block, picking the latest date, and recognizing "ALTA survey" is ordinary code, not an LLM job.
- **Tier 1 ‚Äî deterministic, in the browser, $0 (the default now):** for any PDF with an embedded text layer (most CAD-exported vector drawings), read the text with the existing `extractPageText` (pdf.js, the same reader B267 uses) and parse the filing fields with pure code:
  - `src/shared/files/titleBlockParse.js` (pure, **17 unit tests**): `classifyDiscipline` (a keyword table ‚Äî **ALTA** ‚Üí Survey/ALTA Survey, boundary/topo ‚Üí Survey, grading/paving/drainage ‚Üí Civil, fire sprinkler, landscape, environmental, geotech‚Ä¶; sheet-number prefix as the tie-break), `findDates`/`latestDate` ("search all dates, pick the newest" = the issue date, across MM/DD/YYYY, YYYY-MM-DD, "June 30, 2025", "30 June 2025"), `parseSheetNumber` (labelled-first, conservative ‚Äî returns "" rather than grab a grid ref), `parseRevision`, `readTitleBlockText`.
  - `src/shared/files/matchProject.js` (pure, **8 unit tests**): `matchProjectInText` **searches the sheet text for each named project's identifiers** (name phrase, or exact parcel/account/job number) and reuses the B299 "never auto-guess" decision (confident single ‚Üí matched; none/ambiguous ‚Üí needs-filing tray). Mirrors `server/filing/matcher.js`'s thresholds.
  - `src/workspaces/doc-review/lib/localRead.js` glues them to pdf.js (lazy-imported) ‚Üí a decision in the SAME shape the server returns.
- **Tier 2 ‚Äî AI fallback, only when Tier 1 finds NO text** (a scanned/image-only sheet) **and** the backend is enabled. So tokens are spent only on the hard minority, not every file. `autofile` (`lib/autofiling.js`) is now local-first with an injectable `localRead`; `capturePlacementFacts` uses a new `forceServer` flag (placement is genuinely an AI/CV step).
- **On by default, safely:** the provider now exposes `autofileReady = true` (Tier 1 always works in the browser ‚Äî no key, no deploy), so the drawer auto-files dropped drawings out of the box. A **confident match auto-routes**; **anything else falls back to today's behavior** (the active project, or the holding tray) ‚Äî so the only behavior change is that confident matches now file themselves, and a wrong confident match is still re-filable from the row. `backendReady` stays gated on `VITE_AUTOFILE_ENABLED` (the honest "AI can also read scanned sheets / capture placement" signal).
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 743 tests (53 new: titleBlockParse 17 + matchProject 8 + autofiling tiering) ¬∑ build green; doc-review lazy-chunk split intact.** Headless on the built app (`ui-audit/verify-b299-autofiling.mjs`): the Files drawer opens, the new modules (parser, matcher, lazy-pdf localRead) evaluate in a real browser, **0 page/console errors**. **Real-sheet accuracy** (the keyword table + name match against the owner's actual KG B1 / Jacintoport drawings) is the live acceptance check ‚Äî logged as **VERIFICATION V79** (needs a signed-in drop of a real construction sheet; the deterministic logic itself is exhaustively unit-tested).
> **Dedup:** does NOT replace the B299 AI reader (`server/filing/`) ‚Äî it puts a free deterministic front-end on it and demotes it to a fallback. Reuses `extractPageText` (B267) for text, the B299 matcher logic/thresholds, the B299 file-facts index + drawer wiring. The AI path stays the answer for scanned sheets + placement-fact capture.

### B310 ‚Äî Accidental parcel selection while panning the planner canvas `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; first filed B300, renumbered **B310** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B300‚ÄìB309)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/blissful-mccarthy-dkozi0`).** With parcels rendered, grabbing the planner canvas to pan kept registering as a parcel select ‚Äî `startMoveParcel` (`SitePlanner.jsx`) fired `setSel` on pointer-**down** and `e.stopPropagation()` blocked the background pan, so a press anywhere on a lot selected it whether the gesture was a click or the start of a drag. Navigating across lots felt like constantly clicking into them.
- **Fix ‚Äî click-vs-drag discrimination on the parcel layer.** A press on a **locked** parcel (the default every county-pulled / drawn lot carries ‚Äî created `locked:true` in all six creation paths) now starts a **PAN** (`drag.current.mode:"pan"`) tagged with the parcel id + the press origin (`tapParcel`, `downX/downY/downT`), instead of selecting. On pointer-**up** (`onUp`) it counts as a deliberate **click ‚Üí select** only if travel ‚â§ `PARCEL_CLICK_SLOP_PX` (**5px**, measured in SCREEN px so it's zoom-independent) **and** the press was < `PARCEL_CLICK_MS` (**400ms**); any larger/longer movement panned and leaves the selection untouched. Uses Pointer Events + `setPointerCapture` (already the canvas's model) so the up fires even if the pointer left the polygon, and the gesture joins the existing `abortGesture` recovery (`capturePidRef`) so an interrupted parcel-pan can't strand the grab cursor (B271-class).
- **Preserved:** a deliberately **unlocked** parcel still grabs-to-move on press (you unlocked it to reshape/move it ‚Äî matches elements); the full-polygon hit area is unchanged (we gate on gesture *intent*, never shrink the target); Shift-click-to-merge and align-edge picking still work. Space / the Pan tool remain the always-on pan escape hatches.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 712 tests ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.** Headless on the built app (`ui-audit/verify-b310-b311.mjs`, logged-out, seeded one locked parcel): a deselected‚Üí**click selects** (stroke‚Üí#c2410c / width 3); a **drag of 95px pans and does NOT select** (stroke stays #5b6650 / width 2, the parcel's on-screen box shifted +95px), **0 page JS errors**. Logged as **VERIFICATION V78**.

### B311 ‚Äî "Select parcels" mode toggle (non-hijacking default) `[Site Planner]` (feature) ‚Äî layered on B310  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; first filed B301, renumbered **B311**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/blissful-mccarthy-dkozi0`).** A **Row-2 toolbar toggle** ("Select parcels", next to Snap, shown only when the plan has parcels) as a hard-off fallback for pure browse/measure workflows where zero accidental selection is wanted. **Non-hijacking default = ON:** click a lot to select it, dragging always pans (normal selection works out of the box thanks to B310, so the toggle isn't the primary gate). **OFF:** a press on a parcel is click-through ‚Äî `startMoveParcel` returns *without* `stopPropagation`, so the event falls through to the background pan exactly as if it landed on empty canvas; a click never selects. Turning it OFF also drops any current parcel selection so browse mode is clean.
- **Persistence:** stored as `settings.parcelSelect` (default `true` in `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`), so it rides the existing per-project Site Model `settings` save/restore path ‚Äî saved per project, restored on reopen. No new store, no localStorage key.
- **Verified ‚Äî same harness (`ui-audit/verify-b310-b311.mjs`):** default reads **ON** (`aria-pressed=true`); flipping it **OFF** ‚Üí a click no longer selects (parcel stays unselected); flipping it back **ON** ‚Üí a click selects again; **OFF persists across a full page reload** (per-project). lint 0 ¬∑ 712 tests ¬∑ build green. Logged as **VERIFICATION V78**.

### B315 ‚Äî Undo (Ctrl+Z) unreliable after moving a building `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as coworker-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-21; renumbered B310‚ÜíB313‚Üí**B315** as a very hot `main` twice consumed the number ‚Äî B310/B311 parcel click-vs-drag + B312 auto-filing, then B313/B314 multi-tab + optimistic-concurrency)*
`[x]` **Fixed + headless-verified 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/ecstatic-ritchie-ihzkym`).** Moving a building then pressing Ctrl+Z now reverts the **entire** move in one step, every time (was: sometimes nothing, sometimes a partial revert).
- **Root cause (confirmed by reading, NOT guessed ‚Äî the brief's hypothesis #2, the race):** the drag-move transaction boundary was already correct ‚Äî `startMove`/`startMoveParcel`/`startGroupMove` push history **once** at drag-start, nothing during the drag, nothing on pointer-up (so hypothesis #1, per-frame pushes, did **not** apply). The defect was that `stateRef` ‚Äî the single source both for the snapshot pushed onto the undo stack AND for the baseline `undo()` compares against (the B32 no-op dedup `histKey(stateRef.current)` check) ‚Äî was updated in a **passive `useEffect` (no deps)**. A ref written in a passive effect lags the committed render by a paint, so a quick undo‚Üîdrag sequence could snapshot/compare a **stale** state ‚Üí revert to the wrong frame (partial) or skip the frame in the dedup loop (does nothing). Timing-dependent ‚áí intermittent, matching the fuzzy repro.
- **Fix:** (1) `stateRef.current` is now assigned **during render** instead of in a passive effect, so `pushHistory`/`undo`/`redo` always read the TRUE current state ‚Äî the race window is gone. (2) Extracted the stack + dedup into a **pure, unit-tested** module `lib/history.js` (`createHistoryStack({ keyOf })` ‚Üí push/undo/redo/drop/canUndo/canRedo), matching the `stitchGeom.js` precedent; `undo`/`redo` take the live state **explicitly**, so the stale-ref class of bug can't recur. (3) **Interrupted-drag edge case** (brief's list): Esc / lost-focus / pointer-cancel **mid-move** now reverts to the pre-drag snapshot stashed on `drag.current` and drops the dangling frame (`cancelActiveMove` in `abortGesture`), so a cancelled drag leaves no half-recorded command.
- **Edge cases covered + verified:** one drag = one undo (full revert); redo restores; two moves = two undos (one each); multi-select/group move = one push = one undo (geometry-agnostic stack); independent transactions don't clobber each other (a move-undo doesn't touch an unrelated vertex edit); Esc-mid-drag cancels cleanly.
- **Verified:** lint 0 ¬∑ **full suite green** (11 new in `test/history.test.js`, incl. a deterministic repro of the stale-baseline failure mode) ¬∑ build green. Headless on the built app (`ui-audit/verify-b315.mjs`, chromium-1194, logged-out): drag a building 300px ‚Üí **one Ctrl+Z snaps it fully back, Œî=0.0px** (not partial); redo; two-moves-two-undos; Esc-mid-drag revert; **0 JS errors**.
> **Dedup:** net-new. **Related but distinct from B32 (done)** ‚Äî B32 stopped no-op edits from polluting the stack (the *dedup* the `while`-loop does); B315 is the *stale-baseline race* that made even a clean move-frame revert wrong/skipped. NOT a duplicate of any open item; no open item covered undo-after-move. Kept as ONE item (the brief said split only if the diagnosis turned out to be redo- or multi-select-specific ‚Äî it wasn't; the race affects all undo, redo + multi-select already work as separate transactions).

### B308 ‚Äî Server-side Mapillary token proxy so the street-level layer works for all users `[Site Planner / functions]` (feature)  *(coworker-chat "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; first filed B303 then renumbered **B308** ‚Äî concurrent `main` landed a Doc Review batch on B303‚ÄìB307, so both can't share the number)*
`[x]` **Built + shipped 2026-06-21 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** The "Poles & hydrants from street imagery" layer now works for **every visitor with no per-user token**, and the Mapillary access token never reaches the public bundle or any client request URL ‚Äî it lives only as an encrypted Cloudflare Pages Secret the owner set (`MAPILLARY_TOKEN`, Production). Resolves the audit's *token-in-bundle* + *token-in-URL* LOW findings; honours the KEY DECISION "Mapillary token is a secret."
- **Pages Function** `functions/api/mapillary/[[path]].js` reads the token from the runtime binding `context.env.MAPILLARY_TOKEN` (NOT `import.meta.env`/a `VITE_*` var) and forwards to the Graph API. **Guardrails** (pure helpers in `functions/api/mapillary/_proxy.js`, unit-tested): allow-list ONLY `map_features` + fields `id,object_value,geometry`; **Origin check** (same-origin / `*.planyr.io` / `*.planyr.pages.dev`, foreign Origin ‚Üí 403); bbox/limit validation; short edge-cache (`max-age=300`) to cut quota. **Dormant-graceful:** no token (e.g. a Preview deploy, which doesn't have the secret) ‚Üí 503 + empty `data`, the client shows "not available here", never a hard error.
- **Client:** new leaflet-free `lib/mapillaryClient.js` (`mapillaryRequestUrl`/`pickDetections`); `evidenceLayers.fetchMapillary` calls the same-origin `/api/mapillary/map_features` with **NO `access_token`** by default (a pasted token = an optional power-user override straight to Mapillary). Removed the no-token gate in `mapillaryLayer` + `syncOverlayLayers` and the `needsSetup` flag on the layer; the LayerPanel box is now "Works automatically ‚Äî (Advanced) use your own token". `.env.example` + README document the secret-lives-in-Cloudflare rule.
- **Verified:** lint 0 ¬∑ **722 tests** (10 new, `test/mapillaryProxy.test.js`: allow-list, Origin, limit-clamp, and the client default carrying no token) ¬∑ build green; **0 `MLY|` token literals + 0 `VITE_MAPILLARY_TOKEN` in `dist/`**. Headless on the built app (`gis-verify/mapillary-proxy-verify.mjs`): toggling the layer with no token ‚Üí it loads via **same-origin `/api/mapillary/map_features`**, **0 token leaks** in any request URL, **no** direct `graph.mapillary.com` call, graceful degrade in preview, **0 JS errors**.
- **‚è≥ LIVE confirm (the one piece the sandbox can't do ‚Äî a Pages Function needs the Cloudflare runtime):** on planyr.io Production after the next deploy, zoom ‚â• 16 over a covered area ‚Üí pole/hydrant dots render via `/api/mapillary/‚Ä¶`, token nowhere in page source/bundle/URLs. Logged in VERIFICATION. (The owner already set the secret, so this is just the deploy + a coworker eyeball.)
> **Dedup:** net-new; builds on B285/B286 (Mapillary rename + gating). The cleanup half (drop the dead `VITE_MAPILLARY_TOKEN` read) stays as **B309** `[~]`, held until this is confirmed live.

### B303 ‚Äî Undo / redo for Document Review markups + calibration `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B283, renumbered **B303** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B283‚ÄìB302; batch B303‚ÄìB307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: place/delete/move a markup or measurement, press Ctrl/‚åò-Z ‚Üí nothing happened; the workspace had no history at all, so a mis-edit was unrecoverable. **Fix:** **Ctrl/‚åò-Z undo, Ctrl/‚åò-Shift-Z + Ctrl-Y redo** in BOTH `DocReview.jsx` (single sheet) and `Stitcher.jsx` (stitched set), plus on-canvas **‚Ü∂ / ‚Ü∑** buttons (disabled when there's nothing to undo/redo).
- **Pattern reused, not reinvented:** mirrors the Site Planner's `pushHistory` ‚Äî `pastRef`/`futureRef` of editable-state snapshots taken **by reference** (DocReview `{markups, calByPage, calInfo}`; Stitcher `{measures, ftPerUnit}`), with a `histKey` signature so `undo` **skips frames identical to the current state** ‚Äî the **B32/B105 lesson** that a stray push can't make Ctrl-Z look like a no-op. `pushHistory()` fires only on a REAL mutation; the background stated-scale auto-scan (B267) deliberately does NOT push. History resets when the document context changes (open new PDF / load / new review).
- **Covers `main`'s viewer edits too:** a markup **move** (B293, committed on pointer-up) and a **text create/edit/delete** (B293 inline editor) each push one frame, so the new editing affordances are undoable as well as plain draws.
- **Poly-vertex placement:** mid-draw, Ctrl-Z (and Backspace/Delete) step back the **last placed vertex** of a polygon/area/count draft before falling through to full undo / delete-selection.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b303-b307.mjs`): draw a rect ‚Üí Ctrl-Z removes it ‚Üí Ctrl-Shift-Z and Ctrl-Y each restore it; undo disabled before any edit; same proven in the Stitcher.

### B304 ‚Äî Manual Calibrate validates input (no more silent mis-calibration) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B284, renumbered **B304**; batch B303‚ÄìB307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: Calibrate ‚Üí click two points ‚Üí at the length prompt type a non-decimal form (e.g. **"1/8"** or **"1:240"**) ‚Üí `parseFloat` returned **1** and the sheet calibrated to a wrong scale with NO warning, silently poisoning every downstream measurement; gibberish ("abc") silently did nothing. **Root cause:** `parseFloat(window.prompt(...))` stops at the first non-numeric char, and the invalid branch `return`ed with no feedback.
- **Fix:** replaced `window.prompt` with an **inline on-canvas entry box** (honoring the owner "no dialog boxes" rule, like `main`'s B293 text editor) backed by a new tested parser **`parseFeet`** (`lib/parseLength.js`). It validates the WHOLE string: accepts plain feet (`120`, `120.5`, `120'`), **feet-and-inches** (`38'-7 3/4"`), and explicit fractional feet (`12 1/2 ft`); **rejects** scale ratios (`1:240`), bare ambiguous fractions (`1/8`), non-numeric junk, and zero/negative ‚Äî each with a clear inline message. A bad entry keeps the box open to fix; a blank cancels. Applied in BOTH `DocReview.jsx` and `Stitcher.jsx`.
- **Dedup:** distinct from **B267/B268** (auto-calibrate / scale cross-check) ‚Äî the **manual-entry** path they don't cover. Clears the **calibration** half of the B155/B156 "no dialog boxes" note; `main`'s B293 already converted the **text** prompt, so only ParcelDrawing's calibrate prompt remains under B155.
- **Verified:** unit ‚Äî `test/parseLength.test.js` (7 cases incl. the exact "1/8" / "1:240" / "abc" bugs). Headless ‚Äî the inline box opens (no prompt), **rejects "1/8" and stays uncalibrated**, rejects "1:240" as a ratio, and **accepts "100" ‚Üí sheet calibrated** (single sheet + Stitcher).

### B305 ‚Äî Markup toolbar overcrowds; header buttons wrap into uneven multi-line labels `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B285, renumbered **B305**; batch B303‚ÄìB307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro (confirmed live at 1568px wide): the header's "Open another‚Ä¶", "Stitch sheets ‚ñ∏", "Library" buttons wrapped their labels onto 2‚Äì3 lines at uneven heights; the single toolbar row was too crowded and worsened as the window narrowed. **Fix (the B117/B118 density treatment):** every toolbar button now carries **`white-space: nowrap`** (labels never break mid-word) + tightened padding; the three file-action buttons are condensed (`Open‚Ä¶`, `Stitch ‚ñ∏`, `üìÅ Library`) with full-text `title`s; sections are grouped with thin dividers (file ¬∑ tools ¬∑ undo/redo ¬∑ zoom). `DocReview.jsx` + `Stitcher.jsx`.
- **Verified headless:** the Open / Stitch / Library buttons compute `white-space:nowrap` and render as a **single 25px line** (‚â§34px) at 1440px ‚Äî no wrapping. Screenshot `screens/b303-b307.png`.

### B306 ‚Äî Sheet paging: Prev/Next buttons + keyboard `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B286, renumbered **B306**; batch B303‚ÄìB307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: on a 32-sheet set the only way to change sheets was clicking each entry in the left list ‚Äî no Prev/Next, and arrow / PageUp / PageDown didn't flip sheets. **Fix** (`DocReview.jsx`): a **‚Äπ N / total ‚Ä∫** pager above the sheet list, plus **‚Üê / ‚Üí and PageUp/PageDown** keyboard paging (gated so they don't fire mid-draw or mid-calibrate-entry), and the sheet list **auto-scrolls to keep the current sheet in view** (`scrollIntoView`). A shared `goToPage` keeps the current zoom (matching `main`'s viewer behaviour) and drops any in-progress draft/selection.
- **Verified headless:** Next advances 1/4‚Üí2/4; ‚Üí / ‚Üê page 2/4‚Üí3/4‚Üí2/4; the indicator + active-sheet highlight track.

### B307 ‚Äî Measurement labels sit at the path midpoint / true centroid `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5" 2026-06-20 owner chat; provisionally B287, renumbered **B307**; batch B303‚ÄìB307)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/stoic-faraday-th9mp8`).** Repro: a Distance label rendered on the first endpoint (`pts[Math.floor((len-1)/2)]` resolves to `pts[0]` for a 2-point line); an Area label sat at the vertex average, which can fall outside a concave (L-shaped) region. **Fix** (new pure helpers in `lib/takeoff.js`): **`midOfPath(pts, closed)`** anchors distance/perimeter labels at the true **arc-length midpoint**; **`centroidOf(pts)`** anchors area labels at the **area-weighted centroid**, and when that lands outside a concave shape it drops to the midpoint of the widest interior scanline span so the label stays **inside**. Wired into `DocReview.jsx` (distance/perimeter/area) and `Stitcher.jsx` (area). Coexists with `main`'s B296 (the label's 1-dp numeric format) ‚Äî B307 is the label's POSITION.
- **Verified:** unit ‚Äî `test/takeoff.test.js` (midpoint of a 2-pt line + an L; closed wrap-around; square centroid; concave-L centroid proven interior by ray-cast). Headless ‚Äî a horizontal distance label renders at **x‚âà454** (midpoint ‚âà450), not ‚âà250 (pts[0]).
### B300 ‚Äî Stitcher alignment has no degenerate-baseline guard; coincident clicks fling the sheet with a garbage transform `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B288 then renumbered **B300** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B288‚ÄìB299; batch B300‚ÄìB302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro (numerically verified): in Stitch, aligning a sheet means clicking two matching points; if the two clicks on the moving sheet (or the two reference points) land on ~the same spot, `solveM`'s `lb = Math.hypot(vb) || 1` **masked the zero baseline** and returned an extreme similarity transform (e.g. `solveM(b1==b2, A1, A2 100 apart)` ‚Üí √ó100 scale, e/f ‚âà ‚àí500), throwing the sheet far off-canvas at huge scale ‚Äî silently, and Stitch has no undo. **Fix:** extracted the pure stitch geometry (`fwd`/`inv`/`solveM`/`sheetBBox`) out of `Stitcher.jsx` into a unit-testable **`lib/stitchGeom.js`**, and added **`alignBaselinesDegenerate(b1,b2,A1,A2)`** + `MIN_ALIGN_BASE`, which rejects an alignment whose moving-sheet baseline `|b2‚àíb1|` **OR** reference baseline `|A2‚àíA1|` is below a small threshold (mirrors DocReview's Calibrate "line too short" guard). The align commit checks it **before** `solveM`: on a degenerate baseline it shows the banner ("Those two points are too close together ‚Äî pick two points farther apart‚Ä¶") and restarts the alignment at step 0, leaving the sheet **untouched**; only a healthy baseline applies the transform (and now also stamps the sheet `aligned:true`, see B301).
- **Verified:** 8 unit tests (`test/stitchGeom.test.js`, incl. the runaway-scale case the guard blocks + `solveM` scale/rotation recovery + `fwd`/`inv` round-trip) and **headless on the built app** (`ui-audit/verify-b300-b302.mjs`, chromium-1228): a degenerate Align shows the banner and the sheet's `<g transform>` is **unchanged** (not flung); a real Align still succeeds. lint 0 ¬∑ build green; DocReview lazy chunk still splits (stitchGeom rides inside it).
> **Dedup (batch B300‚ÄìB302):** net-new ‚Äî no existing item covers the stitch alignment math. NOT main's single-sheet-viewer **B288‚ÄìB296** (zoom/pan/markup-edit) nor its auto-filing **B299** (server-side title-block read), all different surfaces; distinct from **B181/B182/B183** (the *map* placement cascade) and **B130/B131** (parking). Shares `lib/stitchGeom.js` with B301.

### B301 ‚Äî Measuring over a not-yet-aligned sheet silently uses the composite scale ‚Üí wrong quantities `[Doc Review / Stitch]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B289 then renumbered **B301**; batch B300‚ÄìB302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro: add a second sheet (it drops at identity scale, offset to the right) and draw a Distance/Area over it **before** pressing Align ‚Äî the measurement applied the single composite calibration (ft per world unit, defined by sheet 1), so if that sheet's real scale differed the reading was **silently wrong** (and even at a shared scale its position/rotation could be off). **Fix:** each placed sheet now carries an **`aligned`** flag ‚Äî the first sheet *is* the world frame (auto-aligned `true`); every later sheet starts `false` and flips to `true` only when its Align completes (B300's commit path). Unaligned sheets are **flagged visually** ‚Äî an amber dashed "‚öÝ Not aligned ‚Äî click Align" overlay on the canvas, plus a "‚öÝ Not aligned ‚Äî measurements may be off" chip + amber-emphasized Align button in the Placed-sheets list. Committing a Distance/Area whose points fall over an unaligned sheet (**`measureOverUnaligned`** / `sheetContains` in `lib/stitchGeom.js`) raises a **warning banner** ("Heads up: that measurement is over a sheet that isn't aligned yet ‚Äî Align it first‚Ä¶"). **Warn, not block** (the app's "surface it loudly, let the user decide" principle). The flag is persisted in the stitch snapshot and restored on load ‚Äî older saves default their non-base sheets to aligned, so nothing already-saved is falsely flagged.
- **Verified:** unit tests for `sheetContains` + `measureOverUnaligned` (warns only over an `aligned:false` sheet; never over the base or with no sheets) and **headless**: a fresh 2nd sheet shows the canvas overlay + the panel chip, a measurement over it shows the warning, and a successful Align clears both. lint 0 ¬∑ build green.
- **‚Üë Superseded by B316 (2026-06-21, owner call "don't let it measure on uncalibrated things"):** the **warn** became a **hard block** ‚Äî a Distance/Area point over an un-aligned sheet is now refused at click time (`blockedOverUnaligned`, nothing commits), and the chip reads "Not aligned ‚Äî Align before measuring." `measureOverUnaligned`/`aligned`-state unchanged. See B316 / V83.

### B302 ‚Äî Degenerate 2-point Area (0 sf) and 2-point Perimeter (single segment) are committable `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20 owner chat; first filed B290 then renumbered **B302**; batch B300‚ÄìB302)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/admiring-hypatia-xjv8a1`).** Repro (numerically verified): `finishDraft` committed Area/Perimeter at ‚â•2 points, but a real polygon needs ‚â•3 ‚Äî a 2-point Area saved as **0 sf** (shoelace) and a 2-point Perimeter drew closed yet measured only the single segment (10 ft for a 10-unit span at 1 ft/u, not the 20 ft a closed loop implies), leaving meaningless zero/half entries in the takeoff list. **Fix:** added **`MIN_MEASURE_PTS` + `canCommitMeasure(kind,n)`** to `lib/takeoff.js` (area/perimeter ‚â•3, distance 2, count 1 ‚Äî matching what `polyArea`/`pathLength` actually need) and gated **both** finish paths on it ‚Äî Enter/`finishDraft` and (after merging main's B291 phantom-point fix) double-click/`onDbl` ‚Äî so a 2-point Area/Perimeter is a no-op (the draft is cleared) whichever way you finish, consistent with the existing count min-point guard. Other kinds (distance/rect/cloud/calibrate) are unaffected.
- **Verified:** unit tests for `canCommitMeasure` (the ‚â•3 / 2 / 1 contract) + the degenerate-geometry rationale (2-pt area = 0; a 2-pt "closed" path = one 10-unit segment, not 20; a real 3-pt loop closes 3+4+5=12) and **headless**: a 2-point Area finished by Enter or double-click commits nothing and the takeoff stays "No measurements yet", while a 3-point Area commits one polygon. lint 0 ¬∑ build green.
> **Dedup:** minor severity (clutter, not corrupted totals ‚Äî a 0-sf area contributes 0 to the rollup), filed with B300/B301 but a separate surface (`takeoff.js` / single-sheet Markup). Complements main's **B291** (which stripped the double-click's phantom points) by also enforcing the ‚â•3 minimum on that finish path.

### B299 ‚Äî Auto-filing: drop a drawing ‚Üí it reads the title block ‚Üí matches a project ‚Üí files itself `[Document Review / Server + Files]` (feature)  *(owner HANDOFF 2026-06-20; first built as B270, renumbered through a very hot `main` that consumed B270‚ÄìB298 ‚Äî incl. a different **B270** (Project Files drop-zone queue) and a different **B297** (account profiles) ‚Äî so it landed at the real next free ID **B299** at merge time)*
`[x]` **Built + wired + tested this session (branch `claude/sleepy-archimedes-gts4wa`).** The auto-filing **backend tranche**: drop a PDF ‚Üí a server-side title-block read ‚Üí match to one of the named projects ‚Üí auto-route + auto-name, with a "needs filing" tray for anything it can't confidently match. Server-side because the read uses an **API key that must never reach the browser** (KEY DECISIONS) ‚Äî it lives in the `/server` compute layer (Cloud Run), distinct from Supabase. Status mirrors the convert (B238) / Drive (B207) backends: **code complete, fully unit-tested, wired through the UI, gated dormant** until the owner provisions Cloud Run + `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `DOC_FILING_URL`.
- **Title-block reader** `server/filing/titleBlockReader.js` ‚Äî mirrors the client `titleReader.js` request shape (model `claude-opus-4-8`, adaptive thinking, a `json_schema` output, the PDF as a base64 `document` block) but runs **server-side** and calls the Messages API over **raw `fetch` with an injectable `fetchImpl`** (like `server/convert/aps.js`), so the Cloud Run image stays dependency-free and the read is unit-testable without a key. **One read, two payoffs:** the same pass captures the FILING fields (project / number / address / parcel / discipline / sheet # / title / revision / date) AND the PLACEMENT-readiness facts (scale callout + bar, north arrow, drawn boundary, stated coord system, labeled dimensions) in the shape of `src/shared/placement/placementFacts.js`. Pixel-geometry (scale-bar length in px, dimension endpoints) is deliberately left to the later CV step (B268/B183) ‚Äî the read captures presence + printed values, never guessed geometry. `parseStatedScaleFeetPerInch` handles engineer's (`1"=40'`) + architectural (`1/4"=1'-0"`) scales, NTS‚Üínull.
- **Matcher** `server/filing/matcher.js` (pure) ‚Äî scores each project on parcel/account (exact) ‚Üí job number (exact) ‚Üí address (token overlap) ‚Üí name (token overlap), combined noisy-or; **never auto-guesses** (a misfiled drawing is worse than an unfiled one). A confident SINGLE project ‚Üí `matched`; **no / multiple / low-confidence** ‚Üí `needsFiling` with a reason (`no-readable-identifiers` / `no-match` / `ambiguous` / `low-confidence`). Thresholds tunable via env. `scoreProject` is transparent (lists the signal it matched on). Auto-name `server/filing/naming.js` mirrors the canonical `reviewStore.composeTitle` "<Project> - <Item> - YYYY.MM.DD".
- **Service + HTTP** `server/filing/filingService.js` (read ‚Üí match ‚Üí decision + the index row) + `server/filing/server.js` (`POST /file` body = PDF bytes, `X-Planyr-Projects` header = base64 JSON; `GET /health`) ‚Äî honest status codes (200 real decision / 400 / 413 / 422 unreadable / 503 not-configured), **never a 200 with a junk decision**. `Dockerfile` (no native binary, no npm install ‚Äî built-ins only) + `README.md`. The reader/service/server are injectable end-to-end (mirrors `dwgConvert.test.js`).
- **File-facts index (Supabase Postgres, NOT /server)** ‚Äî `src/workspaces/doc-review/db/file_facts.sql`: `public.file_facts` (one small row per filed drawing: project / discipline / sheet / revision / date / match confidence / needs-filing / placement jsonb), RLS private-by-default identical in shape to `doc_reviews`, indexed `(user_id, project_id, discipline, doc_date desc)` for the north-star "map ‚Üí project ‚Üí discipline ‚Üí latest set" without re-reading the PDF. Client I/O `reviewStore.upsertFileFacts/listFileFacts` (degrade gracefully if unmigrated) + pure helpers `lib/fileIndex.js` (`toFactsRow`, `mergeFactsIntoReviews` ‚Äî surfaces captured placement on the drawer's review rows).
- **capturePlacementFacts wired (deliverable #4)** ‚Äî `src/workspaces/doc-review/lib/autofiling.js` is the real `createIndexProvider`: `capturePlacementFacts` + `autofile` ride the SAME server read. `backendReady` reflects `VITE_AUTOFILE_ENABLED` honestly (false by default ‚Üí UI never claims "auto-detected" while dormant). Same-origin proxy `functions/api/file.js` (verifies the Supabase session, forwards to Cloud Run `DOC_FILING_URL`; 503 until set). The drawer drop handler auto-files when `backendReady`, else the **exact** prior manual path (a 404/503 is a graceful SKIP, like the Drive path) ‚Äî **no regression**.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 602 tests (52 new: `test/docFiling.test.js` 37, `test/autofiling.test.js` 15) ¬∑ build green; doc-review lazy-chunk split intact.** Headless on the built app (`ui-audit/verify-b299-autofiling.mjs`): the Project Files drawer opens, the new `autofilingProvider`/`fileIndex` imports evaluate in a real browser, **0 page/console errors**, auto-filing dormant by default (no spurious "it files itself" behavior). The signed-in drop‚Üíread‚Üífile round-trip + the live read are the deploy-gated checks (sandbox blocks sign-in + no key) ‚Äî logged as **VERIFICATION V74**.
- **Dedup:** this is the backend that fills the `createIndexProvider.capturePlacementFacts` seam B180/B181 stubbed and the auto-filing roadmap item; it WRITES THROUGH the Drive substrate (B207) and feeds the placement cascade (B182/B183). Distinct from B266/B267/B268 (the in-Markup sheet-label/scale siblings of the read pass) ‚Äî those share the title-block read principle but run browser-side on the open sheet; this is the filing index. **Owner to-do (deploy, when ready):** `gcloud run deploy` `server/filing/` + set `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (server-side) + point `DOC_FILING_URL` at it + set `VITE_AUTOFILE_ENABLED=1` + run `db/file_facts.sql` once.

### B297 ‚Äî First/last name capture at signup + a real `profiles` table `[Auth / Backend]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; first labeled B271, renumbered **B297** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B271‚ÄìB296)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eloquent-edison-6anmlb`).** Names are now persisted in a queryable **`public.profiles`** table (one row per `auth.uid()`), not just in auth `user_metadata` ‚Äî the scalable foundation for the B2B direction (org/role/prefs later). The signup form already collected First/Last/Org; that path is unchanged (still seeds `signUp({ options: { data } })`), but a DB **trigger** now copies those into the table so there's one queryable source of truth for display.
- **Migration (idempotent, run once in the Supabase SQL editor):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/db/profiles.sql` ‚Äî the `profiles` table (`id uuid pk ‚Üí auth.users on delete cascade`, `first_name`, `last_name`, `org`, `updated_at`); **RLS private-by-default** (the same select/insert/update own-row shape as `public.sites`/`public.doc_reviews`, `auth.uid() = id`, no cross-user reads, no delete ‚Äî the row lives/dies with the user); a `handle_new_user()` **SECURITY DEFINER trigger** on `auth.users insert` that inserts the matching row from `raw_user_meta_data` (the trigger route avoids the client-side follow-up-insert race ‚Äî the row always exists before the user can read it); and a **backfill** that seeds rows for all existing users (null names are fine ‚Äî the UI falls back, see B298). `on conflict (id) do nothing` throughout so re-running is safe.
- **Client I/O + hook (additive, reuses the existing anon client + session ‚Äî no new keys):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/profile.js` (`loadProfile`/`saveProfile`, mirrors `cloudSync.js` shape; throws on a real fetch error so "no row" ‚âÝ "offline"; `saveProfile` also best-effort syncs the name into auth `user_metadata` so the table and the auth record never disagree and the offline fallback stays fresh) and `src/shared/profile/useProfile.js` ‚Äî the `useProfile(user)` hook returning `{ profile, loading, displayName, firstName, org, initial, reload, save }`, with a stale-fetch guard (a slow load can't show the previous user's profile) and an optimistic local update on save so the pill refreshes instantly.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 572 tests (562 + 10 new) ¬∑ build green.** The never-blank display chain is pure-extracted (`displayNameFor`/`firstNameFor`/`orgFor`/`initialFor`) and unit-tested in `test/profileDisplay.test.js` (profile wins over metadata; First Last ‚Üí first ‚Üí last ‚Üí metadata ‚Üí email; whitespace-only trims to email; empty only when there's no user). The actual cloud round-trip (real profiles table read/write while signed in) needs a signed-in click-through ‚Äî the sandbox proxy CORS-blocks auth ‚Äî logged as **VERIFICATION V73**.
> **Dedup:** builds on the existing email/password auth (Supabase Phases 2‚Äì4) and the `AuthPanel` signup form (which already had the name fields). Distinct from the Site Model `status` reuse (B14) ‚Äî this is per-*user* identity, not per-*project* lifecycle. The deferred `planarfit:* ‚Üí planyr:*` localStorage rename is untouched (separate item).

### B282 ‚Äî Opening a file from the global Project Files panel no-ops on the first click when launched from another workspace `[Doc Review]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, repro'd in the signed-in session; arrived as "NEW-1"; first filed B270 then renumbered **B282** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B270‚ÄìB281 (incl. a different B270, the Project Files drop-zone queue) while this was in flight, so B282 is the real next free ID. "NEW-1" is only a scratch label ‚Äî B180/B206/B266/B270 also "arrived as NEW-1".)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/wonderful-galileo-abbbus`).** From the Site side, opening the global **üóÇ Files** panel (with a project like Jacintoport open) and clicking a filed document (e.g. the MEP set) switched to the **Markup** tab but landed on the empty **"Open or drop a construction PDF"** placeholder ‚Äî the document did **not** open; it stayed empty even after a multi-second wait, with **no console errors** (silent). The breadcrumb also reset to "Select a project". Clicking the **same file a second time** (now that Document Review was mounted) opened it correctly. 
- **Root cause (confirmed via the repro).** Document Review is a **lazy-loaded workspace** ‚Äî the Shell renders only the active workspace (`React.lazy`/`Suspense`), so DR's code doesn't mount until you first enter the tab. The **global** Project Files drawer lives in the Site Planner (`SitePlanner.jsx`), and its open handler was `onOpenReview={() => onShellSwitch?.("doc-review")}` ‚Äî it **switched workspaces but threw away the clicked review row entirely**. So in the same tick the app switched to DR *and* dropped the open request; DR mounted fresh and booted to its default/resume state, never opening the clicked file. The second click worked because DR was by then already mounted and its **own** in-workspace drawer wires `onOpenReview={openReview}` (the real handler). (The in-workspace path was never broken ‚Äî only the cross-workspace one.)
- **Fix ‚Äî persist the open-intent across the mount, mirroring the existing `navIntent` pattern.** New **`docIntent`** channel in `Shell.jsx`: `openReviewInDocReview(row)` stashes a **token-stamped** `{ kind:"open-review", row }` and *then* switches to `doc-review`; the Shell passes `docIntent` + `onOpenReviewInDocReview` to every workspace (parallel to the `navIntent`/Dashboard plumbing). The Site Planner's global drawer now calls `onOpenReview={(row) => onOpenReviewInDocReview?.(row)}` (threaded `SitePlannerApp` ‚Üí `SitePlanner`), handing the **whole review row** up. `DocReview` consumes the pending intent in a mount/update effect (`openReview(row)`), guarded by a **module-scoped `lastConsumedDocToken`** (same technique as `SitePlannerApp`'s `lastConsumedNavToken`) so a plain tab switch-back never re-fires the last open.
- **No race with resume.** DR's boot effect (resume-the-last-review) now **stands down** when a fresh open-intent is present at mount (captured once via `bootDocIntentRef`), so the two async loads can't fight and silently land the wrong file.
- **Breadcrumb carries through.** `markupProject` is **seeded from the fresh intent** at mount (handling both a `listReviews` row's `project_id` and a loaded record's `projectId`), and `openReview` re-confirms it after load ‚Äî so the project context no longer flashes to "Select a project".
- **Can't fail silently again.** `openReview` is hardened: it wraps `loadReview` in try/catch and, when the row can't be loaded (removed row / cloud unreachable), shows a **visible dismissible error banner** ("Couldn't open ‚Ä¶") with a **Browse Files‚Ä¶** retry, instead of the previous bare `if (!rec) return`.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 550 tests ¬∑ build green; the DocReview / SitePlannerApp / ProjectFilesDrawer lazy chunks all still split (workspace isolation intact).** Headless smoke on the **built** app (`ui-audit/verify-new1.mjs`): Document Review **mounts and remounts cleanly** with the new `docIntent` prop + ref capture + intent effect + hardened `openReview` + error banner ‚Äî **zero JS errors** on a fresh mount AND after an unmount/remount. The signed-in **first-click open** itself (global Files ‚Üí click a real filed set ‚Üí DR opens it on the *first* click, breadcrumb shows the project) is **auth-gated** ‚Äî the sandbox proxy blocks sign-in and this build has no Supabase creds, so the panel can't list real files headless ‚Äî logged for a live signed-in confirm on planyr.io as **VERIFICATION V70**.
> **Dedup:** net-new ‚Äî the only cross-workspace "open a file into Document Review" handler is the global `ProjectFilesDrawer` rendered by `SitePlanner` (the in-workspace DR drawer + `ReviewsBar` + `ProjectLibrary` already call `openReview` directly and were unaffected). Distinct from **B180** (the Files tagged-index/saved-views feature this rides on) and from the silent-no-op family (**B82** calibrate, **B32** undo, the map-click open in B66) ‚Äî those are unrelated surfaces. Reuses the **B191‚ÄìB193** `navIntent` cross-workspace pattern rather than inventing a new mechanism. Distinct from the concurrently-landed **B270** (Project Files drop-zone + processing queue) ‚Äî same `ProjectFilesDrawer` file, unrelated concern (file ingestion vs. cross-workspace open).
