### B283 ‚Äî Coverage detection engine + honest per-layer status states `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B283** ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B273)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** New **`lib/coverage.js`** engine answers, per layer, whether its DATA reaches the current view ‚Äî so a layer that loads green but paints blank outside its region reads as "no data here," not "broken" (the COH water/sewer/storm root cause). Each layer is tagged **national | statewide | regional** (`LAYER_SCOPE`). For a **regional** layer the engine reads the service's own **`fullExtent` from the existing `?f=json` health probe** (`probeService` now captures it ‚Äî **no extra request**), reprojects it to lat/lon, buffers it by the nearby radius (NEW-2/B284), and intersects it with the viewport ‚Üí **`in` / `out` / `unknown`**. The three honest states (`displayCoverage`): **data-in-view**, **covers-region-but-empty-here**, **out-of-coverage**. National/statewide are **always in-coverage** (their empty/painted state still comes from the in-view query). **Fails open everywhere** ‚Äî missing extent or errored probe ‚Üí treated as available, never hidden.
- **Real reprojection (the crux):** services publish their extent in mixed SRs ‚Äî verified live 2026-06-20 that **HCFCD/City-of-Houston use EPSG:2278 (Texas State-Plane, US ft)** while AGOL layers use **Web Mercator (3857)**. So the shared `src/shared/coordinates/index.js` stub's reserved **`projectToGrid`/`gridToProject`** are now **implemented** (Lambert Conformal Conic 2SP per EPSG GN 7-2), **validated against pyproj to <1e-4¬∞**; `coverage.js` dispatches 4326 / Web-Mercator / 2278 and reprojects all 4 extent corners to safely enclose the conic footprint. This is a read-only screening use ‚Äî the planner keeps its own per-site feet frame.
- **HARD RULE honoured + unit-tested:** coverage is a **picker-only** signal and **never** alters a layer's request bbox/where/extent. The request-spec builders live in a leaflet-free **`lib/layerRequest.js`** that takes **no coverage input by construction**; `test/coverage.test.js` asserts the COH request always carries its **full pinned sublayer set [0,1] and no where/bbox**, coverage-independent.
- **Wired** into the map finder + planner (recompute coverage on map move / view change, debounced, + when the nearby-range pref changes; regional extents prefetched once via the health probe and cached). **Tests:** `coverage.test.js` (27) + projection assertions in `coordinates.test.js` + `layerRequest.test.js` ‚Äî **609 tests green**, lint 0, build green, lazy chunks intact. **Verified live headless** (`gis-verify/coverage-picker-verify.mjs`, V71): panning north out of Houston flipped **HCFCD (State-Plane path) + H-GAC ETJ (Web-Mercator path)** to "No data in this area," 0 JS errors.

### B284 ‚Äî Coverage-aware layer picker: relevance modes + nearby range `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature) ‚Äî depends on B283  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B284**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** The Layers panel (`components/LayerPanel.jsx`) now consumes B283's coverage. A **"Relevance"** control ‚Äî **Show all / Dim / Hide** (**Dim** is the default) ‚Äî plus an adjustable **"nearby range"** slider (default **2.5 mi**, the buffer fed back into B283) decide how out-of-coverage layers are presented:
- **Dim:** out-of-coverage layers sink to the bottom of their group, grayed, with a **"No data in this area"** caption ‚Äî still one-click toggleable.
- **Hide:** they collapse behind a **"Show N layers with no local data here"** toggle (reveal shows them dimmed).
- A layer that is currently **ON is never demoted** (you always see what you've enabled). The mode + radius are **shared across both the map-finder and planner panels and persisted** (`coverage.js` prefs with pub/sub, `planarfit:relevance:v1`), so a change in one panel reflects in the other live.
- **List ordering/visibility ONLY ‚Äî never the rendered map** (the map is driven by `overlays` + `syncOverlayLayers`, untouched). `normalizeMode`/`normalizeRadius` clamp + default; unit-tested. **Verified live** (V71): the control + slider render, Dim is default, and the dim/"No data in this area" treatment fires on a real pan out of region.

Needs a free access token."**; the **"Mapillary"** brand (which the owner didn't recognize) is **demoted to a small `Source: Mapillary` attribution note** (`EVIDENCE.mapillary` in `layers.js`; LayerPanel renders the new `sublabel` + `source`). **Verified live** (V71): the new name + sublabel + source render and the old "Street-level detections" name is gone.

### B286 ‚Äî Mapillary layer was inert ‚Äî gated clearly as "needs setup" + excluded from the default set `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B286**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** The layer fired zero requests + showed a red "failed"-style "Add a Mapillary token" message as shipped ‚Äî it never worked. **Chose option (b): keep it, but gate it honestly** (not (a) bake a token ‚Äî that violates the secrets rule and ships a shared rate-limited key; not (c) remove ‚Äî its detections can be richer/fresher than OSM later, and the owner can have it gone with one word). A new **`needsSetup` flag** marks it as **not part of the default working set** (the relevance picker sorts a tokenless instance to the bottom as "Needs setup"), and the no-token state now reads **"Not configured ‚Äî add a free access token to enable this layer"** via a distinct **`unconfigured`** status (a gray "needs setup" dot, **not** the alarming red "failed") in `syncOverlayLayers` + `evidenceLayers.mapillaryLayer` ‚Äî and **no error toast** fires. **Note:** poles already come from OSM and hydrants from OSM + City-of-Houston, so this layer is redundant-but-optional today; say the word and it's removed entirely. **Verified live** (V71): toggling it (no token) reads "Not configured", no red failure.

### B287 ‚Äî Retry/backoff for transient 5xx on jurisdiction VECTOR services (City ETJ, County boundaries) `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5" 2026-06-20; minted **B287**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/busy-allen-ofgy9l`).** Live 2026-06-20 the City ETJ (H-GAC FeatureServer) and County-boundaries (TxDOT/AGOL) layers threw intermittent **503s on their geojson queries**. **Deduped against the existing retry/backoff** and found the gap: raster tiles already retry via `withTileRetry` and the `?f=json` metadata probe via `fetchWithRetry`, but **esri-leaflet's FeatureLayer issues its own GeoJSON query with no retry** ‚Äî so one transient blip dropped the whole vector layer to "failed." New **`attachFeatureRetry`** (`layers.js`) wires a pure **`featureRetryDecision`** policy (`layerRequest.js`) onto every `esriFeature` layer: on a `requesterror` it re-issues via `refresh()` with **exponential backoff** (400‚Üí800‚Üí1600 ms), holds the dot at "loading" while retrying, reports "failed" **only after `max` retries**, and resets on a successful `load`; a **hard 4xx is permanent** (no retry). The transient set (`429, 500, 502, 503, 504`) is now **one shared constant** (`TRANSIENT_STATUS`) across raster/metadata/vector. **9 unit tests** (`layerRequest.test.js`); lint 0 ¬∑ 609 tests ¬∑ build green.

### B279 ‚Äî Production error telemetry ‚Üí Supabase table `[Infra / Telemetry]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20 owner chat; filed **B279** in the B278‚ÄìB281 Infra tranche ‚Äî jumped past B271‚ÄìB277 consumed by concurrent `main` + PR #217; batch comment lives in BACKLOG.md)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/trusting-hawking-1c4d6g`).** The app now self-reports runtime errors so silent production failures stop being invisible until someone stumbles on them. New **`src/shared/telemetry/clientErrors.js`**: three global sources ‚Äî window `error`, window `unhandledrejection`, and Vite's `vite:preloadError` ‚Äî plus the React **ErrorBoundary** (`componentDidCatch`) all funnel into one fire-and-forget sink that inserts a row into a new **`public.client_errors`** table via the EXISTING anon Supabase client (the "Supabase table, not Sentry" decision ‚Äî no new vendor, no new keys). Installed in `main.jsx` before render; the Shell tags each row with the active workspace (`setTelemetryModule`).
- **Session-optional + no read hole (RLS):** `src/shared/telemetry/client_errors.sql` makes the table **INSERT-only** for `anon` + `authenticated` (no SELECT/UPDATE/DELETE policy), so an error **during login ‚Äî before any session exists ‚Äî still records**, and clients can write but can never read the table back (admins read via the dashboard / service role). `user_id` defaults to `auth.uid()` (null when anonymous); `WITH CHECK (user_id is null or user_id = auth.uid())` blocks forging another user's id. **Run the SQL once in the Supabase SQL editor** (idempotent; same pattern as `doc_reviews.sql`).
- **Fail-safe + storm guard:** every path swallows its own errors and never rethrows into the app (telemetry that throws is worse than none). `decideReport` (pure, unit-tested) suppresses an exact-duplicate signature within 10 s and caps sends to 20/min, so a render-loop error storm becomes a handful of rows, not thousands. Messages/stacks truncated (2 k / 8 k). NOT capture-phase, so blocked tiles / broken images don't spam it.
- **Build provenance:** `vite.config.js` bakes the short git SHA into the bundle (`__BUILD_ID__` define, read via a typeof guard ‚Üí "dev" under dev/test) and stamps it on every row, so a report traces back to the exact deploy.
- **Dedup (the filing's own correction held):** the `vite:preloadError` listener it "pairs with" already existed and shipped (**B221** `installChunkReloadGuard`, `src/app/chunkReload.js`); this **adds** a telemetry write for that event through its OWN listener (chunkReload.js left untouched + pure). NET-NEW otherwise ‚Äî no prior telemetry / Sentry item in either file.
- **Verification:** lint **0 errors** (only the pre-existing `SitePlanner.jsx`/`MapFinder.jsx` warnings); **587 tests** (12 new in `test/clientErrors.test.js` ‚Äî storm-guard dup/rate/window, row shaping, message/stack extraction + truncation, signature); `npm run build` green, all three workspace lazy chunks intact, `__BUILD_ID__` fully replaced (no leftover token). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-telemetry.mjs`, **6/6** on the built bundle via `vite preview`, re-run clean after merging the latest `main`): all three global sources captured with the correct `source` tag, a duplicate suppressed, build id baked in, and the page stays alive after firing synthetic errors (fail-safe). The live **cloud insert** (signed-in, after the one-time SQL) is the one auth-only path the sandbox can't exercise logged-out ‚Üí logged in **VERIFICATION V69**.
> Independent of the B278 (Playwright) ID-collision concern; built + shipped this same session per the owner's "ship ship and then build whatever you need to." B278 / B280 / B281 stay Open (CI/secret-bound ‚Äî see their `‚õî Verify-blocker` notes).

### B277 ‚Äî Overlay visibility toggle (hide without deleting) `[Document Review / Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B277** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B270‚ÄìB273 while this was in flight; batch B274‚ÄìB277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** Added a per-overlay eye / eye-slash toggle to the Site-plan overlay panel (`SitePlanner.jsx`) so a placed overlay can be switched OFF the map without deleting it ‚Äî the standard layers-UI affordance (Bluebeam/ArcGIS/Photoshop). Distinct from B272's delete (hide ‚âÝ delete): a hidden overlay stays in the panel, listed + recoverable.
- **Render:** the canvas overlay map skips an overlay with `visible === false` (returns null) ‚Äî off the map, still in the panel with the eye-slash to bring it back. **Persistence:** `visible` rides in the overlay record (saved + cloud-slimmed + content-merged like every other overlay field), so a hidden overlay stays hidden across reload (and, signed in, across devices); it's also folded into the undo/redo signature so a hide/show is undoable.
- **Data shape was already reserved (B131):** `isOverlayPrintable = o.src && o.visible !== false` was shipped "forward-compatible with a future per-overlay hide," so hiding an overlay **also drops it from Print/PNG export automatically** (WYSIWYG) ‚Äî no extra wiring. Inline `EyeIcon`/`EyeOffIcon` SVGs render crisply everywhere.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-overlay-delete-hide.mjs`, the built app, logged-out): hide removes the overlay from the map but KEEPS it listed; the hidden state PERSISTS across reload (the record carries `visible:false`); show brings it back. lint 0 ¬∑ 549 tests ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview` lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** B131 (print-overlay master toggle) reserved the `visible` semantics; this implements the per-overlay UI toggle it anticipated. Pairs with B276 (delete persistence) ‚Äî same overlay surface, shipped together. (B314/B313, the data-integrity pair from the same batch, shipped this session too.)

### B276 ‚Äî Overlay delete doesn't persist across reload `[Document Review / Site Planner]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, "Jacinto Port"; arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B276** ‚Äî concurrent `main` consumed B270‚ÄìB273; batch B274‚ÄìB277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** Deleting a placed overlay (the owner's "Jacinto Port" sheet) made it vanish, but it RETURNED on reload. **Root cause (as the backlog predicted):** the cross-copy reconciler `mergeSiteContent` (`siteModel.js`) **unions `sheetOverlays` by id**, so when the post-delete local copy (overlay gone) is merged with a copy that still has it ‚Äî the cloud copy on the next `pullCloud`/`mergePulledSites`, or another tab via the `storage` fold ‚Äî the deleted overlay is **resurrected**. Exactly the documented B126 union-merge trade-off ("a delete in only one copy can reappear once ‚Äî per-item tombstones are the fully-correct future hardening"); `removeOverlay` only dropped it from local state, nothing recorded that the deletion was deliberate.
- **Fix ‚Äî per-item tombstones (`deletedIds`), the B126 hardening, now built:** an additive Site Model field (`SITE_MODEL_VERSION` 5‚Üí6) holding ids the user deliberately deleted. `mergeSiteContent` unions the `deletedIds` from BOTH copies and **drops any tombstoned id from every unioned collection**, so a deletion wins over presence in either copy ‚Äî across reload, tab-sync, and device-sync. `removeOverlay` records the tombstone; it's threaded through the save effect, the live/undo refs, the cross-tab `storage` fold, `applySnapshot`, and version-restore so it persists and undo correctly resurrects (the tombstone rolls back with the overlay). Bounded + deduped (‚â§5000 ids).
- **General but scoped:** the mechanism works for any collection (a tombstoned building stays deleted too) but is wired only at the overlay delete site for now; other delete handlers can adopt `setDeletedIds` trivially. **No regression:** collections not yet recording a tombstone keep the existing recoverable union behavior; `slimForCloud`/`slimForHistory` pass `deletedIds` through untouched (only inline rasters are stripped). **Composes with B297** (optimistic concurrency, shipped this session): a delete already rides the normal save, so it'll advance B297's version like any edit.
- **Verified:** unit ‚Äî `test/storage.test.js` (6 new B276 cases: tombstone in either copy wins, set-union, no-regression on non-tombstoned items, generalizes to a building, end-to-end through `mergePulledSites`). Headless ‚Äî `ui-audit/verify-overlay-delete-hide.mjs` (built app, logged-out): delete persists across reload and the record carries the `deletedIds` tombstone. lint 0 ¬∑ **549 tests** ¬∑ build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** net-new bug; the fix is the per-item tombstone B126 explicitly deferred. Distinct from B260 (overlay *scale* misread, done). Pairs with B277 (visibility), shipped together.
### B313 ‚Äî Multi-tab open warning (same project open in another browser tab) `[App Shell]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B313** ‚Äî renumbered B275‚ÜíB298‚ÜíB313 as a very hot `main` reached B311; pairs with B314 + the already-live B276/B277)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`).** A non-blocking header banner now warns when the SAME project is open in another tab of the same browser ‚Äî "This project is open in another tab. Editing it in more than one tab can conflict ‚Äî work in a single tab to be safe." ‚Äî so a two-tab clash isn't a surprise. Same-browser only; cross-DEVICE conflicts are B314's server guard.
- **How:** `src/shared/presence/multiTab.js` ‚Äî a BroadcastChannel (same-origin cross-tab bus) presence tracker. Each tab announces its open project (`hello`/`here`/`update`/`bye` + a heartbeat); a pure `summarizePresence` reduces the live peer set into the banner state (conflict only when another tab is on the *same* project; stale peers pruned by TTL). Wired into the shared `AppHeader` via a `useMultiTab(projectId)` hook (BOTH workspaces get it); the banner clears the moment the other tab closes/navigates (its `bye`, or the TTL). Degrades to a silent no-op where BroadcastChannel is unavailable.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-multitab.mjs`, 4/4, the built app, two real tabs in one browser context): Tab A alone shows nothing; opening Tab B on the same project raises the banner in BOTH; closing Tab B clears A's banner. Plus **10 unit tests** (`test/multiTab.test.js`) incl. a real two-instance BroadcastChannel round-trip (same-project ‚Üí conflict; different project ‚Üí present-but-no-conflict; clears on leave). lint 0 ¬∑ build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** the VISIBLE companion to B127 (which made two same-browser tabs silently *converge*) ‚Äî surfaces the situation, doesn't replace the merge. **Optional, deliberately not built:** the Web Locks single-active-editor *lock* (non-leader tabs go read-only) ‚Äî the spec marked it optional; the banner is the required warning, the read-only lockout is an invasive follow-up. Pairs with B314 (the cross-device half).

### B314 ‚Äî Reject stale saves (optimistic concurrency on the save path) `[Platform / Persistence]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B314** ‚Äî renumbered B274‚ÜíB297‚ÜíB314 as a very hot `main` reached B311; pairs with B313)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/peaceful-ride-k41y6e`); migration RUN by owner 2026-06-20 ‚Üí goes ACTIVE on deploy.** Two sessions editing the same project no longer silently last-write-wins: a save carries the `version` it last synced, and the DB applies it ONLY if the stored version still matches (a single atomic conditional UPDATE), bumping it. A stale write (another session advanced the row) is **REJECTED as a conflict**, not applied ‚Äî the Site Planner shows a loud blue "this project was changed in another session ‚Äî reload before saving" banner with a **Reload** button. No silent clobber; work is never lost (the edit is saved on-device, and the reload union-merges it via mergeSiteContent, then re-pushes the combined result).
- **Reusable primitive (foundation for the deferred multi-user feature):** `src/shared/cloud/optimisticUpsert.js` ‚Äî a pure `casUpsert` compare-and-swap over `(user_id, id, version)`, used by BOTH `public.sites` (cloudSync.js) and `public.doc_reviews` (reviewStore.js). Version tokens are tracked per-tab in the cloud layer (populated on list/load, advanced on each write, cleared on delete / user-switch), so a conflict propagates back as a typed `{ conflict:true }` the UI turns into the reload prompt. Doc Review surfaces it on its save badge (the persistence hook gains a `conflict` state).
- **Graceful degradation = merge-safe:** before the migration ran, the conditional write returned "column version does not exist" and the client fell back to a plain upsert (today's EXACT behaviour) ‚Äî so saving never regressed; the guard was simply dormant. (The detector requires the error name the *version* column, so doc_reviews' optional library columns can't be mistaken for it and wrongly disable the guard.)
- **Verified:** **16 unit tests** (`test/cloudConcurrency.test.js`) cover the whole matrix ‚Äî conflict (0 rows), success (+version), degrade (un-migrated), brand-new insert, unique-violation‚Üíconflict, never-throws, and the not-the-version-column guard. The live cloud conflict path needs sign-in (the sandbox blocks auth logged-out), so it's logged for a signed-in click-through (VERIFICATION V79). lint 0 ¬∑ build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **‚úÖ MIGRATION RUN (owner, 2026-06-20):** `src/workspaces/site-planner/db/optimistic_concurrency.sql` was run in the Supabase SQL editor (added the `version` column to `sites` + `doc_reviews`). The guard goes ACTIVE on this deploy. Composes with B276's tombstones (a delete advances the version like any write).

### B271 ‚Äî Canvas could get stuck unclickable behind a frozen grab/hand cursor when a pointer gesture was interrupted `[Core / Site Planner + Doc Review]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20 via chat, with a screenshot of the "Claude is debugging this browser" banner; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B271** ‚Äî real next free ID after concurrent `main` consumed B270)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/gifted-lamport-miamoc`).** Owner hit a state where the whole app went unclickable ‚Äî a hand cursor over everything, clicks doing nothing ‚Äî while every other website kept working. It coincided with a browser devtools/remote-debugger session attaching to the tab (the on-screen "Claude is debugging this browser" banner), but the fragility is **ours**: Planyr was the only page that locked up, so a latent bug in our pointer handling is the real cause (the attachment merely exposed it).
- **Root cause.** The planner canvas (`SitePlanner.jsx`) starts a pan/drag by capturing the pointer (`setPointerCapture`) and setting `panning` + `drag.current`, and relied **only** on `onPointerUp` (`onUp`) to release capture and clear that state. But the browser fires **`pointercancel`** (not `pointerup`) when a gesture is interrupted ‚Äî a devtools/remote-debugger session attaching, an OS gesture takeover, or the window losing focus mid-drag ‚Äî and the canvas had **no `onPointerCancel` handler and no blur/visibility recovery**. So the cleanup never ran: `panning` stayed `true` (cursor stuck on the select-mode grab/grabbing hand) with pointer-capture still held ‚Üí the canvas swallowed every click. Other sites don't hold global pan/drag state, which is exactly why only Planyr broke. The same capture-pan pattern (same latent lockup) existed in the Doc Review **Stitcher** and the **ParcelDrawing** canvas.
- **Fix ‚Äî four independent recovery paths where there were zero** (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `doc-review/Stitcher.jsx`, `site-planner/components/ParcelDrawing.jsx`):
  1. **`onPointerCancel` on each canvas** ‚Üí an `abortGesture()` that releases pointer-capture (via `e.pointerId`) and clears `drag.current` / `panning` / the in-progress marquee + draw drafts (it **aborts**, never commits a half-finished gesture).
  2. **Window `blur` + `visibilitychange`(hidden) recovery** ‚Üí same teardown, **plus** it drops the Space hold-to-pan flag (`spaceRef`/`spacePan`) so a missed Space key-up can't leave the hand cursor on. Mirrors the existing Shift-reset-on-blur effect.
  3. **Escape** now also tears the gesture down (release capture + clear `drag`/`panning`/`spacePan`) ‚Äî a manual safety hatch on top of the draft/menu reset it already did.
  4. **`onBgDown`/`onUp` bookkeeping** ‚Äî record the captured pointer id (`capturePidRef`) so blur/Escape can release a capture they didn't see start, cleared on normal release.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 543 tests ¬∑ build green; lazy chunks (`SitePlannerApp`/`DocReview`) intact.** New headless test `ui-audit/verify-pointer-recover.mjs` drives a **real** pointer on the **built** app: a pan shows `grabbing`; **window blur** mid-pan recovers the cursor to `grab`; a **`pointercancel`** mid-pan recovers to `grab`; the canvas is still interactive afterward (a fresh pan re-engages); no uncaught errors. Before the fix, both interruptions left `grabbing` stuck (the lockup).
- **Dedup:** folds into the established pointer-capture discipline already in `onUp` (`setPointerCapture`/`releasePointerCapture`), not a parallel mechanism. The "ghost portal overlay" hypothesis was investigated and **disproved** as the cause: the full-canvas inline-editor catchers (`numEdit`/`editCallout`) already commit-and-clear on pointerdown and are bounded by their own state ‚Äî the stuck pointer-capture / stuck-pan path is what produced the lockout. Secondary "main-thread stall" hypothesis tracked separately as **B272** (investigated; no actionable bug; low priority).

### B270 ‚Äî Project Files: persistent drop-zone + processing queue (multi-file ingestion + persistent upload tray) `[Site Planner / Document Review ‚Äî Project Files]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" from a parallel chat ‚Äî only Amendments A & B reached this session; minted **B270**, the real next free ID after concurrent `main` consumed B246‚ÄìB269)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/quirky-bardeen-xje4nv`).** Turned the Project Files drop zone (the shared `ProjectFilesDrawer`, opened from Row 1 across workspaces) from a one-file-at-a-time loop that reported errors through a `window.alert` (a KEY-DECISION violation) into a **persistent processing queue with an upload tray**. Pure, browser-free model + derived view in **`src/shared/files/uploadQueue.js`** (`QUEUE_STATUS`, `makeQueueItem`/`makeQueueItems`, `splitQueue` (the derived two-group view), `hasPendingDemote`, `runPool` (concurrency pool), `isAcceptedFile`; **12 unit tests**, `test/uploadQueue.test.js`). UI wiring in `ProjectFilesDrawer.jsx` (`UploadTray` + `QueueRow` + the ingest/pipeline/demote logic); demote slide/fade in `index.css`.
- **Folded spec ‚Äî Amendment A (multi-file ingestion is first-class).** Drop, the native file picker (`multiple`), AND clipboard paste all funnel through one `ingest()` that iterates the file list and creates **one independent queue item per file**, each with its own `uploadId`, run through a small **concurrency pool** (3 at a time) ‚Äî so dropping 8 files yields **8 independent concurrent rows**, not one batch row and not a serialized chain. **Mixed types in one action:** PDFs enter the pipeline; unsupported types get a clear **per-file rejection row** (`rejected`, with a Dismiss √ó) ‚Äî never silently discarded.
- **Folded spec ‚Äî Amendment B (persistent tray, not a vanishing toast).** Filed items do not disappear from under the user. On success a row goes to a calm muted **`done`** state (green check, reduced weight); after a ~3s confirmation beat it **demotes** from the active **PROCESSING** group into a collapsible **"Recently filed ¬∑ N"** group via a subtle slide/fade ‚Äî never an abrupt removal. The trail **collapses by default once it has more than ~3 entries** and has a **Clear** affordance. `needs_filing` (filed but unrouted ‚Äî a **Triage** button jumps to the holding area's one-click confirm) and `failed` (a **Retry** button) **never auto-dismiss** ‚Äî they stay in the active group until the user acts. **Net:** active group = in-flight + exceptions (live to-do); recently-filed = an auditable, clearable trail. The two groups are a **derived view over one queue array** (filter by status + a `filedAt` timestamp), not two lists ‚Äî the demote is a status/timestamp transition, exactly as the implementation note specified.
- **Graceful degrade kept:** an oversize (>50 MB) or upload-failed file still files the work layer and the row carries a non-fatal "re-drop on open to view" warn (it is `done`, not `failed`); a Drive-copy failure is a soft warn too. "Drive not enabled yet" stays silent (B207 best-effort).
- **Verification:** lint clean on the changed files (the 13 repo warnings are all pre-existing in `SitePlanner.jsx`); **549 tests** (537 + 12) green; `npm run build` green; the doc-review/`ProjectFilesDrawer` lazy chunk split still holds (28 kB chunk). Real-browser headless: (a) the existing `verify-files-refile.mjs` still PASSes (drawer mounts, **0 JS errors** ‚Äî the new imports/components load), and (b) drove a **mixed 3-file pick** through the real component ‚Üí **"PROCESSING ¬∑ 3"**, two PDF rows + one **"Not a PDF" rejection row** with Dismiss, Retry buttons, **no `window.alert`** (screenshot captured). The `done`‚ÜíRecently-filed demote / >3 collapse / Clear need a *successful* cloud filing (= sign-in, which the sandbox blocks logged-out) ‚Äî that path is unit-tested (`splitQueue`/`hasPendingDemote`/`RECENT_COLLAPSE_AT`) and logged for a signed-in click-through in VERIFICATION (**V66**).
> **Dedup ‚Äî build on what's shipped, don't fork:** this upgrades **B180**'s drop zone (the saved-views drawer) and reuses **B217**'s "needs filing" holding area + one-click confirm (Triage routes there ‚Äî no second filing UI). **Auto-file-by-title-block** (read title block ‚Üí match a project ‚Üí auto-route/auto-name; low-confidence ‚Üí holding area) is **NOT** this item ‚Äî it stays the **backend tranche** (B180 ‚è≥ + the auto-filing roadmap item), stubbed behind `createIndexProvider`; B270 is the browser-only ingestion/queue surface it will feed. Filing still files under the active project (or the holding area) until that lands.

### B265 ‚Äî Doc Review (Markup) PDF render is blurry ‚Äî honour devicePixelRatio `[Doc Review / Markup]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; renumbered **B265** as concurrent `main` consumed B246‚ÄìB264; batch B265‚ÄìB269, the other four filed Open: B266/B267/B268/B269)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/friendly-euler-hw8v1t`, PR #205).** Sheets in Markup rendered soft/illegible ‚Äî note text unreadable at fit-to-page, only marginally better zoomed ‚Äî because `renderPageToCanvas` (`src/workspaces/doc-review/lib/pdf.js`) sized the canvas backing store to `(scale √ó base)` with **no devicePixelRatio factor** and gave the canvas no explicit CSS size, so on a HiDPI/Retina display the browser **upscaled a 1√ó-density bitmap** to fill 2√ó physical pixels = blur. (Same HiDPI class as the Site Planner's B169/B170 basemap fix ‚Äî different surface: the PDF.js canvas, not Leaflet tiles.)
- **Fix:** the page now renders the backing store at `scale √ó dpr` (`dpr = min(window.devicePixelRatio, 2)`) while the canvas's **on-screen (CSS) size stays at the logical `scale√ó` size** (`canvas.style.width/height`), so the dense bitmap is sampled down ‚Üí crisp text. A new `backingScale()` caps the backing store to a **~24 MP budget** (drops dpr toward 1√ó on a huge E-size sheet at deep zoom) so the denser render can't OOM, and **never goes below 1√ó** (never worse than before). Zoom already re-renders at the new scale (true re-rasterization); this makes every render dpr-aware.
- **Overlay geometry unchanged by construction:** `renderPageToCanvas` still returns `dims.w/h = floor(base √ó scale)` ‚Äî byte-identical to before ‚Äî and that's what both the wrapper box and the markup SVG overlay bind to, so measurements/markups land exactly where they did.
- **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new2-dpr.mjs`, the REAL built viewer driven at two pixel densities with a generated 1-page PDF): at **deviceScaleFactor 2** the backing store is **2.000√ó** the CSS size (1054‚Üí2108 px) = crisp; at **deviceScaleFactor 1** it's **1.000√ó** (unchanged); the **on-screen size is identical across both densities** (1054√ó1364) ‚Üí overlay geometry provably unaffected. lint 0 ¬∑ 543 tests ¬∑ build green; DocReview + pdf lazy chunks intact. The crispness *gain* only manifests on real HiDPI hardware (headless DPR-forcing proves the 2√ó mechanism); logged for a live retina eyeball as **VERIFICATION V65**.
> **Dedup:** net-new for the Doc Review canvas ‚Äî **B169/B170** (basemap HiDPI/retina) and the map-finder over-zoom fixes are the *Site Planner basemap-tile* siblings of the same principle, not this surface. The Stitcher's `renderPageToImage` is a separate path (fixed 2√ó + a placed-image transform), intentionally left as-is. Filed alongside **B266/B267/B268/B269** (sheet labels, auto-calibrate, scale cross-check, sample-fixture cleanup) which stay Open ‚Äî this was the cleanly-fixable, verifiable one of the batch.

### B260 ‚Äî Dropped site-plan overlay placed 10‚Äì30√ó too large when its printed scale is misread ‚Üí the drawing's title block blankets the map ("file name all over the map") `[Site Planner / overlay]` (bug)  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20 with a screenshot of "Jacinto"; arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B260** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B246 (dock-zone build-out, PR #204) and B247‚ÄìB259 (Scheduler backlog) while this was in flight, so B260 is the real next free ID after B259)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/sweet-wozniak-txzr3e`).** Owner dropped a landscape drawing onto the planner and a huge rotated string ‚Äî the sheet's title block, ~`BV-255-2024-LD1 ‚Ä¶ ARCH ASSET FOR ‚Ä¶` ‚Äî covered nearly the whole aerial; only the parcel (`26.33 ac`) looked right.
- **Diagnosis (corrected the hand-off's guess).** It is **NOT** a world-scaled *text label*: every label path in the planner is screen-space or px-capped ‚Äî element labels `11¬∑ls`, parcel acreage chip `12¬∑ls`, callouts are boxed + capped at their own `size`, all markup/measure labels are fixed px, and the overlay's name **placeholder** is a hard-coded `fontSize={13}` (confirmed in a headless seed: the placeholder text stays 13 px even when its dashed rect is huge). The giant string is the rasterized overlay **IMAGE** itself. `addOverlayFile` auto-applied a scale note read off the sheet (the B73 `trueScale` path ‚Üí `ftPerPointForScale(detectedScale)`) with **no sanity check on the resulting size**. A landscape sheet commonly prints a **vicinity / key-map scale** (e.g. 1‚Ä≥=600‚Ä≤) next to the plan scale (e.g. 1‚Ä≥=30‚Ä≤), and `parseScaleNote` returns the **first in-range match**, so the vicinity scale can win ‚Üí `ftPerPx` 10‚Äì30√ó too big ‚Üí `imgW¬∑ftPerPx¬∑ppf` renders the sheet (and its title block) enormous, spilling far past the viewport. (The drawing's white paper is knocked to transparent, so on a dark aerial the only thing that reads is the dark title-block text ‚Äî which is why it looks like "just the file name, splattered.") **Reproduced headless:** a seeded overlay at the misread 1‚Ä≥=600‚Ä≤ rendered **14279√ó9519 px** on a 1440√ó900 view.
- **Fix 1 ‚Äî guard the auto-scale (root cause).** New pure, browser-free `chooseOverlayScale()` in `lib/overlayScale.js`: trust the read scale **only** when it lands the sheet at a sane on-screen size (**‚â§4√ó / ‚â•0.04√ó the viewport width**); otherwise fall back to the existing "size to fit" (~60% of the view) and report a `too-big`/`too-small` reason. The read scale is **still stored** on the overlay, so the panel's "Read from sheet: 1‚Ä≥=X‚Ä≤ **[Apply]**" still offers it as a one-click when the user wants it. `addOverlayFile` now routes through it and, on a rejected scale, flashes an **honest, actionable** note ("‚Ä¶its printed scale would place it far too large ‚Äî sized it to fit instead; set the exact scale or 'Trace a length' in the Site-plan overlay panel"). No silent mis-place.
- **Fix 2 ‚Äî one-click rescue.** New **"Size to view"** button in the Site-plan overlay panel: resizes the selected overlay to ~60% of the current view and recenters it ‚Äî recovery for an already-splattered overlay (the owner's existing "Jacinto" file) or any manual scale slip. Distinct from "Fit view" (which zooms the canvas), with tooltips on both to disambiguate.
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 538 tests ¬∑ build green; lazy-chunk split intact.** `chooseOverlayScale` has **7 new unit tests** (`test/overlayScale.test.js`: trusts a correct 1‚Ä≥=30‚Ä≤, rejects a misread 1‚Ä≥=600‚Ä≤ as too-big, rejects a deep-zoom tiny render as too-small, falls back with no/non-standard scale, the fit fallback ‚âà 60% of the view, NaN/zero-divide defense). Headless on the **built** app (`ui-audit/verify-overlay-fix.mjs`): **(A)** dropping an image runs the real import path ‚Üí overlay lands **535 px** wide on a 1440 px view (sane, not splattered); **(B)** a seeded splattered overlay (**14279 px**) shrinks to **535 px** with one "Size to view" click (before/after screenshots). **Honest gap:** PDF rasterization can't run in the sandbox Chromium (pdf.js `getOrInsertComputed` is unsupported there), so the PDF scale-read path is covered by the unit tests + the image-path E2E rather than an end-to-end PDF drop ‚Äî logged for a real-browser confirm as **VERIFICATION V63**.
- **Dedup:** distinct from **B148** (oversized world-space *summary banner* ‚Äî a genuine screen-vs-world text bug) and builds on **B73** (the overlay scale tooling this hardens). The hand-off's "world-scaled label, scaled to the geometry's bounding box" hypothesis was investigated and **disproved** ‚Äî no label path produces it; the cause is overlay-image scaling. The "Place on map" cascade (`shared/placement/placeOnMap.js`, B182) remains a stub (`onPlaceOnMap` only closes the drawer) and emits no label, so there is **no** second "auto-place emits a bogus label" item.

### B247 ‚Äî Scheduler Export modal: Header/Cover fields drop focus after every keystroke `[Scheduler / UI]` (bug)  *(orig "B3/M4" in the owner's Planar backlog; provisionally B246, renumbered **B247** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B246 (dock-zone build-out, PR #204) while this was in flight, so B247 is the real next free ID after B246)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** In Export ‚Üí "Header / Cover", typing in Exhibit / Title / Prep. by / Prep. for / Date / Conf. tag dropped focus after each character (one keystroke at a time). **Cause:** `Field` (and `Toggle`/`SegBtn`/`Row`) were defined *inside* `PDFExportModal`, so every render minted a new component identity ‚Üí React unmounted the live `<input>` and mounted a fresh one, taking focus with it. **Fix:** hoisted `Field`/`Toggle`/`SegBtn`/`Row` to module scope (all props-only ‚Äî no closure over modal state) above `PDFExportModal`; their JSX usages are unchanged (now resolve to the stable module-scope identity). `SHdr` was deliberately left inside the modal ‚Äî it closes over `setSecOpen`/`secIsOpen`, so hoisting it would need prop-threading for zero user benefit (perf-only). **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-scheduler-bugfixes.mjs`, V62): typed "ALTA & Topo Survey ‚Äî Phase 2" character-by-character into the Title field ‚Äî full value intact, focus retained, 0 console errors.

### B248 ‚Äî Scheduler "Export Report" (HTML) doesn't escape user strings `[Scheduler / export]` (bug)  *(orig "B6¬Ω")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** The older `exportHTML` path still did raw template interpolation, so a task named "ALTA & Topo Survey" or "Budget > $1M" (or any `<`/`>`/`&` in name/owner) corrupted the downloaded HTML report. `buildPDFHtml`/`buildGanttSVG` already used the module `escapeHtml` helper; this was the last raw path. **Fix:** wrapped every interpolated user string in `exportHTML` ‚Äî project name, task id, task name, start/end dates, the status label, and owner ‚Äî in `escapeHtml(...)`. Numbers (duration, %) left as-is.

### B249 ‚Äî Deleting a custom status crashes views that still reference it `[Scheduler / status]` (bug)  *(orig "B1")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Create a custom status ‚Üí apply to tasks ‚Üí delete it, and several views went blank (the % Done cell, the HTML export) because the deleted key was dereferenced as `HEALTH[t.health].dot` with no fallback. **Fix, two halves:** **(a) Reassign on delete** ‚Äî `removeOption` now walks every project's tasks and sets `health: "gray"` ("Not Started") on any task still carrying the deleted key *before* filtering the status out (same `setData`), so no task is ever left pointing at a missing key. **(b) Defensive lookups** ‚Äî guarded the two genuinely-unguarded sites with `(HEALTH[‚Ä¶] || HEALTH.gray)` (the `exportHTML` row and the % Done cell), matching the `|| HEALTH.gray` pattern already used in ~10 spots. The project-header lookup (`HEALTH[projHealth(cur)]`) was already safe ‚Äî `projHealth` only ever returns base keys.

### B250 ‚Äî JSON import skips the normalization/migration pipeline `[Scheduler / import]` (bug)  *(orig "B4")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** `importJSON` did `setData(parsed)` raw, skipping the migration the cloud/seed **load** path runs ‚Äî so an old or partial backup could load with predecessors in the old shape, missing settings, and un-cascaded dates. **Fix:** route the import through the *same* pipeline as load: `ensureContacts(normalizeIds(ensureHolidays(normalizeToV6(parsed))))`, then rebuild `HOLIDAY_SET` and run `cascadeDates ‚Üí rollupParentDates` per project (mirrors the seed-load branch exactly). The pre-import `pre-import` snapshot is preserved. A current backup re-imports byte-identically (the migrations are idempotent); an old/partial one loads cleanly with defaults filled in.

### B251 ‚Äî New/renamed custom status renders one beat late `[Scheduler / status]` (bug)  *(orig "B5/M3")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Adding or renaming a custom status often didn't show in pickers until you clicked around. **Cause:** `HEALTH`/`HK`/`HDARK` are module-level mutable globals rebuilt by `rebuildHEALTH(...)` inside the `[data]` effect; the rebuild mutates the globals but doesn't itself re-render, so the render that processed the change read stale values. **Fix (the low-risk option A):** track a `prevHealthKey` ref of the serialized `customHealth`+`healthLabelOverrides`; after `rebuildHEALTH`, when that key actually changes, bump a small `setHealthTick` once to force a re-render that re-reads the fresh globals. Keyed so it fires only on real status-config changes, and loop-safe (the tick isn't a `[data]` dependency, so it can't re-trigger the effect) ‚Äî mirrors the existing holiday-recascade guard in the same effect. **Verified headless** (V62): boots clean, no "Maximum update depth" loop, 0 console errors.

### B252 ‚Äî Undo history holds 50 full board snapshots `[Scheduler / perf]` (task)  *(orig "P3")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/zen-bohr-7xgk6q`).** Every edit pushed a full deep copy of `data` onto the undo stack, capped at 50 (~50√ó the board's JSON held in memory). **Fix:** lowered the cap to 20 (`slice(-19)`) ‚Äî undo still works through many steps, memory footprint cut ~60%. (The bigger "snapshot only the active project / store inverse diffs" options stay deferred under B256/roadmap; not needed yet.)

### B253 ‚Äî "Today" stays fresh across midnight / tab-left-open `[Scheduler / dates]` (bug) ‚Äî already resolved  *(orig "B7")*
`[x]` **Already done in current code; verified 2026-06-20, no change needed.** The owner's doc predated the fix. `NOW` is now a live module value refreshed on `focus`, `visibilitychange`, and a 60s `setInterval`, each bumping a `todayTick` that forces the re-render that re-reads it; `computeDisplayHealth` (overdue/due-soon) and the Gantt "today" line read `NOW`; `NotesModal` stamps `toShortDate(NOW)` / `parseFlexDate(dateStr) || NOW` at open time. So the today line, overdue colouring, and new-note date all roll over without a reload. Filed for the record so the old finding is closed.

### B254 ‚Äî Split-view Snap/Free chip lingers ~5s after releasing the divider `[Scheduler / UI]` (bug?) ‚Äî resolved as won't-change  *(orig "B9"; minted **B254**)*
`[x]` **Resolved 2026-06-20 (no code change ‚Äî owner decision).** The owner's doc suspected the `setTimeout(() => setDragging(false), 5000)` (public/sequence/index.html) was a 500ms typo. **Inspected first:** the chip is an *interactive* Snap/Free toggle (fixed portal, top-right); the ~5s keeps it clickable after a drag so you can flip snap mode for the next drag without re-grabbing the divider ‚Äî i.e. the delay serves a real purpose, not an obvious typo. Raised it to Michael; he said **"don't worry about the chip thing"** ‚Üí leave the 5s as-is. Closed so it isn't re-raised. No change shipped.

### B261 ‚Äî Add an explicit "Group" tool (Bluebeam-style, no content lock) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B261** ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B246, so B261‚ÄìB264 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** A deliberate Group replaces the old implicit drag-to-bond. A persistent group = a shared **`groupId`** on ‚â•2 els/markups (additive Site-Model field; rides `els`/`markups` losslessly, no migration). It is DISTINCT from the temporary multi-selection (marquee / Shift-click; evaporates on the next click) AND from the building-host **`attachedTo`** assembly (a rigid child‚Üíhost bind with resize-refit).
- **Commands:** select ‚â•2 ‚Üí **Group** (toolbar **‚äû Group**, the element context menu's "Group selection (N)", or **Ctrl+G**) stamps a fresh `groupId`. **Ungroup** via toolbar **‚äü**, context menu, or **Ctrl+‚áßG**. **Duplicate group** (Ctrl+D on a group, or context "Duplicate group") clones every member + each member's attached children with remapped ids and a fresh shared `groupId`; a LONE paste/duplicate strips `groupId` (added to `ORPHAN_TAGS`) so a single copy starts standalone.
- **Grouping means "they stay together," nothing more** (owner clarification 2026-06-20): a single click on any member selects the WHOLE group, and move / copy / delete / arrow-nudge then act on all of them ‚Äî basically how a building + its attached features already travel together, extended to arbitrary peers (e.g. a road + an easement). A dashed enclosing box labelled "‚äû Group" marks it as one unit. **There is deliberately NO whole-group resize** ‚Äî scaling everything at once "isn't how you plan buildings" (site elements are real feet). To resize a piece, drill into it (below). (An earlier build added uniform group-resize handles; removed per the owner ‚Äî `startGroupResize`/`scaleMarkup` deleted, the box is now a pure indicator.)
- **No content lock:** double-click a member to "drill in" (`drillId`) and edit it in place (resize / retype / restyle) WITHOUT ungrouping; right-click still opens the actions menu; members keep their own properties. Grouping happens ONLY from the explicit command ‚Äî never from a plain drag or click.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b261-b264.mjs`): group two elements ‚Üí "‚äû Group" box renders with **no resize handles** ‚Üí dragging one member moves **both** (108px each) ‚Üí Ungroup removes the box ‚Üí members move independently again; **0 page errors**. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **537 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Logged **VERIFICATION V64**.
> **Dedup:** no prior open Group item. Supersedes the *bonding* half of the B114 snap/bond work (the Shift-drag‚Üí`attachedTo` bond is removed ‚Äî see **B262**). The owner-mentioned "earlier split-snap item" was the B114 family (already done), not a separate open item; the still-open **B115** (keyboard-shortcuts pass, owner-gated) listed the now-removed ‚áß-drag bond gesture ‚Äî its shortcut table is updated here.

### B262 ‚Äî Keep snap as pure alignment only (no relationship) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B262**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Removed the implicit drag-to-bond entirely: the Shift-drag ‚Üí `alignSnap` ‚Üí `attachedTo` path, the green "+" attach hint, and the bond-on-drop in `onUp` are gone, and the now-unused `alignSnap` / `flushContact` / `isAxisRect` helpers + `canAttach` / `bondTarget` / `bondRot` were deleted (net ‚àí2 lint warnings). Dragging an element now only MOVES it; with snap on, the ambient flush-snap (`edgeSnapCenter`) only ALIGNS position (grid + flush against neighbours, AutoCAD-style) and never creates a group or attachment. The building-host `attachedTo` assembly (docks / parking / sidewalks) and the explicit "Attach to‚Ä¶" command are unchanged.
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): with snap ON, dragging a building flush against a parking field then away leaves the parking untouched (Œî=0px ‚Äî no bond).
> **Dedup:** pairs with **B261** (grouping moved to the explicit Group tool); narrows **B114** (the snap toggle + Alt-bypass stay; only the bond half is removed).

### B263 ‚Äî Snap pref is silently global & sticky across sessions/projects `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20; minted **B263**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Snap was persisted in `localStorage` (`planarfit:snap`) and re-applied on every load, so it could be ON without the user enabling it this session ("I never clicked snap"). It's now a **per-SESSION** pref: it defaults **OFF** every time the app opens, is remembered only within the current browser-tab session (`sessionStorage` ‚Äî survives plan/project switches this session, resets on a fresh tab/session), and `loadSnapPref` retires the old global `localStorage` key on read. The toolbar pill makes state explicit (**"Snap off"** / **"Snap 10‚Ä≤ on"** with a green dot) and its tooltip clarifies snap only aligns position ‚Äî it never groups or bonds (so with **B262** no group/bond-type move can fire from this flag).
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): a fresh session ‚Üí button reads "Snap off" and no global `localStorage` key exists; toggling on writes `sessionStorage` only.

### B264 ‚Äî No way to delete a single plan; only "delete site + all plans" `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; minted **B264**)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eager-keller-1ueisx`).** Added a per-plan delete to the **Plan ‚ñæ** menu: each plan row carries a **‚úï** that arms an inline **"Delete '<name>'? Delete / Cancel"** confirm (no `window.confirm` ‚Äî honours the no-dialog-edits rule). The **last** plan in a site never shows a ‚úï (removing the whole site stays the map/finder's job). App-side `deletePlan` removes just that plan; if it was the plan currently open it switches to a sibling. A new `deletedSelfRef` suppresses EVERY save path for the plan being deleted (the debounced autosave, the leave/unmount `persistOrDrop`, the `beforeunload`/visibility flush, and `flushSite`) so the unmounting planner can't immediately re-write the row we just deleted.
> **Self-verified headless** (V64): a 2-plan site ‚Üí ‚úï shows the inline confirm ‚Üí Delete removes one plan (the **current** plan was deleted ‚Üí it switched to the sibling and did NOT resurrect) ‚Üí the lone remaining plan has no ‚úï; **0 page errors**.

### B246 ‚Äî Employee/non-dock side build-out: "Ôºã" adds sidewalk ‚Üí parking rows (mimics the dock stack) + restore the lost sidewalk `[Site Planner]` (bug/feature)  *(owner-reported, chat ‚Äî "still missing the option to add‚Ä¶ rows of parking. Wired to **both** the on-canvas non-dock "Ôºã/‚àí" pair (per side, with a live title: "Add a 5‚Ä≤ sidewalk" ‚Üí "Add a parking row" ‚Üí "Add another parking row") **and** the panel **Car parking** row (applies to every non-dock side). So car parking now grows unlimited rows like the dockside zones, and the sidewalk is back as the first step. (Non-dock side = the short ends, plus the long side opposite single-load docks.)
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-dock-zones.mjs`, rebased on latest `main`): on a non-dock side the 1st "Ôºã" restores the **sidewalk**, the 2nd adds the **first parking row**, the 3rd **deepens the field by another row** (27px ‚Üí 38px on screen); the panel + on-canvas dock-stack and per-zone flows all still pass; **0 page errors** (`dock-zones-parking.png`). lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **532 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Logged **VERIFICATION V55** (updated).
> **Dedup:** extends B242 (on-building controls); reuses the existing `addSidewalkSide` / `addParkingRowSide` / `growParking` so the employee side stays consistent with the row-stepping used by the Car Parking element elsewhere.

### B244 ‚Äî Resilient county parcel fetch with TxGIO statewide fallback `[Site Planner / parcels]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1" 2026-06-20; minted **B244** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B239‚ÄìB243 (Schedule stale-chunk hardening, brand icons, dock-zone fixes, PDF download) while this was in flight, so B244/B245 are the real next free IDs after B243)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/focused-darwin-8gkesb`).** When a county's own appraisal-district endpoint is down, parcel selection now degrades gracefully instead of hanging. Trigger was the 2026-06-19 FBCAD outage: `gis.fbcad.org/serverarcgis2` returned 503 then **total timeouts on every path** (layer, `/rest/services`, `/rest/info` ‚Äî the whole ArcGIS server unresponsive), so a Fort Bend click **froze the tab ~45s** with no answerer. What shipped:
- **Hard timeout (the freeze fix).** `fetchJson` in `lib/arcgis.js` now wraps every county GIS request in an **`AbortController` with an 8 s cap** (`PARCEL_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`) ‚Äî an indefinite hang becomes a prompt, typed `timeout` failure so the fallback can take over. Covers **every** parcel surface automatically (map click-select, address-search select, in-planner identify) since they all route through `fetchJson`/`queryAtPoint`.
- **Per-source circuit breaker.** New `lib/sourceHealth.js` (pure, injectable clock, **7 tests**): after **3 consecutive failures** a source's breaker **opens for a 5 min cooldown** (`recordSourceResult`/`isSourceOpen`/`sourceCooldownMs`), then auto-resumes (half-open) so a recovered server is picked back up without a reload. `filterHealthyCandidates` drops an open primary from the click's candidate list **but never the statewide source** ‚Äî so we stop re-hammering a dead host while coverage always survives. A success resets the streak (a blip never trips it). Wired into `MapFinder.handleClick` + `selectParcelAt`: candidates are health-filtered before the query and `identifyParcelDetailed`'s new per-source outcomes feed the breaker.
- **Fallback chain (primary ‚Üí TxGIO statewide).** B137 already appended the statewide TxGIO layer (`feature.geographic.texas.gov/.../stratmap_land_parcels_48_most_recent`) as a universal click candidate; this makes the chain *robust* (timeout + breaker above) and adds the **search-side** fallback: `lib/parcelQuery.js` `lookupParcels` tries the county's own CAD and, on a typed outage, retries the TxGIO layer **scoped to that one county**.
- **County-scoped statewide search.** `lib/counties.js` `statewideFallbackFor(county)` returns the TxGIO layer + `county='<NAME>'` scope (HARRIS / FORT BEND; Chambers already rides TxGIO so it has no separate backup). The shared, injection-safe `buildParcelWhere` (`parcelQuery.js`, **10 tests**, ports the B47 identifier guard) ANDs the scope **only when the layer actually has a `county` field** (self-healing for a pasted single-county URL) so an ID/address search can never match a like-named parcel in another county. Click-to-select is a point query and needs no scope.
- **Honest source labeling.** When a hit comes from the statewide layer while a real CAD existed for that spot, MapFinder now shows an amber **"Statewide backup source ‚Äî <County> county's own parcel server is unavailable; ‚Ä¶ may lag county updates"** notice (a click banner + a badge in the address-search info card). The county name is read from the parcel's own `county` attribute (`findAttr(attrs, /^county$/i)`), title-cased.
- **Field mapping / normalization.** `lib/appraisal.js` `APPR_FIELDS` extended to cover TxGIO's column names (`legal_area`/`gis_area` ‚Üí Acreage, `mkt_value` ‚Üí Total value, `stat_land_use` ‚Üí Land use, `year_built` ‚Üí Year built) so a backup parcel surfaces the **same curated rows** as one from its home county (`test/appraisal.test.js`, **6 tests**). FBCAD's *native* field names can't be captured/mapped yet ‚Äî its server is down ‚Äî so that mapping is the one explicitly-deferred sliver (the generic detectors already read TxGIO's `prop_id`/`situs_addr`/`owner_name` fine).
- **Verified ‚Äî lint 0 ¬∑ 532 tests ¬∑ build green; lazy-chunk split intact.** **Live headless run (`gis-verify/fbcad-outage-fallback-verify.mjs`):** with `gis.fbcad.org` intercepted as 503 (the real outage), a Sugar Land / Fort Bend click **selected the real TxGIO lot (prop_id 40594, county "FORT BEND") in 1.2 s** ‚Äî HCAD answered empty, FBCAD's 503 never froze the click ‚Äî and the **"Statewide backup source" notice rendered** (`gis-verify/fbcad-outage-fallback-verified.png`). Logged **VERIFICATION V61**; no owner action.
> **Dedup vs B137:** B137 made TxGIO a *queryable candidate* so a Fort Bend lot *can* be answered (coverage). B244 is the **resilience layer on top** ‚Äî the timeout that stops the hang, the breaker that stops re-hammering, the honest backup labeling, the search-side county-scoped fallback, and the TxGIO field normalization. Also distinct from **B233** (which added the "source unavailable ‚âÝ no-parcel-here" split ‚Äî B244 *feeds* that split with typed failures, see B245) and **B36e** (AbortControllers on *evidence* fetches, a different, busy-gated path). **Note (honest):** the search-side fallback lives in the canonical `runLookup` seam, which the in-planner lookup panel doesn't currently mount (the live search is the map address box, a point query that's inherently single-parcel) ‚Äî the mechanism is built + unit-tested at the seam so it's correct if/when that panel returns.

### B245 ‚Äî Validate the ArcGIS response BODY, not just the HTTP status `[Site Planner / parcels]` (bug) ‚Äî prereq for B244  *(arrived as "NEW-2" 2026-06-20; minted **B245** ‚Äî next free ID after B244)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/focused-darwin-8gkesb`).** ArcGIS routinely returns **HTTP 200 with a JSON `{error:‚Ä¶}` body** (e.g. 499 Token Required) for a failed query; the old `fetchJson` did already throw on `j.error`, but it threw a *generic* `Error`, so a caller couldn't tell a **server failure** from a healthy **"no parcel at this point."** Now `lib/arcgis.js` throws a typed **`ParcelFetchError { kind, status, unavailable:true }`** classifying every failure ‚Äî `timeout` (aborted), `http` (non-OK status), `arcgis` (200 + error body), `network` (fetch/CORS throw) ‚Äî while a **healthy empty feature list still returns `null`, never an error** (no-parcel-here is a valid answer, not a failure). `identifyParcelDetailed` already separated `responded` vs `errors` for the B233 "unavailable vs none" card; it now also returns **per-source outcomes** (`sources:[{county, ok, hit, error}]`) so the B244 circuit breaker can mark exactly which source failed. `humanizeError` gives each `kind` its own plain wording. This is the prereq that makes B244's fallback trigger reliably (a 200-with-error-body now *counts* as a failure, not a masked success). **Tests:** `test/arcgis.test.js` extended (+7: empty‚Üínull, 200+error‚Üí`arcgis`/499, 503‚Üí`http`, network‚Üí`network`, the timeout-abort path via fake timers, per-source split, humanized wording). lint 0 ¬∑ 532 tests ¬∑ build green.
> **Dedup:** extends **B233** (typed "couldn't reach any service" vs "no parcel here") from the address-search card down into the fetch layer, and reuses the same body-parse principle the layer **`probeService`** (`lib/layers.js`) already applies (HTTP 200 + `.error` = failed) ‚Äî now applied to the parcel **query** path and surfaced as a typed error. Folded into the B244 ship (one branch); kept as its own item because it's the reusable classification primitive every parcel surface now leans on.

### B243 ‚Äî Replace browser print with a Planyr-composed PDF download (no print dialog, white background, exact page size) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B228, renumbered **B243** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B228‚ÄìB242 (dock-zone stack, DWG service, map-finder search, brand icons, ‚Ä¶) while this was in flight, so B243 is the real next free ID after B242)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/eloquent-mendel-jioa4q`).** Owner reported (3 screenshots) that **Print** opened a blank `about:blank` window and the output carried a browser date/time header (top-left), an `about:blank` URL (bottom-left), a `1/1` page number (bottom-right), a cream page background, and Letter-sized content floating in a corner of a Tabloid sheet. **Inspected first (as asked):** the path ALREADY did the hard part ‚Äî `printPDF` composed the WHOLE sheet (title block + plan + B197 buildings table + metrics) as ONE SVG at the exact declared page size (B200) ‚Äî and the ONLY defect was the final DELIVERY: `window.open("","_blank")` + `win.print()` handed that sheet to the **browser's** print dialog, which injects the header / `about:blank` / page number (none strippable by CSS or code), and the cream was `PAL.paper` (`#f4f1ea`, the on-screen page colour) bleeding into the sheet fill **and** the plan-clone background rect.
- **Fix = keep the composition, replace the delivery with a real PDF we build ourselves.** New pure, dependency-free writer `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/imagePdf.js` (`jpegToPdf`): assembles a one-page PDF (catalog ‚Üí pages ‚Üí page ‚Üí image XObject ‚Üí content stream ‚Üí Info) at an **exact physical size** (`MediaBox = inches √ó 72 pt`), embeds the page raster with `/DCTDecode` (the JPEG bytes verbatim, no re-encode), with a **byte-accurate xref** and binary-safe assembly (builds a `Uint8Array`; the JPEG never passes through a UTF-16 JS string). No jsPDF/pdf-lib ‚Äî zero bundle weight, matching the `printSheet.js` pure-lib pattern; unit-tested in `test/imagePdf.test.js` (10 tests: xref offsets land on each object, MediaBox in points, DCTDecode dims, paren/backslash title escaping, bad-input guards).
- **`printPDF` ‚Üí `exportPDF`** in `SitePlanner.jsx`: the old `window.open`/`win.print()` machinery is **gone**. It now forces **white** paper (new `paper` arg to `buildExportSvg` for the plan-clone bg + `pal:{‚Ä¶PAL,paper:'#ffffff'}` for the sheet ‚Äî the two cream sources), inlines the aerial with `dropOnFail=true` so a CORS-blocked image can't taint the canvas (the vector plan still exports), rasterizes the composed sheet at **300 DPI** (`PDF_DPI`, capped by `PDF_MAX_PX = 22M` px ‚Äî Tabloid@300 ‚âà 16.8M, under the cap), fills the canvas white first (JPEG has no alpha), JPEG-encodes at q0.92, wraps with `jpegToPdf`, and **downloads** `"<date> <project> - <plan>.pdf"` (B201 naming). Generating the PDF ourselves is the mechanism that removes the injected chrome; the declared page size kills the Letter-on-Tabloid float. Raster (vs a vector SVG‚ÜíPDF converter) is deliberate: the plan uses `feDropShadow` filters, which the browser renders faithfully into the raster but most SVG‚ÜíPDF converters drop ‚Äî full WYSIWYG fidelity over crisp-vector-text, and 300 DPI keeps text crisp for print anyway.
- **UI:** File ‚ñæ item ‚Üí **"Download PDF / pick frame‚Ä¶"**; the print-frame toolbar action ‚Üí **"Download PDF"** (+ tooltip); a **"Preparing PDF‚Ä¶"** pill (new `exportingPDF` state + a `spin` keyframe in `index.css`) replaces the old blank "Preparing print‚Ä¶" window. The two `exportPNG` alerts that said "use Print to PDF" now say "Download PDF". Paper/orientation (Letter/Tabloid √ó landscape/portrait) and the **B131** overlay toggle are unchanged.
> **Self-verified headless** (**V60**, logged-out, against the built `dist/`): **(1)** real app ‚Äî `ui-audit/verify-pdf-download.mjs` drove File ‚ñæ ‚Üí Download PDF / pick frame‚Ä¶ ‚Üí Download PDF and captured the ACTUAL file: `2026.06.20 Mesa Logistics - Plan 1.pdf`, a valid `%PDF`, **numPages 1**, page **exactly 792√ó612 pt**, **ZERO pop-up windows**, **0** errors. **(2)** pipeline ‚Äî `ui-audit/verify-pdf-export.mjs` ran the exact raster‚ÜíJPEG‚Üí`jpegToPdf` path for Letter (792√ó612) and Tabloid (1224√ó792), each a valid 1-page PDF that paints an image; all four paper corners white, **no cream field** (‚â§1 stray warm pixel = JPEG chroma-edge artifact), the **building drop-shadow + aerial `<image>` survive** the raster, table/metrics crisp at 300 DPI (`live-download-page.jpg`, `pdf-export-letter.jpg`). lint **0** ¬∑ **496 tests** ¬∑ build green (re-verified after merging the latest `main`); existing `verify-print-live.mjs` still passes with the renamed menu item; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** NO existing open item covered this. **B131** (overlay-in-print toggle ‚Äî done) is PRESERVED (the `printOverlay` checkbox still gates the placed overlay in the export). **B50** (export/print robustness) is partly SUPERSEDED for the print path: its "don't strand a blank Preparing‚Ä¶ window on a serialization throw" guard is moot now that there's no window; PNG export keeps its own try/catch + alerts, untouched. **B159/B160** are the *Scheduler* Gantt PDF/Print export (a different module/app), not this Site Planner path. The single-SVG sheet composition (**B200**) + buildings table (**B197**) + filename (**B201**) are reused unchanged ‚Äî only the final delivery step changed.

### B239 ‚Äî Schedule module still dead-ends after a deploy: harden stale-chunk recovery (cache-busting reload + chunk-aware ErrorBoundary) `[App Shell / Deploy]` (bug) ‚Äî follow-up to B221  *(owner-reported 2026-06-20, chat: "my scheduling module not working‚Ä¶ this is obviously a huge deal"; minted B228, renumbered **B239** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B228‚ÄìB238 (dock-zone stack, Bluebeam vertex editing, map-finder batch, two-backend doc note) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B238)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/optimistic-brahmagupta-ubw407`).** The owner still hit the Sequence/Schedule module on the workspace error screen with `Failed to fetch dynamically imported module: ‚Ä¶/Scheduler-<hash>.js` **even though B221 had shipped** the stale-chunk auto-reload. **Confirmed the module itself is NOT broken** (headless `ui-audit/diagnose-scheduler.mjs` scenario A: the embedded Gantt renders **44 task rows** the moment its chunk loads ‚Äî the earlier "blank iframe" reading was just measured before the in-browser Babel transpile of the ~692 KB `/sequence/` doc finished). The residual failure was two gaps in B221's *recovery path*, both fixed here:
- **The recovery reload wasn't guaranteed-fresh.** B221's auto-reload (and the boundary's manual reload) used a plain `location.reload()`, which the browser can satisfy from its OWN cached copy of the stale `index.html` ‚Äî so the reload lands right back on the previous build's deleted chunk ‚Üí second `vite:preloadError` ‚Üí cooldown ‚Üí dead-end. The no-cache `public/_headers` can't retro-fix an `index.html` a long-lived/returning tab already hard-cached. **Fix:** new `reloadFresh()` in `src/app/chunkReload.js` navigates to the same path with a throwaway `?_r=<ts>` query ‚Äî a **distinct cache key** the browser MUST fetch from the server ‚Äî via `location.replace` (no back-button trap), so it always pulls a fresh `index.html` and the current chunk names; `stripReloadParam()` tidies the param off the address bar on the recovered load (called at guard install). The `vite:preloadError` guard now calls `reloadFresh` (loop-guard/cooldown unchanged).
- **The ErrorBoundary's PRIMARY button was a no-op for this error.** "Try again" just `reset()`s ‚Üí re-renders the same lazy import ‚Üí re-requests the same dead chunk ‚Üí fails identically (the dead-end the owner kept hitting). **Fix:** `ErrorBoundary.jsx` is now chunk-aware via a shared `isChunkLoadError()` (matches the dynamic-import failure phrasings across Chrome/Firefox/Safari + the SPA-fallback "expected JS, got text/html" MIME error). For a chunk error it reframes the screen as **"A new version of Planyr is ready"** with a single PRIMARY **"Reload to update"** (cache-busting) button ‚Äî your work is saved. Genuine render crashes keep the Try again / Reload page pair (both reloads now cache-busting too).
- **`public/_headers` unchanged** ‚Äî already correct from B221 (no-cache HTML, immutable hashed `/assets/*`); it's the *forward* guarantee, while `reloadFresh` is the *escape hatch* for tabs that cached the old HTML before it took effect.
- **Verified:** lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **443 tests** (`test/chunkReload.test.js` 4‚Üí11: `isChunkLoadError` cross-browser matrix, `reloadFresh` cache-key/replace, `stripReloadParam`) ¬∑ build green; `dist/_headers` still lands at the deploy root and all three lazy chunks emit hashed under `/assets/`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/diagnose-scheduler.mjs` + `ui-audit/verify-chunk-reload.mjs`, **all green** on the built bundle via `vite preview`): **(A)** a normal Schedule click mounts the iframe and renders 44 task rows; **(B)** a chunk that 404s once then recovers ‚Üí the guard cache-busting-reloads and lands in the module; **(C)** a permanently-missing chunk surfaces the **"A new version of Planyr is ready"** screen (no reload loop), and clicking **"Reload to update"** performs a real cache-busting reload ‚Äî captured nav trail `"/" ‚Üí "/?_r=<ts>" ‚Üí "/"` (the param added, then stripped). `verify-chunk-reload.mjs` still **3/3** (reload-once, cooldown holds, re-arms).
> **Owner note:** nothing to configure ‚Äî the fix ships with the next deploy. Because `reloadFresh` cache-busts, even a browser still holding the *old* `index.html` escapes on the first recovery instead of dead-ending. Logged **VERIFICATION V58**.
> **Dedup:** a hardening of **B221** (same stale-chunk-after-deploy family ‚Äî NOT a new bug class, and explicitly NOT a Scheduler/iframe logic bug, which was ruled out by the 44-row render). Distinct from the render-crash path the ErrorBoundary already handled (B205-era). No change to the lazy-chunk split or the iframe app.

### B238 ‚Äî Scaffold the DWG‚ÜíDXF conversion service in /server (LibreDWG primary, APS fallback dormant) `[server]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B228, renumbered **B238** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B227‚ÄìB236 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B237)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/kind-johnson-oqzqco`).** Stood up the conversion **compute** service as a new `server/convert/` workspace alongside the existing /server storage/oauth scaffold ‚Äî a tiny, dependency-free Node HTTP service that turns a **DWG** into a **DXF**, targeting **Google Cloud Run** (scale-to-zero). Endpoints: `POST /convert` (body = DWG bytes ‚Üí DXF bytes, `X-Convert-Engine` header) and `GET /health`. Engine policy (`convertService.js`): **LibreDWG primary** (`libredwg.js` ‚Äî spawns `dwg2dxf`, treats LibreDWG's error *bitmask* correctly: a non-empty DXF + non-critical code is success-with-warning, a critical code or no output is failure) ‚Üí **Autodesk APS Model Derivative fallback** (`aps.js`) only when **`APS_ENABLED`** is on. **APS is DORMANT by default** (account not provisioned): real 2-legged auth is implemented + the full Model-Derivative pipeline is documented inline as a provisioning fill-in, but every dormant/unconfigured path returns a clear `{ok:false}` ‚Äî never a throw, never a false success. **When LibreDWG fails and APS is off, the HTTP layer returns an explicit error (422), never a 200 with a junk body** ‚Äî the same no-silent-failure contract as the storage adapter (it **reuses `server/storage/result.js`**, no parallel result type). Status map: 200 (DXF) ¬∑ 400 (no/empty body) ¬∑ 413 (over `MAX_UPLOAD_BYTES`) ¬∑ 422 (unreadable drawing) ¬∑ 503 (engine binary missing). All config via **server-side env only** (`config.js`: `PORT`, `LIBREDWG_BIN`, `CONVERT_TIMEOUT_MS`, `MAX_UPLOAD_BYTES`, `APS_ENABLED`, `APS_CLIENT_ID/SECRET`) ‚Äî never a `VITE_` var, never committed. **Dockerfile** is a production-correct multi-stage build: stage 1 compiles **LibreDWG 0.13.4 from source** (it isn't in the Debian/Ubuntu repos), static-linked so stage 2 (`node:22-bookworm-slim`, non-root `node` user) carries just the ~MB `dwg2dxf` binary; no npm install (Node built-ins only).
> **Verified this session ‚Äî built the image and ran the container for real.** `GET /health` ‚Üí 200 `{ok,service:"dwg-convert",engine:"libredwg",apsFallback:false}`. `POST /convert` with two **real** sample drawings: **example_2000.dwg** (582 KB) ‚Üí **200**, a valid `AutoCAD Drawing Exchange Format, version 2000` DXF (1.27 MB), `X-Convert-Engine: libredwg`; **example_2013.dwg** ‚Üí **200**, valid DXF. **Failure path (the important one):** garbage (non-DWG) bytes with APS off ‚Üí **422** `{"ok":false,"error":"DWG‚ÜíDXF conversion failed in LibreDWG and the APS fallback is disabled (APS_ENABLED is off): ‚Ä¶"}` ‚Äî explicit, never a silent success; empty body ‚Üí **400**; `GET /convert` ‚Üí **405**. **+26 unit tests** (`test/dwgConvert.test.js`: config/APS-dormant parsing, LibreDWG success/warning/critical/spawn-fail/no-output, the engine-policy matrix incl. "APS never consulted when off", APS guard + auth shape, and the live HTTP server's status codes). lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **462 tests** ¬∑ `vite build` green; **isolation confirmed ‚Äî `grep` of `dist/` finds zero conversion-service code** (the public bundle never imports `/server`).
> **Follow-on (NOT this item):** actual `gcloud run deploy` waits on the GCP project being provisioned in the Google Cloud Console; the service + Dockerfile are proven locally now. The Dockerfile's `CURL_INSECURE` build-arg exists ONLY to build behind this repo's sandbox TLS-inspecting proxy (CLAUDE.md); production/Cloud Build omits it ‚Üí full TLS verification.
> **Dedup / inspect-first:** checked before writing ‚Äî `/server` already held the B206‚ÄìB209 Drive storage adapter + the B207 Google OAuth helper, so this is **additive** (`server/convert/` only); no existing /server code changed. The browser/Supabase side calls this over the network in the backend tranche (distinct from the Supabase user-data backend).

### B237 ‚Äî Record the two-backend architecture in CLAUDE.md `[infra]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B227, renumbered **B237** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B227‚ÄìB236 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B236)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/kind-johnson-oqzqco`).** Reconciled the existing **"Two backends ‚Äî don't conflate"** section of `CLAUDE.md` **in place** (no duplicate section) so the data layer and the compute layer can never be confused: **(1) Supabase ‚Äî the data/auth/storage layer (BUILT):** cloud Postgres, email/password auth, RLS, cloud save/load; the frontend talks to it **directly with the anon key**, which is safe in the browser **because RLS protects it** (a request only ever sees the signed-in user's own rows); the permanent home for user data. **(2) `/server` on Google Cloud Run ‚Äî the compute layer (built in-repo, not yet deployed):** scale-to-zero containers running **DWG‚ÜíDXF conversion** (LibreDWG primary ‚Üí APS Model Derivative fallback, dormant behind `APS_ENABLED`) and **Google Drive auto-filing + bytes I/O** (the file-facts index itself lives in Supabase Postgres; the one-time OAuth *consent* callback is a thin same-origin Cloudflare Pages Function, the heavy compute is Cloud Run). Documented that **all third-party secrets (APS key, Google credentials, Supabase service-role key) stay server-side only, walled off from the public Cloudflare Pages deploy**; the only Supabase key that reaches the frontend is the RLS-protected **anon** key. The two layers talk **over the network** ‚Äî Supabase the permanent data home, `/server` additive compute added in the backend tranche.
> **Also fixed a stale contradiction** surfaced while reconciling: the Workflow section still said *"Deploy = GitHub Pages (production)"* and *"Cloudflare Pages is optional and deferred"* ‚Äî both false since the Pages-pipeline retirement (already recorded as DONE near the end of CLAUDE.md). Updated to **Cloudflare Pages = production (planyr.io)**, with per-branch previews noted as the separate optional Cloudflare concern, so the doc no longer contradicts itself about where the public deploy (the thing `/server` is walled off from) actually lives.
> **Dedup:** the section already existed ‚Äî this **enriched it in place** (Cloud Run / scale-to-zero / LibreDWG‚ÜíAPS detail + the Cloudflare-Pages walling), it did not add a second copy. Doc-only change: lint 0 ¬∑ 462 tests ¬∑ build green (unaffected).

### B236 ‚Äî Per-layer GIS data-age / source-vintage stamp `[Site Planner / GIS]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; minted **B236** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B225‚ÄìB231 while this was in flight, so B232‚ÄìB236 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/tender-goldberg-ax4n5w`).** Each GIS layer now shows a low-visual-weight **"as of: &lt;source vintage&gt;"** line in `components/LayerPanel.jsx` (rendered when the layer is on), kept **deliberately distinct** from the existing **"refreshed Xm ago"** cache-age stamp by the layer name ‚Äî the two are never conflated. The vintage is the source's **own** effective/publication date or maintenance cadence, from a curated, central `LAYER_VINTAGE` map + `layerVintage(id, cfg)` in `lib/layers.js` (a per-config `vintage` override wins; else the map; else `null`). **Honest by rule:** per-panel / per-area datasets say what actually varies ("Effective date varies by FIRM panel", "Survey date varies by NWI project area", "LiDAR collection varies by county (USGS 3DEP)"); continuously-maintained registries say "continuously updated / current edition"; **any layer with no entry renders "vintage unknown" (italic) ‚Äî never a fabricated date** (same family as "source unavailable ‚âÝ not present"). **Scope:** source-vintage only; the "last refreshed" half rides the planned GIS-cache SWR work and is NOT built here.
> **Dedup:** the **standalone, ship-now** version of the data-age surfacing already specced inside **B96** (GIS layer cache, stale-while-revalidate) ‚Äî when caching lands, fold the vintage stamp + the refreshed-age stamp into one surface rather than duplicating. **Self-verified headless** (**V57**, `ui-audit/verify-b232-b236.mjs`): toggling FEMA on shows "as of: Effective date varies by FIRM panel". lint 0 ¬∑ 448 tests ¬∑ build green; lazy chunk split intact.
