### B232 ‚Äî Address search doesn't recenter the map on "Go" `[Site Planner / map]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B232** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (PRs #188/#189/#190/#191) took B225‚ÄìB231 (building feature-buttons / Yield donut / dock-zone stack / Bluebeam vertex editing) while this was in flight, so B232‚ÄìB236 are the real next free IDs)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/tender-goldberg-ax4n5w`).** Confirmed the impl note first: the geocode handler (`goAddress` in MapFinder.jsx) **already** flew the camera, so the bug was the **geocoder itself**, not unwired plumbing. The old code called OSM Nominatim with only `countrycodes=us` and **no viewport bias**, which routinely returns nothing for a bare house-number street address ("19630 Crossbranch") ‚Äî so the map silently stayed put. Replaced with `geocodeAddress(q, center)`: tries the **Esri World Geocoding Service** `findAddressCandidates` first (keyless single lookup, the same ArcGIS family the app already uses for imagery/parcels, far better at exact US street addresses) **biased to the current map center** via `&location=`; falls back to **Nominatim biased to a ~0.6¬∞ viewbox** around the center. On a hit, `flyTo([lat,lon], 18)` ‚Äî parcel-level zoom. Failure stays honest (the "couldn't find that address" toast).
> **Dedup / scope:** a separate failure path from B233 ‚Äî this is the **geocode‚Üícamera** half; B233 is the parcel identify/select/info half. **Self-verified headless** (**V57**): "19630 Crossbranch Dr, Katy, TX" ‚Üí Go recenters the map on the parcel (not a no-op).

### B230 ‚Äî Replace always-visible "+" midpoint handles with Shift-click / right-click vertex insertion (Bluebeam-style) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B221, renumbered **B230** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (PRs #184/#186/#188/#189/#191) took B221‚ÄìB229 (lazy-chunk recovery, Schedule fixes, building-button gating, Yield-panel redesign, dock-zone stack) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B229; the implementing commit + the PR still say "B221")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/funny-franklin-hrk815`).** The permanent "+" midpoint handle that every editable edge used to carry is **gone in every state** (selected, moving, all of them); editing now follows the Bluebeam model. Built **once in a shared vertex-editing layer** so all editable geometry inherits it ‚Äî **detention ponds, parcels, polygon elements, measurement polygons/lines, markup poly/line, and easement paths** ‚Äî not per element type.
- **Shared core (new):** `editablePath()` resolves the current selection to a uniform `{ layer, id, pts, closed, min }`; `hitEditPath()` returns the nearest vertex / nearest edge within a **screen-pixel** tolerance (9px vert / 11px edge ‚Üí zoom-independent grab radius); `insertVtx()` and `deleteVtx()` are single dispatchers keyed by `layer` (parcel/el/measure/markup/ease), each using functional `setState` so they always act on current state. Wired through **three capture-phase handlers** on the canvas `<svg>` (`onPointerDownCapture` / `onContextMenuCapture` / `onPointerMoveCapture`) so the same interaction reaches every layer **before** its own handlers, **without overlaying any new hit target** ‚Äî a normal click/drag/select is untouched.
- **Add a vertex:** **Shift+click an edge** (away from a corner) drops a control point exactly at the click point on that segment; **right-click an edge** ‚Üí portal "Add control point". **Delete a vertex:** **right-click a vertex** ‚Üí portal "Delete control point"; **Delete/Backspace** removes the active control point. Deletion is blocked below the geometry minimum (**3 for a polygon**), and the menu item reads "(min reached)" + disables there.
- **Discoverability:** a faint **candidate-insertion dot** snaps to the nearest point on the edge under the cursor on **edge-hover during edit**, and brightens while **Shift** arms the insert ‚Äî replacing exactly what the permanent "+" advertised, without the clutter. The **active control point** (the Delete target) renders inverted.
- **Kept:** the square corner handles (the real vertices) ‚Äî shown only when selected, drag behavior unchanged. The five `add*Vertex` "+" handlers and the per-handle Shift-click-delete branches were removed (superseded). **Tie-break rule:** a **corner always wins over its adjacent edges** (`hitEditPath` returns both at a corner; a vertex right-click deletes, never adds), mirroring the insert rule `edge && !vertex` ‚Äî this was the one real bug found in headless testing and fixed before merge.
- **Portal menu:** the Add/Delete-control-point menu is `createPortal`-mounted at `document.body` (z 6000/6001) so it can never be clipped or trapped behind the canvas / tool-rail stacking contexts; it reuses the app's existing `menu`/`menuPanel`/`menuItem` styling.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b221-b222.mjs`, logged-out, live Harris aerial, a polygon detention pond in a parcel): after selecting the pond ‚Äî **0** "+" midpoint handles, **4** square vertex handles; **Shift+click an edge ‚Üí 4‚Üí5** vertices with the candidate dot shown while Shift held; **edge-hover (no shift) shows the dot**; **right-click a vertex ‚Üí portal "Delete control point" ‚Üí 5‚Üí4**; **Delete key ‚Üí 4‚Üí3**; repeated deletes **stop at 3** (polygon min guard). **0 console errors.** Screenshots `ui-audit/screens/b221-pond-selected.png` + `b221-after-edits.png` eyeballed (squares only, no plus marks). Logged **VERIFICATION V56**. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **436 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** AMENDS the now-done Bluebeam-editing items **B141** (editable vertices on the measurement tools) + **B147** (markup/shape vertex-edit for lines/polylines/polygons), which had introduced the "+" midpoint handle, and addresses the clutter **B215** flagged (the "+" stacking at the edge midpoint). Distinct from the open **B155/B156** (whole-shape interior hit-testing + hover highlight) ‚Äî those select/hover a shape; this inserts/deletes control points on the already-selected shape.

### B231 ‚Äî Restyle the detention pond to a modern "Cartographic" water-body treatment `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B222, renumbered **B231** ‚Äî next free ID after B230; concurrent `main` took B221‚ÄìB229; the implementing commit + the PR still say "B222")*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/funny-franklin-hrk815`).** The detention pond no longer reads as dated clip-art. The decorative wavy-line water hatch, the saturated outline (which read as the Markup-accent orange ‚Äî the wrong signal for water), and the monospace label are all replaced with a modern cartographic water-body style (how Mapbox / ArcGIS Pro render water). Implemented as a **named, reusable style token** so future water/basin features inherit it; **scoped to the pond element type** (never auto-applied to other polygons).
- **Token (`lib/planStyle.js`):** the pond `TYPE` is now `{ fill:"#5B97A5", stroke:"#2C5D6B", weight:2, cartoWater:true }` (replaced the old `water:true` wavy-hatch flag); `elStyle` exposes `cartoWater`. One token, reusable.
- **Fill (`renderElPx`):** a **radial steel-teal gradient** `#grad-water` (added to `<defs>`) that **deepens toward the center** ‚Äî `#2F6675` at the middle ‚Üí `#5B97A5` at the edge ‚Äî at ~80% opacity, so a pond reads as water *with volume*, not a flat cutout. The old `pat-water` wavy pattern is deleted. Applies to both the polygon and rectangular pond branches.
- **Outline:** `#2C5D6B`, **2px at a constant screen-pixel width** (the canvas is drawn in pixel space, so the stroke never hairlines when zoomed out nor fattens when zoomed in); **3px when selected**. **No orange anywhere on the water body** ‚Äî selection is signaled by the thicker teal stroke + the (transient, orange) editing handles, not a colour change on the feature itself.
- **Label:** switched monospace ‚Üí **Inter** (the app's proportional UI sans), **dark slate `#0E2E36` with a white casing/halo** (always, so it stays legible over busy aerial), two lines kept ‚Äî name above ("Detention Pond" / "Existing Detention Pond"), area sub-line below ("0.47 ac ¬∑ 20,272 sf") ‚Äî centered on the centroid (or the existing baseline anchor in expansion mode). Threaded through the shared LOD/label renderer via a per-candidate `carto` flag, so **only the pond label changes**; every other element label stays mono.
- **Map overview:** `MapFinder.jsx` resolves element fills through the same `elStyle`, so the map's pond pins inherit the flat steel-teal fill + teal outline automatically (no wavy, no orange) ‚Äî no second code path; the expansion baseline ghost stroke was recoloured to match.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b221-b222.mjs`): `#grad-water` exists with stops **`#2F6675` ‚Üí `#5B97A5`**; **no `#pat-water`**; the pond fill uses `url(#grad-water)`; the **`#2C5D6B`** outline is present; the label uses **Inter** + fill **`#0E2E36`** reading "Detention Pond / 2.14 ac ¬∑ 93,100 sf". Screenshot `ui-audit/screens/b221-pond-selected.png` eyeballed ‚Äî steel-teal body with a deeper center, crisp teal edge, haloed sans label, no hatch, no orange. **0 console errors.** lint 0 ¬∑ 414 tests ¬∑ build green.
> **Dedup:** AMENDS the pond rendering from **B132/B139** (expansion baseline + ghost) and **B140/B157** (on-map pond area labels ‚Äî the two-line name+area is preserved). Distinct from **B219** (cartographic restyle of the map *furniture* ‚Äî north arrow + scale bar); this is the *water body* itself.

### B239 ‚Äî Restore the per-zone "Ôºã" to add trailer parking / buffer from the selected court (regression from B228/B229) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(owner-reported, angry ‚Äî "I literally can't add the 50 foot trailer parking anymore. ### B229 ‚Äî Dock Features panel: add-controls on top, stacked zone list `[Site Planner / UI]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B222, renumbered **B229** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B221‚ÄìB227 while this was in flight, so B228/B229 are the real next free IDs)*

Truck court ‚Üí 2. Trailer parking ‚Üí 3. Buffer), each row an **inline editable depth field** + the **LIFO "‚àí"** (active only on the outermost row). The shared **footprint / bump-out total / dock-doors summary stays at the bottom.** A selected court/trailer/buffer shows a focused "Dock zone" depth editor (length + rotation are stack-controlled). The right-click building menu mirrors the same add-next / remove-outer actions.

### B226 ‚Äî Show feature-edit buttons only on the selected/hovered building `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B226** ‚Äî next free ID after B225)*

Net rule: **buttons visible iff (footprint large enough on screen) AND (building selected OR hovered).** **Hover** (`SitePlanner.jsx`: new `hoverElId` state + a block in `onMove`) is computed **position-based** (the topmost building whose footprint bbox contains the cursor), NOT via SVG `onPointerEnter/Leave` ‚Äî because the buttons sit INSIDE the footprint, an enter/leave trigger would flicker the buttons off the instant the cursor moved toward one; the position test keeps the hover alive. It only runs while idle in select mode with **nothing selected** (selection otherwise drives the buttons), so there's no per-frame churn once you've clicked. Hover previews the add-buttons only ‚Äî resize/rotate grips stay selection-only.

### B225 ‚Äî Hide building feature-edit buttons when the on-screen footprint is too small (anti-cluster) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B225** ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B220, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/lucid-heisenberg-mjhpw3`).** Zooming OUT on a building with feature-add buttons shrank its footprint while the fixed-pixel +/‚àí buttons (truck-dock / sidewalk / bump-out / parking-row ‚Äî each inset ~22px inside a wall, r=9) stayed full size, so the cluster grew larger than the footprint and spilled past the edges into an unreadable pile (the owner's screenshot). **Fix (`SitePlanner.jsx`):** each feature-add button is now gated on the building's RENDERED on-screen footprint size in PIXELS (`el.w/el.h * view.ppf`) against a tunable module const `FEAT_BTN_MIN_PX = 72` (‚âà the ~22px inset + 9px radius clearance on each side, plus a small legibility margin ‚Äî opposite buttons overlap below ~68px). The gate is **per-axis**: a wall's inset +/‚àí needs its PERPENDICULAR on-screen dimension ‚â• 72px (top/bottom gated on height-px, left/right on width-px); the corner bump-outs need BOTH axes. So a long/narrow on-screen footprint keeps its long-side buttons and drops only the cramped short-end ones ‚Äî the overlap case the arriving note flagged ("also check") is handled inherently, no collapse-menu needed ‚Äî and a fully-small footprint drops ALL of them (no spill). Applied to all three feature-add node groups (`sideAddNodes`, `courtAddNodes`, `parkingAddNodes`). **Resize/rotate grips are intentionally NOT gated** (still usable on a small building ‚Äî the spec says "only the editable feature buttons are suppressed"); the map's **Building Pin + Progress Arc live in `MapFinder.jsx`** (a different component) and are **untouched**, so they stay visible at every zoom level, as required.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-b225-b226.mjs`, logged-out, 400‚Ä≤√ó300‚Ä≤ cross-dock building): swept the wheel zoom from large to tiny; at every non-ambiguous step the drawn button count matched the rule predicted from the measured footprint px ‚Äî **8** while large (494√ó370 ‚Ä¶ 127√ó95px), **2** (long-side sidewalks only) at **81√ó60px** (height < 72 ‚â§ width ‚Üí per-axis collision handling), **0** once tiny (‚â§ 64√ó48px). Screens `b225-zoomed-in.png` / `b225-partial-longside.png` / `b225-zoomed-out.png`. Logged **VERIFICATION V53**. lint 0 ¬∑ 414 tests ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Dedup:** distinct from **B149** (LOD tiering ‚Äî which *dimensions/labels* draw at a given zoom) and **B121** (label-overlap engine) ‚Äî those govern annotations; this governs the *interactive edit handles*. Combined with **B226** into ONE visibility rule (size-gate AND selected-or-hovered). Reuses the **B30** precedent of pixel-projected (not feet-based) thresholds.

### B222 ‚Äî Row color fill hides Gantt bars `[Scheduler]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B218, renumbered **B222** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#183, #185, #187) took B218‚ÄìB221)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/awesome-pascal-zlb19p`).** Applying a row color fill made the task bars on that row disappear from the Gantt. **Root cause was a color collision (b):** in `GanttView` (`public/sequence/index.html`), `task.rowColor` was overloaded ‚Äî the same field that paints the row background (`rowBg`) was also the bar fill via `task.rowColor || <neutral>` for **leaf bars, summary brackets, AND milestone diamonds** ‚Äî so a fill repainted every on-row datum its own color and it vanished into its own background. **Fix:** each datum now keeps its **own identity hue independent of the row fill** ‚Äî leaf bars + milestone diamonds = neutral gray `#94a3b8`, summary brackets = depth-navy ‚Äî and carries a **hairline edge** (`#475569`, a slate darker than the fill) so it stays legible on any fill; notably the **solid/complete leaf bar gained a 1px border** (it was borderless and was the one that fully disappeared on a matching fill). The row fill is now pure background decoration. **Paint order verified + documented** (z-index): row fill (row `<div>`, z auto, bottom) ‚Üí grid/today/dependency lines (z2‚Äì4) ‚Üí bars/milestones (z5, data layer) ‚Üí bar + name labels (z6‚Äì7, top). Holistic: covers bars, diamonds, links, and labels.
> **Self-verified headless** (**V51**, `ui-audit/verify-rowfill-bars.mjs`, logged-out seed): with a leaf task seeded a row fill, the fill paints the row bands (`rowBands:2`) with **zero bar-sized collisions** (`barCollisions:0`); the bar keeps `#94a3b8` + the `#475569` 1px edge (`rowfill-bars-crop.png` shows the marker clearly on the tinted row). **Dedup:** distinct from B210‚ÄìB212 (the prior Gantt tranche ‚Äî brackets / status-as-fill / columns). The PDF/Print export path (`buildGanttSVG`) already paints bars neutral gray/navy and never reads `rowColor` for bars ‚Äî no collision there, left untouched. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **419 tests** ¬∑ build green; lazy chunk split intact.

### B221 ‚Äî Lazy workspaces fail to load after a deploy: "Failed to fetch dynamically imported module" (stale content-hashed chunk) `[App Shell / Deploy]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B218, renumbered **B221** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (PR #183) took B218 (dead header controls) + B219 (map-furniture restyle) and a parallel session took B220 (map-finder over-zoom) while this was in flight, so B221 is the real next free ID after B220. The branch's first commit + the PR were opened as "B218". Deduped against the PDF.js `import()` items (B72/B67/B180 lazy-load a heavy library on first use ‚Äî unrelated to the stale-chunk-after-deploy failure here).)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/cool-ptolemy-2lb1js`).** Root cause confirmed as the standard Vite stale-chunk-after-deploy problem (NOT a logic bug inside DocReview, and NOT a broken/partial build ‚Äî the build is green and all three workspace chunks emit cleanly under `/assets/`): an already-open tab is holding the *previous* deploy's `index.html`, which references content-hashed filenames like `/assets/DocReview-<oldhash>.js`; once Cloudflare serves the new build those files are gone, so switching into a not-yet-loaded workspace 404s and throws the user onto the workspace error screen. A hard reload fixes it because it re-fetches the current `index.html` (and its new hashes). Fix, applied globally so it covers **every** lazy route (Site Planner, Document Review, Sequence), not just DocReview:
- **Auto-reload-once on dynamic-import failure** ‚Äî `src/app/chunkReload.js` (`installChunkReloadGuard`, wired in `src/main.jsx` before render) listens for Vite's `vite:preloadError` window event and reloads the page once. **Loop guard:** the time of the last auto-reload is stamped in `sessionStorage` (`planyr:chunkReloadAt`); a second preloadError within a 10 s cooldown does **not** reload ‚Äî a genuinely-missing chunk (a broken/partial deploy) falls through to the existing `ErrorBoundary` instead of reload-looping. The stamp self-expires so a *later, separate* deploy re-arms a fresh one-time recovery ‚Äî deliberately more robust than a boolean flag cleared on mount, which would either race the reload (auto-loop if the default workspace's chunk is the missing one) or reload on every click of a truly-broken module (never letting its error show). The pure decision (`shouldReloadAfterPreloadError`) is unit-tested.
- **Cloudflare cache headers** ‚Äî `public/_headers` (copied verbatim to `dist/_headers` at the deploy root): `/assets/*` (the content-hashed, immutable build files) get `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`; the HTML entry points (`/`, `/index.html`, `/sequence/`) get `Cache-Control: no-cache` so a new deploy's asset hashes propagate on the next load instead of being pinned behind a hard-cached HTML.
- **Verified:** lint 0 errors ¬∑ **418 tests** (incl. the new `test/chunkReload.test.js`, 4) ¬∑ build green; `dist/_headers` lands at the deploy root and the three lazy chunks (`DocReview-*`, `Scheduler-*`, `SitePlannerApp-*`) emit hashed under `/assets/`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-chunk-reload.mjs`, **3/3** against the built bundle on `vite preview`): a first `vite:preloadError` reloads the page; a second within the cooldown does NOT (no loop); pushing the stamp past the cooldown reloads again (re-armed).
> **Owner note:** the `_headers` cache rules take effect automatically once Cloudflare redeploys (on merge to `main`); nothing to configure. **Dedup:** distinct from the PDF.js `import()` lazy-loading in B72/B67/B180 (those defer a heavy library until first use ‚Äî a feature), and from B205-era ErrorBoundary work (that catches *render* crashes; this catches *chunk-fetch* failures and recovers before the boundary is reached).

### B220 ‚Äî Esri imagery shows "Map data not yet available" placeholder on over-zoom (map finder) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B218, renumbered **B220** ‚Äî concurrent `main` PR #183 took B218 (dead header controls) + B219 (map-furniture restyle) while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B219. The implementing commits on this branch still say "B218".)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-20 (branch `claude/quirky-mayer-s3n0pm`).** On the Site Planner **map finder**, zooming in past the area's native imagery ceiling with Esri selected filled the whole canvas with gray "Map data not yet available" tiles while street labels still rendered on top. **Root cause (confirmed):** Esri World Imagery serves those placeholder tiles as **HTTP 200** (not errors), so Leaflet's error-tile fallback never fires; on a retina/HiDPI display `detectRetina` (added in B170 for sharpness) fetches one zoom level **higher** than the display zoom (zoomOffset +1), so a plain `maxNativeZoom: 19` let deep zoom request **z20** = the placeholder. **B182 already fixed this exact bug, but only on the planner-canvas backdrop** (`SitePlanner.jsx` GEO_BASEMAP detail layer's `detailMaxNative`); the **map-finder** layer (`MapFinder.jsx`) got `detectRetina` from B170 but **never the matching clamp** ‚Äî an incomplete original fix across the two call sites, not a refactor revert. **Fix (`MapFinder.jsx`):** the imagery `L.tileLayer` now clamps `maxNativeZoom` to `L.Browser.retina ? bm.maxNative - 1 : bm.maxNative` for **every source in the Imagery dropdown** (Esri 19‚Üí18, USGS 16‚Üí15 on retina), keeping `maxZoom: 21` so Leaflet **upscales** the deepest real tile past native instead of fetching placeholders. The labels/reference overlay (World_Transportation) is capped at `maxNativeZoom: 19` so it can't diverge above the imagery at deep zoom (the "labels float over gray" tell). Durable code comments left at the `BASEMAPS` config + both layer sites so a future restructure can't silently drop them. **Verified headless** (`gis-verify/mapfinder-overzoom-verify.mjs`, the map finder driven deep over a Katy parcel at DSF 1 and DSF 2): max imagery tile zoom requested = **z19 at both densities** (was z20 on retina), max labels zoom = **z19**, **0** placeholder/past-native responses ‚Äî logged **VERIFICATION V50**. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **414 tests** ¬∑ build green; lazy chunks intact.
> **Dedup:** RECURRENCE/completion of **B182** (done ‚Äî planner-canvas placeholder fix) across the second call site; builds on **B170** (detectRetina) + **B169** (blur diagnostic). Distinct from **B171** (gated high-res-source eval ‚Äî correctly NOT triggered; the imagery source isn't the problem) and **B162** (label zoom gating).

### B219 ‚Äî Professional cartographic restyle of the map north arrow + scale bar `[Site Planner]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B219** ‚Äî next free ID after B218)*

### B216 ‚Äî Harden edge-run setbacks for IRREGULAR parcels: concave inward placement + gentle-curve grouping `[Site Planner]` (bug/task) ‚Äî follow-up to B214/B215  *(owner-requested edge-case pass 2026-06-19; minted **B216** ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B215, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`).** Edge-case testing on irregular parcels (L-shapes, flag lots, curved frontage, dense survey boundaries, triangles) surfaced two issues, both fixed. **(1) Concave inward placement (refines B215):** the setback pill / boundary-dim fan chose the inboard side by stepping *toward the parcel centroid* ‚Äî but on a concave / L-shaped / flag-lot parcel the centroid can sit in a notch (or outside the polygon), so a pill was thrown to the WRONG side (outside the lot). Replaced with a **point-in-ring test** (a small step that must land INSIDE the boundary) via a new `inwardScreenNormal` helper (computed in feet, mapped to screen), used by the per-side pill, the per-segment pill, AND the run-length dimension ‚Äî correct on any shape. **(2) Gentle-curve grouping (refines B214):** `edgeRuns` now chains each edge to the **PREVIOUS** edge's bearing (was the run's FIRST edge), so a gently curved frontage (a few degrees per segment) or survey noise on a nominally-straight line groups into **ONE** side (one setback, one pill, one dimension) instead of many; a genuine corner still breaks the run, and a TIGHT curve (each segment turning beyond tolerance) correctly stays per-segment.
> **Tests:** +2 `edgeRuns` unit tests (gentle-curve groups; tight-curve splits ‚Äî **14** in `test/edgeRuns.test.js`). New headless harness `ui-audit/verify-edge-runs-irregular.mjs` (L-shape, flag lot, tight + gentle curved frontage, dense 12-vertex survey boundary, triangle) ‚Äî **19/19**: every setback pill lands inside the lot (the concave fix), every run-length dim outside, no NaN, and the shallow arc groups to 4 sides (not 17). lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **411 tests** ¬∑ build green; the original **B213‚ÄìB215 acceptance still 7/7** (the chain change keeps the 3-segment-east-side case at 4 sides). Verified **V48**. **Dedup:** not a new feature ‚Äî hardens the B214 run-grouping + B215 fan placement for irregular geometry; same canonical `pc.setbacks` model.

### B215 ‚Äî Stacked/occluded dimension labels at shared parcel-edge anchors (boundary dim + setback pill + "+" all at the edge midpoint) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted **B215** ‚Äî next free ID after B214)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`, commit `cc735e9`).** The parcel-edge boundary dimension, the setback value pill, and the add-vertex "+" handle no longer stack at the same edge midpoint. Each logical SIDE now gets **one run-length dimension placed OUTBOARD** of the edge (`parcelEdgeLabels` rewritten over `selRuns` + `runLabelAnchors`), and the **setback value pill is placed INBOARD** (toward the setback line it describes) ‚Äî fanned ~25 px apart along the edge normal, so neither occludes the other. The add-vertex "+" stays at the segment midpoint (it is the add-vertex handle, not a stack-expander) and now reads clearly once the dims move off it. No setback-line *length* label is ever drawn (the only length label is the boundary/run dimension), so there is nothing redundant to suppress.
> **Dedup / dependency:** built **with B214** ‚Äî run-grouping collapses the per-segment dimension stack into one label per side; B215 adds the boundary-vs-setback inboard/outboard fan that run-grouping alone does not. Distinct from **B121** (element NAME/area label overlap, `labelLayout.js`) and **B149** (zoom LOD) ‚Äî those are the centred element-label pool; this is the parcel-edge dimension/setback/handle pool. Self-verified headless (**V47**, `ui-audit/verify-edge-runs.mjs`): 4 run-length dims (one per side), each fanned 25 px from its pill.

### B214 ‚Äî Edit setback across a multi-segment side in one action (edge "runs") `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B214** ‚Äî next free ID after B213)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-edison-7gdn3y`, commit `cc735e9`).** New pure, unit-tested `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/edgeRuns.js` groups a parcel's **contiguous near-collinear edges** (¬±7¬∞ of the run's first-edge bearing, wrap-around-aware) into **runs** = logical sides, so a side a survey digitized as ~10 segments reads as ONE side. On the selected parcel the on-canvas setback editor shows **one pill per side**; editing it applies the value across **every segment of the run at once** via `setRunSetback`, writing the **canonical per-edge `pc.setbacks` array** (what `setbacksOf`/`constraintsOf`/`developableArea` read ‚Äî no parallel store) which `offsetPolygon` already miters into one continuous setback line. A **"By side / Per segment" toggle** (shown only when a side has >1 segment) plus **Alt-click a side pill** give the single-edge override for notches/jogs. The run also drives the single run-length dimension (B215). Easement `restrictsBuildings`/`restrictsPaving` flags already feed the same model via `exclusionZonesOf`, so both setbacks and easement exclusions reach the (stubbed) `developableArea` verdict engine ‚Äî structurally integrated.
> **Dedup:** reuses the contiguous-edge-run idea already shipped for parcel-edge easements (`buildParcelEdgeStrip` + `easeEdges`), here auto-grouped by bearing and applied to setbacks. Distinct from **B146** (interactive ELEMENT dimension callouts). **+12 unit tests** (`test/edgeRuns.test.js`). Self-verified headless (**V47**): selecting a parcel with a 3-segment east side shows **4 pills (S, E-run, N, W), not 6 edges**; "Per segment" ‚Üí 6; toggling back ‚Üí 4.

### B213 ‚Äî Inactive parcel still shows its setback line, acreage label, and edge/boundary dimensions (active-state not inherited by anchored elements) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B213** ‚Äî first filed as B206, then twice renumbered as concurrent `main` (PR #175 then PR #177) took B206‚ÄìB212 in the same window; this Site-Planner trio landed at the next free block **B213‚ÄìB215** to keep IDs unique)*

### B211 ‚Äî Task status as fill treatment (hollow / partial / solid) `[Scheduler / Gantt]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B195, renumbered **B211** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B194‚ÄìB209 while this was in flight)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-keller-wphsna`).** Task status moved **off the color channel onto a single continuous fill treatment** in both Gantt render paths (on-screen `GanttView` + the PDF/print `buildGanttSVG`). Every task bar keeps **one identity hue** (the existing task **gray `#94a3b8`**, or an explicit per-task `rowColor` override); status reads as **0‚Üí100% complete**: **not started (0%)** = hollow rounded pill (outline in the hue, required else invisible); **in progress** = partial fill (solid portion = `percentComplete`, lighter remainder behind it, thin outline around the whole); **complete (100%)** = solid fill. A **min-width floor** keeps a 0% bar from collapsing to a sliver. Fill fraction derives from `percentComplete` (Complete ‚Üí solid regardless). The **red / paused / overdue** signal stays in the **row background + the table** (untouched), so status never collides with the navy hierarchy. Milestone diamonds follow the same monochrome language (gray, filled when complete, hollow otherwise).

Palette preserved (the one purple `SS` dependency line `#7c3aed` untouched). lint 0 ¬∑ 352 tests ¬∑ build green.

### B210 ‚Äî Summary bars as depth-stepped brackets `[Scheduler / Gantt]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B194, renumbered **B210** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B194‚ÄìB209 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sharp-keller-wphsna`).** Replaced the heavy solid summary bars (a thick slab + barely-visible triangle endcaps) with a thin **bracket**: a navy horizontal **span** with **straight-down vertical legs** at each end (no triangles), in both render paths (`GanttView` + `buildGanttSVG`). WBS nesting depth is encoded by **three cues that step together, top-of-tree strongest** ‚Äî **darkness** (navy `#2B3340` ‚Üí `#46506A` ‚Üí `#6E7790` ‚Üí tint), **span thickness** (7/5/4/4 px), and **leg length** (a fraction of row height) ‚Äî the ramp **stops deepening at ~4 levels** (the table's indented name carries depth from there). The summary **name centers just above the span** in the bar's own level-navy (no thick fill to print white onto); no per-level label indentation (bars are date-positioned). An explicit `rowColor` override still wins.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-sequence.mjs`): DOM probe finds **36 navy bracket elements** (‚âà a dozen brackets √ó span+2 legs); a detail screenshot confirms the shape ‚Äî label above a thin span with a straight-down leg, **no triangle**. 0 runtime errors. lint 0 ¬∑ 352 tests ¬∑ build green.

### B203 ‚Äî Schedule project picker showed Site Planner projects; scheduling projects inaccessible `[Scheduler / Header-Nav]` (bug) ‚Äî CRITICAL  *(owner-reported 2026-06-19; minted **B203** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#169‚Äì#172) took B194‚ÄìB202 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B202)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/elegant-bohr-16zcag`).** Owner: in the **Schedule** module the Row-1 project picker listed **Site Planner** sites, and his scheduling projects (Goose Creek, Kilgore - Grand Port / "Grandport", Eight South a.k.a. vSAN, Pursuits, Papadopoulos) were unreachable.
> **Diagnosis first (the silent-data-loss rule) ‚Äî data was NEVER lost.** The Schedule workspace embeds a separate scheduler app in an **iframe** (`public/sequence/index.html`); that app stores ALL projects as one cloud record (`hs-v1`) in its **own** Supabase project (`ksetjztkplttbcehyicv`), cloud-first with the baked `__PLANAR_DATA__` only as a first-run seed. Inside the iframe the scheduler **hides its own header** (`.in-iframe .app-header{display:none}`), which is where its project picker + Dashboard/Projects toggle lived. The B191‚ÄìB193 shared breadcrumb that replaced it reads `listProjects()` ‚Üí the **Site Planner** site store and routes every action into the Site Planner ‚Äî so Schedule showed Site projects and couldn't open scheduler ones. A wiring bug, not a data bug.
> **Fix ‚Äî make the Row-1 picker module-aware via a postMessage bridge** (no second store, no schema change): the embedded scheduler now emits its OWN nav state (project list + active project + section) to the shell (`planar:nav-state`) and accepts select / dashboard / new-project commands back (`planar:nav-*`), same-origin-targeted. `ProjectBreadcrumb` accepts an optional **controlled `projects`** list (falls back to `listProjects()` when omitted, so Site/Markup are unchanged); `Scheduler.jsx` feeds in the iframe's projects and posts commands to it instead of bouncing into the Site Planner. Opened directly (not in the shell) the scheduler keeps its native header ‚Äî no regression.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-schedule-picker.mjs`, **8/8**, logged-out with the scheduler cloud blocked ‚Üí it fell back to its seed, which still flowed through the bridge): Site crumb "Map" lists Site projects; Schedule crumb "Dashboard" lists the SCHEDULER's projects (Goose Creek / Grand Port / Bee Sand) and **not** the seeded Site projects; selecting a project switches it inside the iframe; the Dashboard crumb opens the scheduler's reports view. 381 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green. **NOTE for the owner:** the headless run is offline/logged-out so it showed the scheduler's 3 *seed* projects; the live signed-in/online app will list his real set (the bug never touched that cloud record).
> **Dedup:** direct follow-up to **B191‚ÄìB193** (the shared breadcrumb) ‚Äî fixes their Site-only assumption for Schedule; reuses the same `AppHeader`/`ProjectBreadcrumb`, adds only the module-aware list + the iframe bridge. Paired with **B204** (module-contextual home label).

### B197 ‚Äî Print buildings/site data table `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B197)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The printed sheet now carries a **BUILDINGS** data table anchored on the right, next to the title block: one row per building (row keyed by the building's stable `el.id`), columns **name / sf / clear height / slab**. Clear height + slab are read from the building's stored properties (B198) ‚Äî never recomputed in the print routine ‚Äî and the table is part of the single-SVG composition (B200), so it scales with the sheet. Built in pure `lib/printSheet.js` (`buildBuildingTableSvg`); headless-rendered (`ui-audit/verify-print-sheet.mjs` ‚Üí `ui-audit/screens/print-sheet.png`). 15 printSheet tests.
> **Dedup:** distinct from B131 (overlay-in-print toggle); reuses B198's effective-property selector for the values.

### B198 ‚Äî Auto-assign clear height & slab thickness as building properties by square footage `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B198)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** `clearHeight` + `slabThickness` are now first-class building properties (available to any module), auto-assigned from the building's footprint sf via an **editable per-plan rule** (`settings.buildingRules`) plus an **optional manual override** stored on the element (`clearHeightOverride` / `slabThicknessOverride`; override wins, auto recomputes on sf change when unset). Upper tier inclusive at each boundary ‚Äî `<140k ‚Üí 32'/6"`, `[140k,600k) ‚Üí 36'/7"`, `>=600k ‚Üí 40'/7"` ‚Äî so a 250,000 sf building defaults to 36'/7" with no input (verified). New pure module `lib/buildingProps.js` (12 unit tests); additive el/settings fields (no migration). Surfaced + editable inline on the selected-building inspector and in the print Options flyout (B199).

### B199 ‚Äî Print options interface: edit global defaults and per-building overrides `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted B199)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The print-frame toolbar gained an **Options ‚ñæ** flyout (portal-mounted `AnchoredMenu`, so it escapes the toolbar's stacking context): (a) edit the **global size rules** from B198 (thresholds + their clear-height/slab values, with Reset to defaults) and (b) **override** clear height + slab per building (name editable too), with **auto vs set** surfaced and a one-click revert-to-auto. Editing globals changes defaults for un-overridden buildings; a per-building override pins that building. Live-smoke verified (`ui-audit/verify-print-live.mjs`, 0 runtime errors).

### B200 ‚Äî Print zoom: building/site plan doesn't scale with title block, not a cohesive PDF `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; minted B200)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** Root cause: the plan was a nested SVG but the title block + metrics were HTML flow around it ‚Äî two layout systems, so the print scale slider could scale the chrome while the plan held a fixed size. Fix: the **whole sheet is now ONE `<svg>`** (`lib/printSheet.js` `buildPrintSheetSvg`) ‚Äî title block, the plan (nested `<svg>` keeping its own viewBox), the buildings table (B197) and the metrics share one viewBox and **one scaling transform**, so every layer scales together at any zoom and prints as one cohesive page (`@page margin:0` + intrinsic-inch SVG = exactly one page; inset border clears the printer edge). The on-canvas print frame now matches the printed plan box (WYSIWYG). Headless-rendered: one root SVG, nested plan, letter-landscape 11in viewBox. 15 tests.

### B201 ‚Äî Print filename format `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; minted B201)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commits `8e19081` + follow-up).** Exported PDF (document title ‚Üí Save-as filename) and PNG use **`YYYY.MM.DD {Project} - {Plan Name}`** ‚Äî e.g. `2026.06.19 Cypress Logistics - Plan 1` (or `‚Ä¶ - Scheme A` once the plan is renamed). Date = today at export, project = the active site name, **trailing piece = the plan's own label** (`planLabel`). Filesystem-illegal characters are stripped from project + plan (the ` - ` separator and date dots preserved); a blank plan name just drops the tail. `lib/printSheet.js` `sheetFileName`/`sanitizeFilename` (tested).
> **Owner decision (2026-06-19):** the trailing identifier is the **plan name**, not an incrementing number ‚Äî so the filename always tracks whatever the plan is named (today "Plan 1", later e.g. "Scheme A") and won't drift or surprise. (Superseded the initial incrementing-sheet-number default; the per-session counter was removed.)

### B202 ‚Äî "Preparing print" hangs before producing file `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-6"; minted B202)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/sweet-hypatia-itdlvu`, commit `8e19081`).** The stall was the image-inlining step: aerial/overlay `<image>` fetches ran one-by-one with **no timeout**, so any fetch that hung through the TLS-inspection proxy blocked prep for up to ~60s. Fix: each fetch is now **time-boxed** (`AbortController`, 8s) and they run **in parallel**, so worst-case prep is ~8s and a hung image is dropped (PNG) or keeps its remote href (print loads it natively). Added prep **timing instrumentation** (`console.debug` marks for inline + ready) so any future stall is diagnosable rather than a mystery.

### B196 ‚Äî Scale bar + north arrow as DOM overlays so they're always fully visible (B173 follow-up) `[Site Planner / UI]` (bug)  *(owner re-reported on the live site 2026-06-19 ‚Äî "scale still not fully shown, nor the north cardinal direction"; minted B196 ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B195)*

Relocated the two colliders: calibration pill `left:12 ‚Üí 56` (beside the arrow), zoom controls `bottom:78 ‚Üí 100` (above the scale bar). Also kept the planner root `minHeight:600 ‚Üí 0` (belt-and-suspenders with B173's `index.css` `100dvh`+`overflow:hidden`, so a sub-600px window clips nothing). The **export** furniture path (`buildSheetFurnitureSvg`) is untouched ‚Äî export parity preserved. **Self-verified headless at 1600√ó800 AND 1600√ó540:** page overflow 0; the "FEET" (scale) and "N" (north) labels both `getBoundingClientRect` fully inside the viewport at both heights; corner screenshots show the scale bar clear below the +/‚àí/‚§¢ zoom stack and the north arrow beside (not under) the calibration pill. lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green ¬∑ `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact.
> **Reconciliation:** B173 (DONE, stays) fixed the page-scroll via viewport pinning and judged a portal overlay unnecessary; the owner's live re-report proved the furniture *placement* (in-SVG + pill overlap) was the remaining cause. B196 implements exactly the "fixed overlay anchored to the canvas corner" mechanism B173's note had set aside. B172/B174/B175 (tabs / header ‚àí20% / parcel checkbox) shipped independently on `main` and this branch's duplicates of them were dropped during the merge in favour of `main`'s versions.

### B195 ‚Äî Trailer-parking label stays inside its polygon at every zoom level `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B190, renumbered **B195** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#164/#168 + sibling branches) took B189‚ÄìB193 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B193)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/cool-babbage-mpc9sd`). Zooming out grew the trailer label *relative to its shrinking strip* until it overflowed: the label was sized in fixed **screen** pixels (floored at `ls‚â•0.34`), so it stayed roughly constant while the strip got smaller on zoom-out ‚Äî "fit logic exists but the limits are off." **Fix:** a trailer label is now sized as a **fraction of the strip's real-world extent** (EPSG:2278 feet ‚Üí screen px via the current pixels-per-foot, `view.ppf`), so it scales WITH the area and stays contained by construction. The text runs along the strip's **long** side and the line-stack across its **short** side, each with its own fit bound (the smaller governs ‚Äî this matches `stripLabelRot`, the B186/B188 helper that aligns the label to the long axis). The font is **floored** at a legible minimum (`minPx`, below which a too-small ‚âà2-spot strip takes *controlled overflow* rather than going illegible) and **capped** at the normal label size so it never balloons when zoomed in. The shared label engine `lib/labelLayout.js` gained a **`noLeader`** option: a trailer label that still can't fit overflows **in place** (centred on the strip), instead of being leadered out, and the engine now **prefers dropping a line to fit inside** before accepting that overflow. Per-label font metrics (`fs`/`lh`/`charW`) are threaded through the candidate ‚Üí layout ‚Üí render path; every non-trailer label keeps the existing global metrics (defaults unchanged). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-trailer-label.mjs`): across five zoom levels the label stays **inside** the strip ‚Äî shape **397√ó55px ‚Üí 102√ó14px**, label/shape height ratio **0.50** (capped when the shape is large) **‚Üí 0.96** (floored when small), `inside=true` at every step; `verify-new1to5.mjs` confirms a vertical strip still rotates correctly and other label types are untouched. **2 new `labelLayout` tests** (noLeader overflow-in-place; drop-a-line-to-fit). 354 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.
> **Dedup:** extends the **B121** shared label LOD + collision engine (`labelLayout.js`) and complements **B149** (zoom-out decluttering) ‚Äî area-relative sizing is added *on top of* that one engine, not as a parallel renderer. Reuses **B186/B188**'s `stripLabelRot` (label orientation along a strip) rather than re-deriving it. Depended on **B194** for the final two-line label content. Distinct from B188, which fixed label *orientation/consistency*; B195 fixes label *containment under zoom*.

### B194 ‚Äî Trailer-parking label: stall depth in the title, drop the row-dimension line `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B189, renumbered **B194** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#164/#168 + sibling branches) took B189‚ÄìB193 while this was in flight, so this is the real next free ID after B193)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/cool-babbage-mpc9sd`). The trailer-parking label is now **two lines** instead of three: line 1 = the per-stall trailer length + name (e.g. **"50‚Ä≤ Trailer Parking"**), line 2 = the trailer count (e.g. **"30 trailers"**). The old third line (overall row dimensions, e.g. "360‚Ä≤ √ó 50‚Ä≤" / "355‚Ä≤ √ó 50‚Ä≤") is **dropped entirely** ‚Äî the depth now lives in the title and the overall row length is intentionally gone. The stall depth is read straight off the element's own config (`cfgOf(el).trailerL`, the depth a trailer sits in) ‚Äî **not** the overall row length and **not** recomputed; the count keeps the existing `trailerStalls`/`estTrailers` math (polygon fields still read "(est)"). One code path in `SitePlanner.jsx` (the centred-label builder), so single strips, wide fields, and rotated vertical strips all pick it up. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-trailer-label.mjs` + `verify-new1to5.mjs`): a 360‚Ä≤√ó50‚Ä≤ strip reads **"50‚Ä≤ Trailer Parking" / "30 trailers"** with no dimension line; a wide field reads "53‚Ä≤ Trailer Parking / 18 trailers"; a thin vertical strip runs the same two lines along its long axis. 354 tests (full suite, post-merge with `main`) ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.
> **Dedup:** distinct from **B188** (which fixed label *orientation/consistency* ‚Äî running the label in-line on a narrow strip via `stripLabelRot`); B194 changes the label *content*. Builds on B188's strip-label work, doesn't duplicate it. Paired with **B195** (containment under zoom), which depends on this item's final two-line dimensions.

### B193 ‚Äî Persist current project before switching `[Header/Nav]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; filed provisionally as B191, renumbered **B193** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#168) took B189‚ÄìB190 for the Site Analysis tranche, so this is the real next free ID after B190/B191/B192)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/awesome-gauss-jlrq5v`).** A breadcrumb switch (to another project or to the Dashboard) flushes the current project first, so a switch can't silently drop unsaved work ‚Äî it routes through the **existing** data-loss machinery: in the Site Planner, opening another project goes through `handleOpenSite` ‚Üí `flushSite()` and the `key`-change unmount `persistOrDrop()`; in Doc Review, the `useReviewPersistence` unmount/visibility flush already guarantees the local write. On top of that, B193 adds the owner-requested **cloud-at-risk surfacing** (the B124/B125 silent-failure rule): each workspace passes a normalized `saveState` to the breadcrumb, and when it's `offline`/`error`, the switcher shows a **passive ‚öÝ line in the dropdown** AND a **transient "saved on this device ‚Äî will sync when reconnected" toast** on the switch. The switch is **never blocked** on a successful cloud save, but is **never silent** about an at-risk one.
> **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to3.mjs`): project switches complete cleanly; the at-risk surfacing is gated on `offline`/`error` (the sandbox is logged-out ‚Üí `local`, no false warning). **Dedup:** no new persistence path ‚Äî reuses SitePlanner's `flushSite`/`persistOrDrop` + Doc Review's persistence flush; B193 is the routing + surfacing layer over them. 344 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B190 ‚Äî Click a constraint card to toggle its layer on the map `[Site Planner / Site Analysis]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B185, renumbered **B190** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#164) took B184‚ÄìB188 for unrelated Site Planner items, so this is the real next free ID after B189)*

### B189 ‚Äî Site Analysis constraint queries failing (UNKNOWN / "Failed to execute query") `[Site Planner / Site Analysis]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B184, renumbered **B189** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (#164) took B184‚ÄìB188 for unrelated Site Planner items, so this is the real next free ID after B188)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/bold-edison-h8tfkc`).** Filed AND fixed AND verified live the same session. Bug: on Site Analysis, **Wetlands** + **Pipelines** returned "Failed to execute query." ‚Üí UNKNOWN, while Floodplain worked. The bug report's instinct to **audit every category, not just the two visible**, paid off: a **third** source (**Oil & gas wells**, below the fold) was 400-ing too.
> **Root cause was a different field bug per source ‚Äî confirmed live (HTTP 400 with old fields ‚Üí HTTP 200 with real features) against a known Katy/Sheldon-Lake parcel before patching:**
> - **Wetlands** ‚Äî NWI split layers 1/2 are **JOINED** layers (`Wetlands ‚ãà NWI_Wetland_Codes`), so every field comes back **table-qualified** (`Wetlands_CONUS_West.WETLAND_TYPE`); asking for the bare names 400'd, and the qualifier **differs per sublayer** (East vs West). Fix: request `outFields:"*"` and **`normalizeAttrs()`** strips the `Table.` prefix so the summarizers read plain names.
> - **Pipelines** ‚Äî queried `OPERATOR`/`COMMODITY`, which **don't exist** (real: `OPER_NM`, `CMDTY_DESC`, `DIAMETER`).
> - **Oil & gas wells** ‚Äî queried `LEASE_NAME`, which **doesn't exist** on the Wells layer (real: `SYMNUM`/`API`/`WELLID`/‚Ä¶).
> All three fixed + flipped **`verified:true`**, so a now-working empty query resolves to **None found** (not conservative UNKNOWN) ‚Äî matching the bug report's "expected." The silent-error guard is intact: a genuine HTTP/network error still classifies **unknown**, never a fabricated "none." Added **diagnostics** ‚Äî `defaultFetchJson` carries `{httpStatus,url,arcgisCode}` on the Error and `logQueryFailure()` prints the real failure to the console, so an opaque "Failed to execute query." is debuggable instead of silent.
> **Verified live (headless, `ui-audit/verify-analysis.mjs`, real USFWS/FEMA/TxRRC endpoints):** Floodplain **PRESENT (Zone AE)**, Wetlands **PRESENT (Lake, Freshwater Forested/Shrub Wetland)**, Pipelines **NONE FOUND**, Oil & gas **NONE FOUND** ‚Äî zero "Failed to execute query." 341 tests (siteAnalysis 25‚Üí36, incl. the qualified-field + corrected-field + normalizeAttrs cases), lint 0 errors, build green. **V45.**
> **Dedup:** this is the per-source debug of **B147**'s "üî≤ Remaining (1)." Distinct from **B133/B135** (those fixed the wetlands *map-overlay image* `/export`; this fixed the Site Analysis `/query` connector ‚Äî a different request path on the same host).

### B188 ‚Äî Trailer-parking label inconsistent + should run in-line on the strip `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-5"; filed provisionally as B184, renumbered **B188** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B180‚ÄìB183 for unrelated items, so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). Two trailer-parking instances rendered their labels differently ‚Äî the wide field kept its 3-line label horizontal, while the narrow wall strip overflowed (the collision engine leadered it OUT of the strip). Root cause: there was no orientation logic, so a label wider than the strip was pulled outside rather than turned to run along it. Fix = the **shared label-orientation helper** built for B186 (`stripLabelRot`, applied to `landscape`/`sidewalk`/`trailer` strips): when a label is wider than the strip is narrow, it runs ALONG the strip's long axis (vertical text on a vertical strip), so both instances now render consistently in-line and neither claims more space than the strip itself. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): a thin vertical trailer strip shows its label running vertically down the strip; a wide trailer field keeps its label horizontal. 286 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B187 ‚Äî Truck court resize must anchor to the dock wall and push/pull trailer parking `[Site Planner]` (bug) ‚Äî high severity  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; filed provisionally as B183, renumbered **B187**.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). Changing a truck court's **Depth** field (e.g. 135‚Üí140) resized it from the **centre** ‚Äî losing depth on both sides, detaching the paving from both the dock wall and the trailer parking (a silently-wrong geometry state). **Two root causes fixed:** (1) `resizeSelEl` (the numeric Width/Depth editor) kept `cx/cy` fixed, so it grew/shrank symmetrically ‚Äî it now applies the same **`hostClampOf`/`clampToHost`** host-edge pin the resize grips already use, so an attached strip/court stays flush against the dock wall and only the FAR edge moves; (2) `refitChildren` never moved the court's back-side trailer when the court itself was the resized element (it only handled trailers when the *building* resized) ‚Äî it now registers a resized truck court in `courtBox`, so the `forCourt` trailer follows the moved far edge (pushed out on grow, pulled in on shrink, spacing preserved). Covers both the numeric field and the resize grips. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new4b.mjs`, the owner's exact path ‚Äî Depth 135‚Üí170): the building/dock-wall label moved **0 px** (court stays anchored) while the trailer label moved **+54 px** out (pushed flush) ‚Äî court ‚Üí court paving ‚Üí trailer stay connected, nothing detaches. 286 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B186 ‚Äî Buffer-strip width labels run along the strip's long axis `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B182, renumbered **B186**; shares its helper with B188/NEW-5)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). A "5‚Ä≤ Landscape" / "5‚Ä≤ Sidewalk" label rendered horizontally even on a thin vertical strip, eating canvas across the strip. Added one shared, holistic helper ‚Äî **`stripLabelRot(el, lines, charW, ppf)`** (covers `landscape`, `sidewalk` AND `trailer`, no per-type duplication) ‚Äî that returns a rotation when the label is wider than the strip is narrow: the label then runs ALONG the strip's long axis (vertical text on a vertical strip, horizontal on a horizontal one). The shared `labelLayout` collision engine was extended to test the label's **rotated** on-screen footprint, so a vertical label is fitted against the strip's tall height and narrow width (and so it lands INSIDE the strip instead of being leadered out). New unit test in `test/labelLayout.test.js`. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): vertical landscape/sidewalk/trailer strips show vertical labels; horizontal strips and wide fields stay horizontal. 286 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B185 ‚Äî Site acreage chip is draggable + persisted `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; filed provisionally as B181, renumbered **B185**.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). The parcel acreage chip ("32.51 ac") was pinned at the parcel centroid and obstructed the layout. It's now **click-and-drag** (in Select), to anywhere ‚Äî including outside the parcel boundary ‚Äî storing a `labelOffset` (parcel-local feet) on the parcel so it survives geometry edits. New `startAcChip` + an `acChip` drag-move case mirror the B146 dimension-callout drag pattern; the offset persists via the existing Site Model save path (additive field on `parcels[]`, mirrors to Supabase when signed in). **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new3.mjs`): the chip dragged 182 px and `parcels[0].labelOffset` was written to the saved store. 286 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B184 ‚Äî 24‚Ä≤ road-width dimension drifts left of centre `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B180, renumbered **B184** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B180‚ÄìB183.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/happy-goldberg-piym6g`). The road-width dimension ("24‚Ä≤") rendered shifted toward the left edge of the road instead of centred on the span. Cause: the dimension line/label were placed at **18 %** along the element's long axis (a sensible default for a building's depth tick, but wrong for a road, where the width tick should sit on the centreline of the length). Fix: roads now place the width dimension at the **midpoint (50 %)** of the length (`posF = el.type === "road" ? 0.5 : 0.18`); the measured value and the perpendicular span anchor were already correct (the label sits at the midpoint of the measured width), so this is a position-only fix ‚Äî no measurement-accuracy change. **Self-verified headless** (`ui-audit/verify-new1to5.mjs`): the "24‚Ä≤" label sits centred along the road. 286 tests ¬∑ lint 0 ¬∑ build green.

### B183 ‚Äî Editable layers decouple from backdrop during pan while loading `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B177, renumbered **B183** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B176‚ÄìB181, so this is the real next free ID after B181/B182.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** On a freshly-loaded site, grabbing and panning before load settled made the drawn layers (massing/parcels/markup) visibly offset from the aerial for a frame or two, then snap back. **Root cause (confirmed, not the pasted race-condition theory):** in Planyr the SVG *is* the source of truth and the basemap follows it, so the layers can't reproject against a stale transform ‚Äî the decoupler was **B65's own ghost snapshot**. A `commit` clones the basemap into a frozen overlay held until the fresh tiles `load`; while loading, that `load` is delayed so the snapshot lingered, and a pan moved the live SVG while the **frozen** snapshot stayed put ‚Üí the aerial lagged the drawn layers until the snapshot expired (hence "only early on, then snaps back"). **Fix:** drop any lingering snapshot the instant a new gesture starts (`dropGhost()` at the top of the transform path), so a pan is tracked by the live CSS transform (welded to the SVG) and the backfill covers any reveal; a fresh snapshot is taken only at the next commit. **Verified headless** (`ui-audit/diagnose-decouple.mjs`, retina + throttled, pan immediately after load): **0 %** of pan frames have a snapshot on top (idle baseline has one, correctly dropped on the first pan). lint 0 ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green.

### B182 ‚Äî Basemap tiles missing at high zoom ("Map data not yet available") `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B176, renumbered **B182** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B176‚ÄìB181 (jurisdictions/tax + cost takeoff), so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** Zooming in deep showed gray "Map data not yet available" placeholder tiles instead of imagery. **Root cause (measured, `ui-audit/diagnose-zoomdepth.mjs`):** Esri World Imagery is native to **z19**; `detectRetina` (added in B170 for sharpness) fetches **one zoom level higher** than the display zoom, so at deep zoom on a retina display the detail layer requested **z20** (168 requests), which Esri answers with the placeholder image. `maxNativeZoom:19` didn't account for the retina offset. **Fix:** drop the detail layer's `maxNativeZoom` by 1 on retina (`L.Browser.retina ? maxNative-1 : maxNative`), so the highest native fetch is z19 and beyond that it **upscales the deepest real imagery** instead of fetching nonexistent tiles ‚Äî exactly the requested "clamp to deepest available zoom, scale the last good tiles up; never put placeholders over the plan." **Verified:** max tile zoom requested now **19** at both retina (DSF 2) and non-retina (DSF 1), **0** placeholder/empty responses (was 168). The coarse backfill (`maxNativeZoom:13`) was already clamping correctly. lint 0 ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green.
> **Follow-up ‚Üí B218 (2026-06-20):** this fix was applied only to the **planner-canvas** backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx` GEO_BASEMAP). The **map-finder** imagery layer (`MapFinder.jsx`) had the same `detectRetina` (from B170) but never got this retina clamp, so the placeholder still showed there on a retina display. B218 brought the identical clamp to the map finder (every dropdown source) + capped the labels overlay. Both call sites now clamp.

### B180 ‚Äî Verify paving area excludes curb footprint `[Cost]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted **B180** ‚Äî highest B# across both files was B179, so this is the real next free ID. Prerequisite for B181's paving-area trim.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/determined-feynman-l7c61b`). Investigated ‚Üí confirmed correct by construction, and locked it in.** There was no pre-existing *cost* paving figure to fold curb into ‚Äî the only paving area the app derived was the **impervious/SF** metric, where including the curb band is *correct* (curb is impervious surface), so that stays untouched. The new cost takeoff (B181) derives paving from the road's **face-of-curb-to-face-of-curb travel width** (`roadTravelWidth` = `min(w,h) ‚àí 2¬∑curb`), which **excludes** the curb by definition: a 30‚Ä≤ FC-FC road yields 30‚Ä≤ of paving, never 31‚Ä≤. So the defect the brief warned about (folding the 6‚Ä≥ curb each side into paving) cannot occur ‚Äî the cost math reads travel width, not the full element rectangle.
> **Locked against regression:** `roadQuantities` (in `lib/costTakeoff.js`) takes the FC-FC width explicitly and a unit test asserts a 30‚Ä≤ FC-FC √ó 1000‚Ä≤ barrier-curb road = exactly **30,000 SF (3,333.33 SY)** of paving with curb **outside** that width ‚Äî so a future change that folded curb back in would fail the suite. **Live-confirmed in-browser:** a seeded 26‚Ä≤-cross road (FC-FC travel 25‚Ä≤) reads **1,611 SY** in the Yield panel (25 √ó 580 √∑ 9); had curb been folded in (26‚Ä≤) it would read 1,675 SY ‚Äî the 1,611 proves the exclusion. 300 tests green, lint 0 errors, build green.

### B181 ‚Äî Curb as a separate linear quantity type with curb-type attribute `[Cost]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B181** ‚Äî next free ID after B180.)*
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/determined-feynman-l7c61b`).** A road segment now derives **two independent, separately-priced quantities**:
> - **Paving** ‚Äî an AREA item, **square yards (SY; 1 SY = 9 SF)** = length √ó FC-FC paving width √∑ 9. Width is stored/derived as **face-of-curb to face-of-curb** (the drivable surface), so a back-of-curb dimension can't silently inflate it.
> - **Curb** ‚Äî a LINEAR item, **linear feet (LF)** = length √ó curbed-side count. **Both sides counted** (a 1,000‚Ä≤ road curbed both sides = 2,000 LF).
>
> **Curb carries a `curbType` attribute that selects its unit price:** `none` / **`barrier`** (vertical ~6‚Ä≥ lip, no gutter pan) / **`curb-gutter`** (curb + flat concrete gutter pan, typ. 18‚Äì24‚Ä≥). For **curb-and-gutter**, the gutter pan rides with the curb LF item, so **paving trims by the pan width on each curbed side** (`paving = FC-FC ‚àí panWidth √ó sides`); pan width is a property of the curb-and-gutter type (default 2.0‚Ä≤/24‚Ä≥, editable). Curb LF is split **barrier vs curb-and-gutter** in the rollup so each rides its own price.
> **Implementation:** new pure library `src/workspaces/site-planner/lib/costTakeoff.js` (`roadQuantities`, `costRollup`, curb-type readers) ‚Äî no React, fully unit-tested (`test/costTakeoff.test.js`, 15 cases). Road-element fields are additive/optional (`curbType`, `curbedSides`, `panWidth`) and persist losslessly through the Site Model (els pass through untouched; no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump). UI: a **"Curb & paving (cost)"** group in the road inspector (curb-type dropdown, curbed-sides Both/One, gutter-pan width, live per-segment SY/LF readout ‚Äî inline editors only, no dialogs) and a collapsible **"Road cost (screening)"** section in the **Yield** panel (site-wide Paving SY + Curb LF by type, **user-supplied** unit-price inputs ‚Äî blank by default, never a hardcoded $/LF ‚Äî and a priced subtotal).
> **Hook left for later (not built):** `roadQuantities` tags each curb run `curbCategory: "linear"` so a future **radius/corner curb** category (often a higher unit price) can be broken out as its own priced line without reworking the rollup.
> **Verified:** 300 tests green (15 new), lint 0 errors, build green, lazy-chunk split intact. **Live headless (logged-out preview):** Yield ‚Üí "Road cost (screening)" renders **Paving 1,611 SY ¬∑ Curb ¬∑ barrier 1,160 LF** with the FC-FC caveat and unit-price inputs, **zero page errors** (`ui-audit/verify-cost.mjs`).

### B176 ‚Äî Jurisdictions overlay `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B176** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B167‚ÄìB175, so this is the real next free ID after B175.)*
`[x]` Toggleable boundary overlays so you can see, on the map, which districts a site sits in ‚Äî county, city limits, city ETJ, and MUD/water districts. "See which sites are in a MUD around me." No school (per spec). Screening-grade, with a hard "boundary = has jurisdiction, NOT physically served/connected" caveat on every layer.

> - **County boundaries** (`esriFeature`) ‚Äî reuses the **verified** TxDOT county FeatureServer already used by jurisdiction *identify* (B93), so the line you see is the line the identify reports.
> - **City limits** (`esriFeature`) ‚Äî verified TxGIO city-boundaries layer (same source as identify).

> - **MUD / water districts** (`dynamic`) ‚Äî **statewide TCEQ water-district boundaries** (the data behind TCEQ's public Water Districts Map Viewer, republished by HARC: `harcags.harcresearch.org/.../Boundaries/TCEQ_Water_Districts/MapServer`). Covers **Harris + Fort Bend + statewide** ‚Äî not county-gated. (Initial cut shipped Fort-Bend-only; switched to the statewide TCEQ source same day when the owner pointed out TCEQ's mapper.) A `dynamic` image export renders via a CORS-exempt `<img>` even if the probe can't reach the host.
> All ride the existing probe + honest per-layer status + data-age (B96), so a dead endpoint shows a quiet "failed" dot, never wrong data. **Reuses verified endpoints (no new credentials, no parallel renderer); URLs imported from `lib/jurisdiction.js` so there's one source of truth (no drift).** lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green. **Self-verified headless** (`gis-verify/jurisdictions-overlay-verify.mjs`): the Jurisdictions group + all four toggles render in the Layers panel and toggling County boundaries works with **zero JS errors**.
> **Live-render verification = V44 (handed off to a fresh session).** county/city/ETJ hosts (services.arcgis.com, feature.geographic.texas.gov) are reachable + return 200; the MUD host `harcresearch.org` was added to the env egress allowlist 2026-06-19 but is **not live in the session that shipped this** (already-running container keeps the old policy ‚Üí still 403) ‚Äî so a NEW session confirms the MUD tiles paint over a known Harris MUD parcel. If HARC ever proves unreliable in prod, alternates: City of Houston cohgis MUDs, or `services.twdb.texas.gov` water districts ‚Äî a one-line URL swap in `JURISDICTIONS.jur_mud`.
> **Foundation for B177 (tax breakdown) + B178 (rate choropleth).** Supersedes the GIS-overlay "B" path of the old B165.

### B65 ‚Äî White flashing on zoom/pan and general redraw `[Site Planner / map]` (bug)
`[x]` **Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/nice-heisenberg-r6lmf1`).** Zooming/panning a located site flashed (originally white) as the aerial blanked between redraws. **Root cause, measured not guessed** (headless probe `ui-audit/diagnose-flash.mjs`): the basemap view-lock effect called `map.setView(center, z, {animate:false})` on *every* planner `view` change; Leaflet's `setView`‚Üí`_resetView` fires `viewreset`, whose GridLayer handler `_resetAll` **wipes and reloads all tiles**, so each wheel step blanked the aerial for a frame (loaded tiles collapsed **22 ‚Üí 2**), exposing the backdrop.
> **Fix shipped (two parts):**
> 1. **Mitigation (commit `cf26912`):** the basemap container backdrop was `PAL.paper` (`#f4f1ea`, near-white) ‚Üí any gap read as a *bright* flash. Changed to a neutral mid-dark gray (`#3f3f3f`) **only while the aerial is on** (stays `PAL.paper` with the aerial off so the SVG-off background still matches). Bright flash ‚Üí dim blink.
> 2. **Real fix ‚Äî seamless transform-based zoom (commit `af10d1c`):** stop re-`setView`-ing on every frame. Hold Leaflet at a committed center/zoom and, for the small deltas of a live gesture, CSS-`transform` (translate+scale) the whole map container so the already-loaded tiles (and the shared FEMA/NWI overlay layers, which live on the same map) scale to track the gesture ‚Äî no tile reload, no wipe, no flash. A debounced (180 ms) `setView` re-renders crisp once the gesture settles. First paint / resize / >1.5-zoom-level jumps commit immediately so the aerial is never scaled into a blurry mess. Transform math: `scale = getZoomScale(z, committed)`; translate so the desired center maps to the container centre (matches the SVG, which renders at true scale every frame), `transform-origin:0 0`. Container CSS transforms don't affect Leaflet's coordinate math (it uses cached `_size`/pixel-origin, and `clientWidth` is layout-box, unaffected by transform), so alignment is preserved.
> **Tested + rejected on the way:** flipping the map to `zoomAnimation/fadeAnimation:true` made it *worse* (gap frames 1‚Üí4, min loaded still 2) and reintroduces SVG-desync risk ‚Äî not used.
> **Verified headless:** `diagnose-flash.mjs` now reports **0 gap frames** (min loaded 8, was 2); `ui-audit/verify-zoom-align.mjs` confirms the drawn building/parcel stay locked to the aerial through the transform and after the crisp commit (no jump). lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green. **Live confirmation on planyr.io still nice-to-have** (a one-frame flash can't be captured headless), but the mechanism + alignment are proven. **Note:** Document Review's PDF viewer uses a different (canvas raster) renderer, not Leaflet ‚Äî if zoom-flashing shows there too it's a separate fix, tracked if/when reported.
> **Follow-up 2026-06-19 (same branch) ‚Äî kill the blank-backdrop reveal during the gesture.** After the flash fix shipped, the owner saw (screenshot) large flat cream patches while panning/zooming a project. Cause: the CSS-transformed basemap container (`geoWrapRef`) slid/scaled and exposed the canvas's `PAL.paper` (`wrapRef`) behind it. Fix (no new dependency): wrap the basemap in a **static clip box** (`inset:0`, `overflow:hidden`, dark `#3f3f3f` bg, never transformed) holding an **oversized inner map div** (`inset:-GEO_OVERSCAN`, `GEO_OVERSCAN = 320` px). The map now overhangs the viewport by 320 px on every side with `keepBuffer` tiles already loaded, so a normal pan/zoom transform reveals **real imagery**; anything beyond the overhang shows the **static dark backdrop**, never the cream page. The transform math is unchanged (it already uses `map.getSize()/2`, which adapts to the larger container, so basemap‚ÜîSVG alignment is preserved). Verified headless: `ui-audit/pan-reveal.mjs` (a hard mid-pan drag) now shows imagery edge-to-edge with no cream; `verify-zoom-align.mjs` still shows the geometry locked to the aerial through the transform + crisp commit. lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green.
> **Follow-up 2 2026-06-19 (same branch) ‚Äî kill the whole-screen "flash to black" on zoom-out.** Owner: zooming out from a building flashed the entire screen dark, even parts already loaded. Cause: the crisp re-render (`commit`) calls `map.setView`, whose Leaflet `viewreset`‚Üí`_resetAll` **removes ALL tiles and reloads them**, so for one frame the dark backdrop showed everywhere. Fix = **ghost-buffer the commit**: before the `setView`, clone the current basemap container (with its live CSS transform baked in) into a frozen overlay (`geoGhostRef`) pinned on top; the fresh tiles load underneath; on the tile layer's `load` event (or a 1.4 s fallback) the ghost is removed ‚Äî so the old picture stays visible until the new one is ready and the wipe is never seen. Also dropped the old non-buffered ">1.5 levels ‚Üí hard commit" branch; the crisp re-render now fires on settle (160 ms) OR once accumulated zoom drift passes ~0.75 levels, both **ghost-buffered** so a mid-gesture re-base no longer flashes. Verified headless (`ui-audit/zoomout-frames.mjs`, samples a continuous wheel zoom-out and measures the fraction of dark-backdrop pixels per frame): worst-case dark coverage **1.6 %** (UI edges only) ‚Äî no full-screen black at any frame (was a brief whole-screen wipe). Alignment + crisp settle unchanged (`verify-zoom-align.mjs`). lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green.
> **Follow-up 3 2026-06-19 (same branch) ‚Äî fix the slow gray initial load (regression).** Owner: after the above, a freshly-opened site sat on the gray backdrop for ~10 s before the aerial appeared. Cause: the overscan (2.5√ó viewport) **√ó** detectRetina (2√ó density) ‚âà **4√ó the tile bytes** on first paint, so on a real connection the detail tiles took ~10 s to cover (the sandbox is too fast to feel it ‚Äî reproduced with Playwright CDP network throttling at ~1.2 Mbps: time-to-coverage **9.1 s**). Fix = a **coarse "instant" backfill layer**: a second `L.tileLayer` under the detail layer capped at `maxNativeZoom: 13` (a handful of large-area tiles, no detectRetina) that loads near-instantly and blankets the view with blurry imagery, then the heavy detail layer is added **only after the backfill paints** (`bf.once("load", addDetail)` + a 600 ms fallback) so its many retina tiles don't flood the connection and starve the coarse ones. Result (same 1.2 Mbps throttle): time-to-coverage **9.1 s ‚Üí ~3 s** (blurry), detail then sharpens on top to the full 45 tiles; on a normal connection the coarse coverage is ~instant. No regression to the interactive fixes (zoom-out flash still 1.6 %, pan still full-imagery). `addDetail` guards against the aerial being toggled off mid-wait. lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green. Harness: `ui-audit/initial-load.mjs` (optional `THROTTLE=1`).

This item added the **literal checkbox affordance** the owner asked for (the prior control was a `‚úì Active / ‚óØ Inactive` chip on the *selected* parcel only; now every row carries a checkbox, and the row + label dim with a "¬∑ inactive" tag) and **closed the merge-candidacy gap**: `toggleMerge` now refuses to add an inactive parcel to the combine set, and `mergeParcels` filters inactive parcels out of the chosen group ‚Äî so an inactive parcel is excluded from yield **and** from the working merge, matching B100's intent. `SitePlanner.jsx` only; reuses the existing `toggleParcelActive` (pushes history + autosaves). **Self-verified headless (Chromium, logged-out preview):** two-parcel site ‚Üí both checkboxes checked ‚Üí unchecking parcel A dims its row + canvas polygon and stamps "¬∑ inactive"; the other parcel stays active. 257 tests green, lint 0 errors, build green.
