### B173 ‚Äî App pinned to the viewport; map scale bar always visible `[Site Planner / UI + Shell]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B168, renumbered **B173** ‚Äî #152 + #153 collisions; next free after B171.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/optimistic-wozniak-4iltkx`). Root cause: nothing guaranteed the app couldn't grow taller than the window, so the page itself could scroll and push the bottom-of-canvas scale bar below the fold (and the header off the top). Fix is structural, not a scale-bar move: `index.css` now sets `overflow:hidden` on `html, body, #root` and pins them to `100dvh` (dynamic viewport height ‚Äî handles mobile browser chrome) via `@supports`; `Shell.jsx` adds a defensive `overflow:hidden` on the shell column. The in-canvas measurement-grade scale bar (bottom-right, `lib/sheetFurniture.js`, shared with print/export) sits a fixed 40 px above the canvas bottom, so once the page can't scroll it is **always** visible ‚Äî no need to fork a second portal-mounted overlay (kept export parity; the owner's "bottom-left fixed overlay" was the suggested mechanism, the real need was "always visible," now met). **Self-verified headless at 1440√ó900 AND 1280√ó600:** `document.scrollHeight === innerHeight` (no page overflow) at both sizes, and the scale bar + north arrow render at the canvas bottom with both header rows visible simultaneously.
> **Dedup note:** distinct from completed **B144** (scale bar clipping/measurement-grade in print/export) ‚Äî this was on-screen viewport layout.

### B172 ‚Äî Module tabs read as inactive, not disabled `[global UI / Shell]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B172** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B167/B168 (#152, map items) and B169‚ÄìB171 (#153, basemap-blur trio), so this is the real next free ID after B171.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/optimistic-wozniak-4iltkx`). The inactive Schedule/Markup tabs were `rgba(255,255,255,0.30)` ‚Äî low-opacity, which both killed contrast (read as disabled) and muddied the glyphs (the "fuzzy / low-res" feel). New `ModuleTab` component in `AppHeader.jsx`: inactive tabs are **full-opacity `#c9c3b4`** (muted-but-legible, AA on the `#14110e` bar), the **module accent reveals on hover** (Site `#1D9E75`, Schedule `#7F77DD`, Markup `#EF9F27`), and the **active** tab keeps the accent text + 2 px underline. Icons are crisp fixed-13 px SVG with `shapeRendering:geometricPrecision` (no bitmap scaling). Inactive font-weight bumped 400‚Üí500 for legibility; `aria-current="page"` on the active tab. Browser-verified: Schedule/Markup clearly readable and obviously clickable next to the active Site tab.
### B170 ‚Äî Fix retina/HiDPI tile requests so the aerial basemap renders sharp `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; filed provisionally as B168, renumbered **B170** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (`claude/brave-galileo-wm8gti`) took B167 + B168 for unrelated map items, so this is the real next free ID; was gated on B169)*
`[x]` Gated on B169 (the diagnostic), which confirmed the dominant blur causes were **(a) HiDPI tiles never requested** and **(b) the planner's fractional zoom** ‚Äî so the source-swap fix path (B171/NEW-3) was correctly NOT triggered, since the imagery source isn't the problem.
> ‚úÖ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/awesome-darwin-7ui0qm`). Added **`detectRetina: true`** to **both** Esri World Imagery tile layers ‚Äî the map finder (`MapFinder.jsx`, `L.tileLayer(bm.tiles, ‚Ä¶)`) and the planner backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `GEO_BASEMAP`). On a HiDPI display (`devicePixelRatio > 1`) Leaflet now requests **one-zoom-higher native tiles and renders them at half size** (downsampled = crisp) instead of upscaling 1√ó tiles (= soft). This also sharpens the planner's *fractional* zoom (`zoomSnap:0`, driven by `ppfToZoom`) because it prefers downsampling a higher-zoom tile over upscaling a lower one. **Kept the Esri source** (per the NEW-2 constraint) and **did NOT touch the planner map's `zoomSnap:0`** ‚Äî snapping that map to integer zoom would desync the aerial from the feet-space SVG (the deliberate ppf‚Üízoom scale lock); `detectRetina` only changes which tiles are fetched + their display size, never the map's CRS zoom, so the lock is untouched. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (`gis-verify/retina-basemap-verify.mjs`, simulating `deviceScaleFactor` 1 vs 2 over a Katy parcel): at standard density the map requests **z11** tiles; at retina density it requests **z12** (one level higher = 2√ó pixel density), with **0 failed/gray tiles** at either density (no coverage regression) ‚Äî logged **VERIFICATION V43**. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **257 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. (The sharpness gain is invisible at the sandbox's `devicePixelRatio = 1`, so the *visible* improvement is best confirmed on Michael's own retina/4K display ‚Äî but the higher-density tile request is proven engaged.)

### B169 ‚Äî Diagnose basemap blur: retina/DPR vs. fractional zoom vs. source resolution `[Site Planner]` (task)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B167, renumbered **B169** ‚Äî concurrent `main` (`claude/brave-galileo-wm8gti`) took B167 + B168 for unrelated map items, so this is the real next free ID)*
`[x]` Diagnostic only ‚Äî instrument + report the root cause of soft aerial imagery **before** any provider change (the fix paths are B170 + B171).
> ‚úÖ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/awesome-darwin-7ui0qm`). Root cause established from the two tile-layer call sites (both the **Esri World Imagery** source, `server.arcgisonline.com/.../World_Imagery/MapServer/tile/{z}/{y}/{x}`) plus a live headless instrumentation:
> - **(a) Retina/HiDPI NOT requested ‚Äî CONFIRMED, primary.** Neither `L.tileLayer` set `detectRetina` (nor any `@2x` / `tileSize:512`): the map finder (`MapFinder.jsx:291`) and the planner backdrop (`SitePlanner.jsx:1043`) both fetched **1√ó tiles**, which the browser then **upscales** on any `devicePixelRatio > 1` display (most modern laptops / 4K monitors) ‚Üí soft. This is the most likely "it looks blurry on my screen" cause.
> - **(b) Fractional zoom ‚Äî CONFIRMED for the planner backdrop.** The planner map runs **`zoomSnap: 0`** (`SitePlanner.jsx:1031`) and its zoom is driven **continuously** from `ppfToZoom(view.ppf, lat)`, so the raster is almost always displayed at a **fractional** zoom = interpolated = blurred (independent of DPR). The map finder uses Leaflet's default integer zoom, so it's not affected by (b) ‚Äî only (a).
> - **(c) Genuinely low-res source ‚Äî RULED OUT as primary.** Esri World Imagery is **native to z19** (`maxNativeZoom: 19`, ~0.3 m/px) with good Houston-metro coverage; both layers merely *display* past native (21/24), so the only "source" softness is upscaling past z19 at very tight zoom ‚Äî not a stale/low-res source. Verified live (Katy parcel): tiles return **HTTP 200** with no gray/missing tiles at the working zooms.
> - **Live instrumentation:** `gis-verify/retina-basemap-verify.mjs` drove the headless map at `deviceScaleFactor` 1 vs 2 and recorded the **zoom level of every World_Imagery tile actually requested** + load status. Confirmed the pre-fix behavior (1√ó tiles, no DPR awareness) and gave the before/after baseline for B170.
> **Outcome ‚Üí fix routing:** causes (a)+(b) are real and fixable **without** changing the imagery source ‚Üí **B170** (add `detectRetina`, keep Esri, don't snap the planner's locked zoom). Cause (c) is not the issue, so **B171** (license-clean high-res source evaluation) stays **gated** ‚Äî only revisit if B170 proves insufficient by eye on a real retina display. lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green (no app-code change in this diagnostic item beyond the verify harness).

`[x]` Done 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/brave-galileo-wm8gti`). ### B166 ‚Äî Geometry check reads wrong county acreage (homesite carve-out, not total) `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; minted B166)*
`[x]` **Repro (owner-reported):** parcel `0440110000065` ‚Äî Appraisal panel + drawn boundary agree (17.00 AC vs 17.06 ac) but the geometry check screamed **"county 0.50 ac vs 17.06 ac (3,312% off)."** The 0.50 ac was the **HOMESITE carve-out** (Legal: "PT TR 4D (HOMESITE)"), not the total tract.
> ‚úÖ **Done 2026-06-19** (branch `claude/busy-carson-1zuiuq`). Confirmed root cause against the **live HCAD parcels layer** field list: the record carries **both** `Acreage` (total) **and** `acreage_1` (a sub-acreage) ‚Äî both match the acres regex, and `countyAcres()` used `keys.find(...)` which returned whichever came first (the homesite ~0.50). Fix in `SitePlanner.jsx` `countyAcres()`: collect **all** acreage-named fields, drop any whose name marks it a sub-acreage (`home_site|homestead|hs_|hmst|exempt|imprv|improv`), and take the **MAX** of what remains ‚Äî the total tract is always the largest, so a homesite/ag/exemption carve-out can never win. County-agnostic (fixes the statewide carve-out pattern, not just this parcel). Distinct root cause from B75 (that was a m¬≤-vs-acres unit misread; the TxGIO unit handling is untouched). lint 0 errors ¬∑ 257 tests ¬∑ build green.

### B157 ‚Äî Added-detention area label seats on the NEW ground, not the whole-pond centre `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived 2026-06-18 in chat ‚Äî owner: when expanding an existing pond, show the added surface area + acreage at the centre of mass of the NEW area, because the whole-pond centroid often stays inside the existing basin. Refinement of B139/B140; filed provisionally as B151, renumbered **B157** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B150‚ÄìB156 (easement tool, multipart-parcel + Delete-key bugs, markup hit-testing), so this is the real next free ID.)*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-18 (branch `claude/brave-noether-rwzkqk`). B140 stacked the "+added" increment as a third line on the pond's single centred label, so on a one-sided (or uniform) expansion the added figure floated over the EXISTING basin ‚Äî the exact case the owner flagged, where the whole-pond centroid stays inside the old pond. Now the added detention area gets its OWN on-map label, seated on the **thickest part of the new ground**:
- **New `lib/pondGeom.js` (`addedAreaLabelPoint`, unit-tested):** the pole-of-inaccessibility of (expanded footprint ‚àí baseline footprint) via a coarse grid + local refine ‚Äî the interior point of the new area farthest from any edge. Handles a one-sided strip (lands mid-strip), a uniform "push banks out" ring (lands in the band, never the centre), and a corner push; returns null on no-expansion / pure shrink / degenerate ring. Pure world-feet geometry (no React/DOM), so it unit-tests without a browser.
- **Label (`SitePlanner.jsx` element-label builder):** in expansion mode the centred label reads **"Existing Detention Pond"** + the existing area, re-anchored over the **existing basin** (baseline centroid); a second label titled **"Additional Detention"** + `"+X.XX ac ¬∑ +Y sf"` is pushed at the added-region point (owner wording, 2026-06-18). A plain (non-expansion) pond label is unchanged ("Detention Pond" + area). The added area is the **footprint / top-down** area (the metric behind the owner's "20‚Äì25 % of the site" pond-coverage rule ‚Äî NOT water-surface). Both ride B121's existing LOD/collision pool via a per-label id (`<id>` / `<id>#add`) ‚Äî no parallel renderer. A net shrink / sub-`POND_ADD_MIN_SF` (50 sf) change falls back to the inline "+/‚àí" increment so the delta still shows.
- **Verified (self, headless Chromium, logged-out preview build, 2026-06-18):** seeded a one-sided expansion + a concentric expansion; the existing-area label seats over the old basin and the "+added" label seats over the new ground (one-sided: to the right of the basin; concentric: out on the new ring, 183 px off the centre that sits inside the old pond), correct sf/ac, **zero console/page errors**. Re-verified after the owner wording change ‚Äî labels read **"Existing Detention Pond"** and **"Additional Detention"** with the +ac/sf in place. lint **0 errors** (14 pre-existing warnings) ¬∑ **257 tests** (6 in `test/pondGeom.test.js`) ¬∑ build green ¬∑ `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. Browser pass ‚Üí **VERIFICATION V42**.
> Refines **B140** (stays Done as the acres+sf label); builds on **B139**'s `det.baseline`. No `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump ‚Äî reads the existing persisted baseline, adds no field.

### B154 ‚Äî Delete key intermittently needs two presses to remove a selected element `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; filed provisionally as B151, renumbered **B154** ‚Äî concurrent `main` took B150‚ÄìB153 (easement tool) plus a second B151 (multipart parcel), so this is the real next free ID; the implementing commit references the bug as NEW-1)*
`[x]` Repro: click an element to select it, press Delete ‚Äî sometimes it deletes on the first press, sometimes it takes two ("works when I was already on the canvas; fails when I came from a panel/button first"). **Root cause (confirmed, but NOT the report's first guess):** the keydown handler is **already** `window`-level ‚Äî so it isn't a focus-scope problem. The real cause is a **stale closure via passive-effect re-binding:** `onKey` is created inside a `useEffect`, and although `sel`/`multi` are in its deps, the effect re-binds the listener **after** the commit/paint. A Delete pressed in the brief window right after a selecting click runs the *previously* bound `onKey`, which closed over the old `sel` (often `null`) ‚Üí the guard `(sel || multi.length)` was false ‚Üí no-op, no `preventDefault`; the next press (listener now re-bound) works. Under a heavy render (this is a ~6k-line component) the window widens enough to be hit intermittently.
> ‚úÖ **Done 2026-06-18** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`). Added live `selRef`/`multiRef` mirrors (synced during render ‚Äî a passive effect would lag the same window) and made the **Delete/Backspace branch read the refs**, and `deleteSel` read `selRef.current`/`multiRef.current`, so deletion always acts on the *current* selection no matter which listener instance fired ‚Äî no second press. The handler stayed `window`-level (no scope change). Also **hardened the existing typing guard** ‚Äî it already bailed when `document.activeElement` is INPUT/SELECT/TEXTAREA (so Delete never nuked canvas elements while editing a field); extended it to **`contentEditable`** too. The lone same-tick `setSel(x); deleteSel()` caller (the element context-menu Delete) is unaffected ‚Äî the element is already selected when that menu opens, so the ref holds it. lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **230 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (built app): (A) select an element ‚Üí one Delete removes it (2‚Üí1); (B) touch a tool/panel button, then select an element, then a **single immediate** Delete still removes exactly one ‚Äî the reported flow, now first-press reliable; zero console errors. Logged as **VERIFICATION V40**.

### B150 ‚Äî Easement drawing tool (core): first-class Easement object, input modes, attributes, editing, render, persistence `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; minted B150 ‚Äî next free ID after B149)*
`[x]` New first-class **Easement** object on the editable layer (immutable-backdrop model preserved): a `markups[]` entry `kind:"easement"` with a stable UUID and a display label derived from type + width (cosmetic, editable override). **Mode A ‚Äî Centerline + width:** digitize a polyline centerline, enter total width ‚Üí strip generated by offsetting the centerline ¬±width/2 with flat end caps; width is editable after creation and re-offsets the strip live. **Mode B ‚Äî Boundary polygon:** draw a closed ring directly. Attributes panel (Element tab): type (Utility/PUE, Sanitary Sewer, Storm/Drainage, Water, Pipeline, Access/Ingress-Egress, Aerial/Overhead, Temporary Construction, Other), holder/beneficiary, width (auto-filled in mode A), recording reference, exclusive (y/n), status (existing/proposed), restrictsBuildings (default true), restrictsPaving (default false), notes. Editing: draggable centerline/polygon vertices (Ôºã add, Shift-click delete), move, delete, relabel; reuses the existing snap system + persistent toggle. Rendering: semi-transparent hatched fill color-coded by type, centerline shown for strip easements, proposed rendered dashed; per-easement area readout + total encumbered area in Yield. Persistence: Supabase, editable layer, private by default, RLS-protected.
> ‚úÖ **Done (branch `claude/clever-franklin-7ds6kg`).** **Engine:** inspected the codebase first per the gate ‚Äî an offset/buffer utility already existed (`bufferPolyline` in `lib/metesAndBounds.js`), so **no JSTS added**. Generalized it to be asymmetric-ready (`{leftW,rightW}`, default still symmetric ¬±w/2) so a future asymmetric-strip UI needs no geometry rework, and factored out a shared one-sided `offsetPolyline` primitive. **Domain logic** in new `lib/easements.js` (`EASEMENT_TYPES`, `easementLabel`, per-mode `deriveEasementRing`, `easementArea`). The **type dropdown uses the shared portal `AnchoredMenu`** so it can't render behind the rail/zoom rail. Easement is a markup ‚Üí persists through the existing markups[] save path (Supabase, private, RLS) with no schema change. New rail "Easement" section (mode + default width/type via the portal menu). Self-verified in a headless browser (centerline + boundary draw, attributes panel auto-opens, portal type dropdown swaps type + relabels, vertex grips). **246 tests pass** (16 new in `test/easements.test.js`); lint 0 errors; build green.

### B147 ‚Äî Markup/shape tools: Bluebeam-style editing (rotate + resize boxes, vertex-edit lines/polylines/polygons) `[Site Planner]` (feature)  *(arrived 2026-06-17 in chat: "fix the rectangle and markup tools ‚Ä¶ make them more like bluebeam, not being able to rotate a rectangle is wild"; minted B147 ‚Äî next free after B146)*
`[x]` The neutral markup shapes (drawn with the Line / Rectangle / Ellipse / Polygon / Polyline tools) could only be **moved, restyled, or deleted** ‚Äî selecting one just recoloured it, with **no handles**. You couldn't rotate or resize a rectangle/ellipse, or reshape a line/polyline/polygon. Meanwhile elements have resize/rotate grips and measures/parcels have vertex editing, so markups were the odd one out. **Owner's headline: "not being able to rotate a rectangle is wild."**
> ‚úÖ **Done 2026-06-17** (branch `claude/gallant-lovelace-82konu`). Added Bluebeam-style geometry editing to the markups[] layer, **reusing the existing element/measure transform machinery** (no parallel system):
> - **Rect / ellipse:** on select (Select tool), 4 corner + 4 edge **resize grips** + a **rotate handle** above the top edge ‚Äî mirrors the element handles. Resize is computed in the shape's own rotated frame (opposite side stays fixed); rotate spins about the centre, snapping to 15¬∞ when Snap is on, free (whole degrees) when off. The `rot` field already existed on rect/ellipse (rendered via `transform=rotate`), so this is purely the missing UI. New `mkResize`/`mkRotate` drag modes + `startMarkupResize`/`startMarkupRotate`.
> - **Line / polyline / polygon:** draggable **vertex dots**; **Ôºã** on edge midpoints (polyline/polygon) to insert a point; **Shift-click** a dot to delete one (keeps the kind's minimum ‚Äî 2 for line/polyline, 3 for polygon). New `mkVertex` drag mode + `startMarkupVertex`/`addMarkupVertex`, mirroring the measure-vertex handlers (B141). Shared helpers `mkPts`/`setMkPts` normalise line `{a,b}` ‚Üî point arrays.
> - **Properties panel:** rect/ellipse gain numeric **Width / Height** and **Rotation¬∞** fields (precise entry; kept out of `mkStyle` via a separate `setSelMarkupGeom` so new shapes don't inherit a past size/angle), plus a one-line editing hint per shape.
> - **Scope:** only the 5 neutral annotation kinds get grips; **semantic markups stay move-only** (utilRoute / traced / infwater / encumbrance carry derived geometry ‚Äî corridor/pad/centerline/calls ‚Äî that hand-editing would desync). Locked markups show no grips.
> lint **0 errors** ¬∑ **225 tests** ¬∑ build green; `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified in a real headless browser** (drove the built app): drew a rectangle ‚Üí corner+edge grips + rotate handle appear ‚Üí dragged a corner (300‚Üí410 px) and the rotate handle (rotate(0)‚Üírotate(53)); drew a 3-point polyline ‚Üí 3 vertex grips + 2 Ôºã handles ‚Üí dragged the middle vertex and the path updated; zero errors from the change. ### B143 ‚Äî Text box edits like Bluebeam: Enter = newline, click away / Esc to finish `[Site Planner]` (bug) ‚Äî follow-up to B142

Two causes, both fixed to match Bluebeam's Text Box markup (researched against the Bluebeam Revu docs ‚Äî "finish by selecting away or pressing Esc"; a text box is multi-line):
- **Click-out was trapped at ANY distance:** the canvas pointerdown `preventDefault`s the textarea blur, so `onBlur`‚Üí`commitEditCallout` never fired and you stayed in the editor even clicking 400 px away. Fix: a full-canvas transparent catcher rendered under the inline editor (`pointerEvents:"all"`, commits on pointerdown) ‚Äî clicking anywhere outside the box now finishes it.
- **Enter committed (single-line behavior):** Enter now inserts a **newline**; you finish by clicking away or Esc (Esc keeps the text). Placeholder updated to "Type; click away or Esc to finish".
- Empty box is still removed when you click away without typing (matches Bluebeam).
- Verified live (headless): Enter ‚Üí "Line1\nLine2" (still editing); click away +80 px ‚Üí finishes + commits two lines; Esc ‚Üí finishes keeping the text; empty box removed on click-away; zero console errors. lint 0 errors ¬∑ build green ¬∑ tests pass. Browser pass ‚Üí **VERIFICATION V33**.

### B132 ‚Äî Detention pond expansion: lock an existing pond as a baseline, then read the storage gained `[Site Planner]` (feature)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-17 (branch `claude/practical-noether-ln1f46`). Owner workflow: trace an existing on-site detention pond, lock it as the baseline, then enlarge it (drag banks out and/or deepen) to read the **added detention** in acre-feet. Built entirely on the existing pond machinery ‚Äî no parallel store, no new schema bump.
- **Panel** (`SitePlanner.jsx`, pond branch of the selected-element inspector): the **Detention storage** section gains a **"Lock as existing pond"** button. Locking snapshots the current footprint ring (world feet: `selEl.points` or `elCorners`) **plus its own depth/freeboard/slope** into `el.det.baseline`, so the comparison is frozen and apples-to-apples. Once locked, an **"Expansion vs. existing"** box shows **Existing** / **Proposed** storage and a live **"Storage gained +X.XX ac-ft"** (green) ‚Äî or **"Storage lost"** (red) when shrunk below baseline ‚Äî plus the cubic-feet delta. **Clear** removes the baseline (keeps depth/freeboard/slope).
- **Increase = `detentionStorage(proposed) ‚àí detentionStorage(baseline)`** ‚Äî the *same* prismoidal/taper function for both sides, so the delta can't drift from a method mismatch. Reflects both footprint growth and any depth/slope change.
- **Canvas ghost** (`renderElPx`): the locked baseline ring draws as a faint **dashed outline** under the pond so the expansion is visible. Handled for both the irregular-polygon branch (drawn in world feet directly) and the rotated-rectangle branch (a counter-rotated `<g>` undoes the element's `rotate(el.rot)` so the world-feet ghost lands true). `pointerEvents:none` so it never interferes with selection/drag.
- **Persistence:** `baseline` rides inside the already-persisted `el.det` (additive, lossless) ‚Äî survives save/reload, no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump. Honest framing kept: "screening only ‚Äî confirm with your civil engineer."
- **Scope (owner-chosen):** "just the increase." Deliberately **excluded** for now (offered, declined): a required-vs-provided "is it enough?" check against added impervious, and a solver ("grow this much to hit a target"). Easy follow-ons if wanted.
- **Verified:** lint 0 errors (14 pre-existing warnings, none in new code) ¬∑ **191 tests pass** ¬∑ build green ¬∑ lazy-chunk split intact (`SitePlannerApp` own chunk). Browser click-through logged as **V25** in `VERIFICATION.md`.

### B122 ‚Äî Auto-number buildings with contiguous renumber-on-delete `[Site Planner]` (feature)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/determined-brown-bf86l7`). Each standalone building now shows a sequential **"Building N"** label, numbered by placement order and contiguous (1‚Ä¶N) at all times. Deliberately **render-derived, not stored**:

- **Identity unchanged + safe:** the "stable internal ID, separate from the number" requirement was already met ‚Äî every element has a persisted, collision-seeded `el.id` (`uid()` + `ensureIdAbove` on load), and every cross-reference (`attachedTo` for parking/trailers/dog-ears) already binds to `el.id`, never a display number. So a renumber can't silently re-point anything. No schema change, no migration, no `SITE_MODEL_VERSION` bump.

### B119 ‚Äî Parking orientation flipped: first bay must sit against the building `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1")*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/youthful-heisenberg-9w64n4`). **Root cause:** `addParkingRowSide` created building-attached parking with `cfg:{ flipDepth:true }`. The strip's inner (local `y=0`) edge sits against the wall, and `flipDepth` mirrors `carStalls`'s layout so the **drive aisle** landed on that inner edge ‚Äî i.e. the aisle hugged the building and stalls were pushed outward (the inverse of the spec). **Fix (one line):** drop `flipDepth` for building-attached parking. `carStalls` now lays the first stall row at the building edge with the drive aisle outboard, and `growParking` already grows on the away-from-host edge ‚Äî so the field grows **outward, away from the building**, exactly as specced. The per-field "Drive aisle on the far side" toggle (B59) still flips it by choice; existing saved parking keeps its stored `cfg` (only newly-added side parking changes). Lint 0-errors, 152 tests pass, build green. Browser-confirm logged as **V17** in `VERIFICATION.md`.

It only *looked* wrong because of **B119**'s flipped orientation: the numerically-correct steps grew toward/into the building. ### B128 ‚Äî Split tool: correctly cut concave parcels (general multi-piece straight cut) `[Site Planner]` (bug ‚Üí enhancement)  *(minted B127 on-branch; renumbered B128 after `main`'s #85 concurrently took B127 for the rail/header dropdown fix ‚Äî the implementing commit still says "B127")*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-17 (branch `claude/inspiring-gates-qrhziq`). Closes the QA marathon's last "substantive bug still present" hand-off and supersedes the long-deferred **B31**.
- **The data-corruption fear was already mitigated, and that was verified, not assumed.** The hand-off carried an `[S2/HIGH]` "Split corrupts area on concave parcels ‚Äî saved silently, no error." That premise was **stale** (written against pre-#48 code): `performSplit` already had a concave-cut **backstop guard** (area-conservation + per-piece self-intersection check, from the B74‚ÄìB92 batch) that *refuses* a bad cut with a warning instead of saving corrupted geometry. Confirmed by replicating the live `splitPolygon` + guard and fuzzing **320k random concave cuts** (combs/L/U/stars) against a Monte-Carlo point-membership oracle: **zero** wrong splits slipped past the guard; every 4/6/8/10/12-crossing cut was rejected. So there was no silent `siteSqft`/FAR/coverage corruption to fix.
- **The real remaining gap was capability, not safety.** Because the old `splitPolygon` only paired the two extreme-`t` crossings, a straight cut that crosses a concave lot **4+ times** (which honestly yields **k+1** pieces for `2k` crossings ‚Äî e.g. 3 for a U cut across both prongs) could only ever produce 2 overlapping/omitting "halves," so the guard always **refused** it. Net user-visible behavior: "the Split tool won't cut an L/U/notched lot through its reentrant part."
- **Fix ‚Äî a correct general slice.** Extracted the parcel-split geometry out of `SitePlanner.jsx` into a new pure, tested module **`lib/polygonSplit.js`**: `splitPolygonByLine(points,A,B)` classifies each vertex to a binary side (guarantees an even crossing count ‚Äî no odd-parity tangency bug), inserts a crossing node on every sign-change edge, **pairs ALL crossings even‚Äìodd along the cut line** (each pair is an interior chord), and traces every resulting piece (walk a boundary arc ‚Üí hop the interior chord to its partner ‚Üí continue), dropping zero-area slivers. Returns the natural set of pieces (`>=2`) or `null`. The bent-polyline cut moved over too as `splitPolygonByPath` (unchanged logic). `performSplit` now replaces the one parcel with **N** parcels and keeps the area/self-intersection guard as a backstop, so the result can never be worse than before (a rare near-vertex-grazing degenerate sliver still self-intersects ‚Üí still refused).
- **UX change to note:** a straight cut through a notched lot now creates **all** the real pieces (e.g. 3 parcels for a U-shaped lot), instead of declining. Convex and 2-crossing concave cuts are byte-for-byte the same two pieces as before.
- **Validation:** new `test/polygonSplit.test.js` (11 cases: convex halving, L 2-crossing, **U ‚Üí 3 pieces with exact areas + membership**, 3-tooth comb ‚Üí 4 pieces, line-misses/degenerate ‚Üí null, bent-path cut, and a 1,500-cut randomized area+membership property check). Standalone prototype passed the 300k-trial oracle (0 area / 0 membership failures; ~0.003% near-degenerate self-int ‚Üí safely refused). Full suite **163 tests** (was 152, +11) ¬∑ lint **0 errors** ¬∑ build green ¬∑ lazy-chunk split intact. Owner approved shipping; merged to `main` via PR.

### B116 ‚Äî Measurement tools (Length / Polylength / Area) in Site Planner `[Site Planner]` (feature ‚Üí already implemented)  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; committed provisionally as B115 ‚Äî renumbered B116 after main's #72 took B115 for "revisit keyboard shortcuts")*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/youthful-heisenberg-9w64n4`). **Dedupe outcome: already implemented ‚Äî this is the "the app already had them" case the PHASE E spec and this very task anticipated.** Site Planner's `measure` tool already ships all three calibration-aware modes; nothing was rebuilt. Evidence in `SitePlanner.jsx`:
- **All three modes present + surfaced:** the **Measure** rail button + `‚ñæ` mode menu (Length / Polylength / Area) ‚Äî `measureMode` state persisted to `localStorage` (`planarfit:measureMode`); two-click **Length**, running-path **Polylength** (accumulate points), closed-polygon **Area** (click the first dot or double-click to close). Click handling, `finishMeasure`, `selectMeasure`, delete, and the in-progress draft preview all exist and work.
- **Area label already matches the spec exactly:** renders `"<sf> sf ¬∑ <ac> ac ¬∑ <perim>‚Ä≤ perim"` (e.g. `12,300 sf ¬∑ 0.28 ac ¬∑ 462‚Ä≤ perim`) ‚Äî perimeter closes the loop; Length/Polylength label the running feet.
- **Calibration-aware, as specced:** labels read from `calibrationState`; when an underlay is `uncalibrated` they render **amber (`#b45309`) with a `‚öÝ`** and the rail shows the **"Underlay isn't calibrated ‚Äî distances may be wrong"** banner (same behavior as Document Review / PHASE E). A drawn/georef/calibrated plan labels in the normal accent.
- **Own editable layer; export behavior consistent:** measurements live in their own `measures[]` layer (migrated `{a,b}`‚Üí`{mode,pts}`), persisted in the Site Model. They export alongside callouts/markups ‚Äî consistent with the existing annotation architecture (the only `data-export="skip"` users are transient chrome: grid, basemap, scale bar, north arrow, zoom/layers UI, draft previews). Reuse note: the Document Review takeoff math (`takeoff.js`) and the Site Planner helpers (`polyArea`/`centroid`/`pathLen`) compute the same geometry ‚Äî doc-review in page-units√ócalibration, the planner natively in feet (the shared EPSG:2278 spine) ‚Äî so no port was needed.
- **Finish UX:** double-click **or Enter** commits (shared `finishActiveDrawing`, per B103); **Esc cancels** the draft. The task floated "Esc to end" ‚Äî deliberately **not** adopted, since Esc-cancels-the-draft is the universal convention used by every other multi-point tool in the app; double-click/Enter already satisfy "click points ‚Üí end".
- **Only change made (label alignment):** the mode display names were **Line / Polyline / Area**; renamed to **Length / Polylength / Area** ‚Äî Bluebeam's own terms (Planyr is "Bluebeam-style") and the names this task uses, which also **disambiguates the measurement from the markup "Polyline" tool** (`mpolyline`, ‚áßN) that shared the word. Label-only via a module-level `MEASURE_MODES`/`measureModeLabel`; the internal `measureMode` values (`line`/`polyline`/`area`) are untouched, so `localStorage` and all logic are unaffected. Lint 0-errors, 138 tests pass, build green. Browser click-through logged as **V12** in `VERIFICATION.md`.

### B114 ‚Äî Snapping always on; can't be suppressed during a drag `[Site Planner]` (bug)  *(arrived as "NEW-1")*
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/epic-dirac-3ljl49`). Dragging an element (e.g. a road) near a neighbour flush-snapped it to that neighbour's edge with no per-move escape, so you couldn't drop it at a deliberate offset (a 15-ft buffer behind trailer parking). Root cause: the existing "Alt-drop to place free" only skipped the *bond* at drop (`onUp`'s `!e.altKey` guard); the element had already been moved to the flush-snapped position during `onMove`, so Alt never placed it freely ‚Äî and there was no keyboard toggle. Fix:
- **Hold-to-suppress (the standard CAD pattern):** a new `altSnapOffRef`, re-armed from `e.altKey` on every `onBgDown`/`onMove`, makes the live snap = `settings.snap && !altSnapOffRef.current`. `snap()`/`snapPt()` read it (so grid snap, draw, vertex, and placement all honour Alt), and a per-frame `snapOn` gates the inline paths the core helper doesn't cover ‚Äî the ambient neighbour flush-snap (`edgeSnapCenter`), resize/edge-resize-to-grid, and rotate-to-15¬∞. Holding Alt bypasses ALL of them for that one move and re-enables on release. Shift-drag (deliberate align+bond) is unaffected.
- **Toggle + shortcut + default OFF:** the toolbar button stays, plus a new **S** shortcut and the Site-defaults checkbox toggle snap; "off" fully disables every snap path above. Per owner request snap now **defaults OFF (free movement)** and is a **global drafting preference** (a tool mode), not a per-site attribute: it lives in `localStorage` (`planarfit:snap`, default off) via `loadSnapPref`/`saveSnapPref`/`setSnap`, seeded at the settings `useState` and preserved across JSON import, so the per-site saved `snap` is ignored on load (every existing site started free, regardless of its baked-in `snap:true`). Turning it on persists across sites/reloads until turned off. (`settings.snap` is still the field every read site uses ‚Äî it just mirrors the pref now.)
- **Visible state:** the toolbar pill now reads `Snap 10‚Ä≤` ‚Üî `Snap off` (green/grey dot, `aria-pressed`), the Site-defaults checkbox is relabeled "Snap to grid & neighbours (S)", the Select-tool hint says "hold Alt to bypass snap & place freely ‚Ä¢ toggle snap with S", and the shortcuts panel gains `S ‚Üí Toggle snap` and `Alt drag ‚Üí Bypass snap`. Build green; lazy-chunk split intact. **Browser-verify** logged in VERIFICATION.md.

### B101 ‚Äî Remove the element-type color legend from the Setup/defaults page `[Site Planner / Setup]` (task)
`[x]` Done 2026-06-16 (branch `claude/blissful-babbage-liboyn`; filed provisionally as B93). ### B6 ‚Äî Auto-parking returns wrong dimension after sidewalk resize + delete `[Site Planner]` (bug)
`[x]` Repro: place building ‚Üí add 30-ft sidewalk ‚Üí parking within sidewalk ‚Üí expand sidewalk to 30 ft ‚Üí delete parking ‚Üí click "add parking" ‚Üí tool produced a ~135-ft parking field. Expected: "add parking" drops a **fixed-depth** field every time, regardless of surrounding geometry. Fixed depth is the spec, so the bug is that **something overrides the depth constant with a measured value**. Trace where the parking field's depth is assigned; confirm it can't be contaminated by adjacent or just-deleted geometry (the resized sidewalk and the gap left by the deleted parking are prime suspects).
> Done 2026-06-14 (PR #10). `addParkingRowSide` now offsets by the sidewalk's true *thickness* (`swThick`, which resolves the correct axis) instead of a raw `w`/`h` read that could pick up the sidewalk's *run* (~wall length); the row depth stays the fixed `stallDepth + aisle` constant and can't be contaminated by adjacent or just-deleted geometry.

### B7 ‚Äî Project lifecycle status on map markers `[Site Planner / map]` (feature)
`[x]` Right-click a project marker to set its status. Lifecycle: **Pursuit ‚Üí Active ‚Üí On Hold ‚Üí Complete ‚Üí Dead** (see B8 for the full state set and visuals). Core of this item:
- Right-click marker ‚Üí menu of states, current one checked. Mirror the same control in the project detail panel if one exists.
- **Status is a real field** on the project record in Supabase ‚Äî persists across devices, stays private per the existing row-level security (each user sees only their own).
- **New projects default to Pursuit.**
- Companion features: **filter by status** (toggle each state on/off ‚Äî "hide Complete" and "hide Dead" will be the common ones), a **legend**, and **pipeline counts** (e.g., "4 Pursuit ¬∑ 6 Active ¬∑ 2 On Hold ¬∑ 11 Complete ¬∑ 5 Dead").
> Done 2026-06-14 (this PR ‚Äî B7‚ÄìB12 batch). `status` added to the Site Model (`SITE_MODEL_VERSION` 2‚Üí3; new sites default to "pursuit"; pre-feature records migrate to "active"), exposed via a `statusOf` selector with ordered `STATUSES` + `STATUS_META`. It persists inside the model `data` ‚Äî i.e. the `sites.data` jsonb in Supabase, so it syncs across devices and stays private under the existing RLS, with **no DB migration / no dedicated column**. Set a site's status by right-clicking its map marker **or** a saved-sites list row (current state checked); applied to the whole site group. Companion legend + per-state show/hide filters + live pipeline counts live in the saved-sites panel.

### B8 ‚Äî Lifecycle states & marker visuals `[Site Planner / map]` (feature)
`[x]` The five states and how each marker reads. Use two redundant cues ‚Äî **color + shape/glyph** ‚Äî so status stays legible for colorblind users and on a busy basemap:
- **Pursuit** ‚Äî amber, dashed ring (tentative, uncommitted).
- **Active** ‚Äî green, solid (the live work; should grab the eye).
- **On Hold** ‚Äî slate/indigo blue, solid ring, pause "‚Äñ" glyph (alive but paused; revivable). Lean slate/indigo rather than sky-blue so it doesn't vanish over blue water on the basemap.
- **Complete** ‚Äî gray, muted, small check ‚úì (done; recedes).
- **Dead** ‚Äî hollow gray, dimmest, faint ‚úï, no fill (didn't proceed; kept for the record). **Not red** ‚Äî red reads as urgent/alert; a dead deal is inert.
- Live (green) should pop; both Complete and Dead recede into the background, with shape/glyph telling them apart.
> Done 2026-06-14 (this PR ‚Äî B7‚ÄìB12 batch). Markers carry two redundant cues exactly per spec: Pursuit amber/dashed-ring, Active green/solid (pops), On Hold slate-indigo/pause-‚Äñ, Complete gray/muted-check-‚úì (recedes), Dead hollow-gray/faint-‚úï/no-fill (recedes; not red). Glyph distinguishes Complete from Dead.

### B10 ‚Äî Consolidate the two header rows into one bar with a module switcher `[global UI]` (feature)
`[x]` The Site Planner currently stacks **two** header rows that repeat information: row 1 is `Planyr | Site Planner | Document Review` (top-level module tabs); row 2 is `‚Äπ Map | Site Planyr | Houston ColdPort ‚ñæ ‚Ä∫ Plan 1 ‚ñæ | undo/redo | Snap 10' | Saved ‚úì | File ‚ñæ`. The brand and the active module name both appear twice.
- **Collapse to a single top bar.** Switch modules via a **product-switcher dropdown** ‚Äî the standard multi-product pattern (think Atlassian/Google Workspace): brand logo + current module name on the far left with a chevron; clicking it reveals the other modules (Site Planner, Document Review, and later Project Scheduling, Cost Estimating). This replaces the row of flat tabs.
- **Recommended one-row layout:** `[‚ñæ Planyr ¬∑ Site Planyr]  ‚Äπ Map ‚Ä∫ Houston ColdPort ‚ñæ ‚Ä∫ Plan 1 ‚ñæ   ¬∑   [undo] [redo] [fit] ¬∑ Snap 10' ¬∑ Saved/Cloud ‚úì ¬∑ [account] ¬∑ File ‚ñæ`. (Map ‚Üí Project ‚Üí Plan reads as a breadcrumb ‚Äî the trail showing where you are in the hierarchy.)
- Honor **B3** spelling here: row 1 still shows the old "Site Planner" ‚Äî the rebuilt bar must use **Planyr / Site Planyr**.
- Removing the county selector (see **B11**) frees additional header space, reinforcing this consolidation.
> Done 2026-06-14 (this PR ‚Äî B7‚ÄìB12 batch). The shell's flat module tabs are now a **product-switcher dropdown** (brand + current module + chevron ‚Üí menu built from the `WORKSPACES` registry, active one marked); the duplicated brand/module mark was removed from the planner header so brand/module appears exactly once. Global account control unchanged. Note: the shell bar and the planner context bar remain two physical rows ‚Äî the dedup + switcher are the substance of B10; a single physical row is a later polish.

### B11 ‚Äî Remove the county pre-selection gate; click anywhere, auto-resolve the county `[Site Planner / map]` (feature)
`[x]` Today the user must pick a county (e.g., Harris vs. Fort Bend) *before* clicking a parcel. Remove that gate ‚Äî the user should be able to pan/click **anywhere** and select any parcel without choosing a county first; the unnecessary upfront choice just adds friction.
- Parcel geometry is published per **county appraisal district (CAD)** ‚Äî the county agency that maintains the parcel map and ownership data (Harris County Appraisal District, Fort Bend Central Appraisal District, etc.). So "click anywhere" means the backend must **resolve which county the clicked point falls in** (point-in-county lookup) and route the parcel query to that county's CAD service automatically.
- Handle the **county-boundary case** gracefully (a click near a line, or a multi-parcel selection that straddles two counties ‚Üí query both services and merge results).
- This also removes the county dropdown from the header, feeding **B10**.
> Done 2026-06-14 (this PR ‚Äî B7‚ÄìB12 batch). County gate removed. The map resolves every configured CAD county's parcel layer up front; a click is auto-routed via `candidateCountiesForPoint` (coarse per-county bbox pre-filter, padded so borders overlap ‚Üí a straddle click queries both) + `identifyParcelAcross` (parallel point-identify across candidates, first hit wins, a down county is skipped not fatal, no match fails gracefully ‚Äî no parcel, no crash). The selected parcel's resolved county rides into the planner hand-off so the saved site still records its county. The county dropdown is gone from the map header. **Interim:** the Layers panel defaults to the Harris/Houston jurisdiction (same as the prior app default) so the Houston utility overlays stay available with no county picked ‚Äî per-area jurisdiction resolution is a future refinement.

The current wording doesn't communicate that.

Candidates, depending on exactly what it does: **"New Site,"** **"Start New,"** **"Import & Edit,"** **"Drop a Survey,"** or **"New Plan."** If it's specifically the *alternative* to selecting existing parcels (start from a survey/blank instead), **"Start Blank"** or **"Start from Survey"** fit.
- **`[?]` resolved:** the control was confirmed to be the map's **"Skip ‚Äî blank canvas"** button, which opens an empty (un-located) planner ‚Äî it does NOT import a survey today.

Behavior unchanged (opens an empty planner; no survey-import was added ‚Äî that would be a separate, larger item if wanted).

### B14 ‚Äî Document Review project library: link reviews/files to Projects + browseable folders `[Document Review]` (feature)
`[x]` Link saved Document Review reviews/files to the existing **Project/Site** records (the entity that anchors Site Planner plans, e.g. "Houston ColdPort") and give them a browseable folder structure. Browser-only + existing Supabase.
- **Lifecycle status** reused from the Site Model (pursuit/active/onhold/complete/dead ‚Äî already shipped in B7/B8); files stay attached regardless of status.
- Each review/file carries a **project link, discipline** (Survey / Civil / Architectural / Landscape / Environmental / CAD / Geotech / Other), **item/type, revision, and date**; the name defaults to **"\<Project\> - \<Item\> - YYYY.MM.DD"** (each piece editable).

- **File-explorer drawer:** project (+ status badge, editable) ‚Üí discipline folder ‚Üí files newest-first ‚Üí click to open in the viewer/stitcher; **drag-drop** a PDF onto a project or discipline to file it.

New `doc_reviews` index columns (`project_id`/`item`/`revision`/`doc_date`) + a `ProjectLibrary` drawer + a project/discipline filing UI in the Reviews menu, all in the doc-review workspace. Projects + their lifecycle status are read from (and written back to) the Site Planner `sites` ‚Äî one source of truth, no parallel store. Status is NOT re-added (it already exists per B7/B8). Migration `src/workspaces/doc-review/db/project_library.sql`. `upsertReview`/`listReviews` fall back to the core columns if that migration hasn't run yet, so saving never regresses.

### B66 ‚Äî Top-left Site Planyr dropdown renders behind the lower header row `[global UI]` (bug)
`[x]` Clicking the top-left module (product) switcher opened its dropdown *behind* the planner's context bar / map header, so it couldn't be used. Root cause: the Shell `<header>` (which holds the dropdown) and `<main>` (which holds the workspace) were siblings, neither establishing a stacking context, so the dropdown menu (`zIndex:50`) competed in the **root** stacking context against the planner context bar (`SitePlanner.jsx`, `zIndex:60`) and the map header (`MapFinder.jsx`, `zIndex:1000`) ‚Äî and lost.
> Done 2026-06-15 (branch `site-planner/b64-b66-runtime-ui-fixes`). Fixed in `src/app/Shell.jsx`: `<main>` now establishes a stacking-context floor (`position:relative; zIndex:0`), capping ALL workspace content (the context bar's 60, the map header's 1000, in-workspace modals) beneath it, and `<header>` is lifted above it (`position:relative; zIndex:1`). The global switcher dropdown now always paints over the workspace regardless of the lower bars' internal z-indexes; the shell-level AuthPanel (`zIndex:5000`) still sits above everything. More robust than just bumping the menu's number (which would depend on the exact stacking tree). Build passes.

### B68 ‚Äî Opening a project with saved elements renders a blank screen (`cfgOf is not defined`) `[Site Planner]` (bug) ‚Äî crash, high
`[x]` Opening a project that has saved layout elements (e.g. **"Schiel Road"**) blanked the whole page; the console showed `ReferenceError: cfgOf is not defined`, thrown inside the `els.map` during render ‚Äî so empty/new projects (iterating over nothing) didn't crash, which is why only populated projects blanked. **Root cause:** `cfgOf` is a component-scoped helper (`SitePlanner.jsx:2449`, it closes over `settings`), but it was *also* called at `SitePlanner.jsx:5237` inside `renderElPx` ‚Äî a **module-level** function that receives `settings` as a parameter ‚Äî where the component-scoped `cfgOf` is not in scope. It shipped because it compiles fine; a build-only CI check can't see an unresolved identifier at runtime. This is exactly the "disjoint-but-interdependent concurrent merge" failure mode called out in **B63**: a parking `cfgOf` call site (added with B29/B59 in PR #22) landed in a scope where the helper isn't visible, and the clean merge + green build hid it. (Arrived from a parallel chat as provisional "NEW-1"; minted **B68** here ‚Äî B67 is reserved by the in-flight PR #23 ‚Äî and deduped: no prior blank-screen item existed.)
> Done 2026-06-15 (branch `claude/loving-knuth-6n43df`, pending PR). Three parts. **(1) Fix:** `renderElPx` now resolves `cfgOf` locally from its `settings` param (identical semantics to the component's), so the parking branch no longer references an out-of-scope symbol. **(2) Build-time guard (the real prevention):** added a minimal ESLint flat config whose headline rule is `no-undef`, run as a CI step before the build (`npm run lint`) ‚Äî verified it flags the exact bug (`5237:38 'cfgOf' is not defined`) on the pre-fix file, so this whole class of dangling reference now fails the build instead of shipping a blank page. **(3) Hardening:** each lazy workspace in `Shell.jsx` is wrapped in a React `ErrorBoundary` (keyed by workspace id), so a future render crash shows a legible "couldn't load this view" fallback (Try again / Reload) instead of unmounting to a blank page ‚Äî the shell, the switcher, and the other workspace keep working. `lint` / `test` (30 pass) / `build` all green.
